Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Obligation of Jumu'ah and Their Legal Effect
Ruling with proof: conditions for obligation and their effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) and conditions for performance (shurut al-ada') of Jumu'ah, and apply the Hanafi ruling that a non-obligated person's Jumu'ah counts as fard.

Core Idea
Conditions for obligation do not affect validity—a non-obligated person's Jumu'ah fulfills the fard.

The passage begins by listing the conditions for Jumu'ah to be obligatory: sanity, puberty, sound eyesight, and ability to walk. It then clarifies a key Hanafi principle: if a person lacking these conditions performs Jumu'ah, it still counts as his obligatory (fard) prayer. This distinction between obligation and validity has practical consequences for who can lead the prayer and how the prayer is counted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions listed for obligation
Read the first line: 'والعقل والبلوغ، وسلامة العين، والرّجل'. These are the conditions for Jumu'ah to be obligatory (wajib 'ayn).
These are not conditions for the prayer to be valid, only for it to be required.
2
Understand the ruling on the blind person
Note the ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says the blind is not obligated even with a guide; the two Sahibayn say it becomes obligatory if a guide is available.
The text also mentions that a blind person who can navigate independently is obligated.
3
Analyze the ruling on the paralyzed person
The paralyzed person is not obligated by consensus because the Qur'anic command 'hasten' implies walking, and walking is impossible for him.
The principle of 'no hardship' (la haraj) is cited.
4
Apply the principle 'taqa'u farḍan'
If a non-obligated person (e.g., a traveler) performs Jumu'ah, it counts as his fard prayer. This follows from the text 'فتقع فرضاً'.
This permits such individuals to lead the prayer and makes their Jumu'ah valid for others.
5
Distinguish conditions for obligation from conditions for performance
The text explicitly states that these conditions are for obligation, not performance. If they were for performance, a person lacking them could not perform Jumu'ah validly.
The condition for performance (being in a city) is treated separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعقل والبلوغ، وسلامة العين، والرّجل . فتقعُ فرضاً إن صلاها فاقدها وإن لم تجب عليه ، وشرط لأدائها : المصر، أو فناؤه [1] قوله : وسلامة العين؛ فلا تجب على الأعمى، وإن قدر على قائد متبرع أو بأجرة عنده لعدم اعتبار القدرة بقدرة الغير على أصله، وعندهما إن قدر عليه تجب. وتجب على الأعور وضعيف البصر والظاهرُ وجوبها على بعض العميان الذي يمشي في الأسواق، ويعرفُ الطرق بلا قائد من غيرِ كُلفة، ويعرف أي مسجد داره بلا سؤال أحد؛ لأنه حينئذ كالمريض القادر على الخروج بنفسه. كذا في رد المحتار). [2] قوله : والرجل؛ بكسر الرَّاء، عطف على العين، فلا تجب على المقعد، وإن وجد حاملاً اتفاقاً، كذا في «الخانية»؛ وذلك لأنَّ السَّعي المأمور به في قوله تعالى : ﴿إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلَوةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكرِ اللهِ﴾ : أي المشي لا يوجد من المقعد وكذا يتعسر على الأعمى، وقد قال الله : ﴿وَمَا جَعَلَ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الدِّينِ مِنْ حَرَجٍ﴾ قوله : فتقع فرضاً؛ يتفرّعُ عليه أنه يجوز إمامة المسافر والعبد والمريض في الجمعة، وتنعقد بحضورهم الجمعة، وإن لم يوجد من سواهم، كما في «الهداية» . قوله : لا لأدائها؛ فإنه لو كانت هذه الشروط شروطاً للاداء لم تصح من فاقدها، كما في الشروط الآتية. [0] قوله : المصر؛ الأصل فيه أنَّ قوله : ﴿فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ﴾ ليس على إطلاقه إجماعاً بين الأمة، إذ لا تجوز إقامتها في البراري إجماعاً، ولا في كل قرية، فكان خصوص المكان مراد إجماعاً. اختلفوا في تفسير المصر": وقدر بالمصر لقول علي الله : «لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا صلاة فطر ولا ضحى إلا في مصر جامع أو مدينة عظيمة، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وصححه ابنُ حَزْم. وعند عبد الرزاق عنه : لا تشريق ولا جمعة إلا في مصر جامع)، وهو موقوف في حكم المرفوع؛ لأن دليل الافتراض من كتاب الله يفيده على العموم، فإقدامه على نفيه في بعض الأماكن لا يكون إلا عن سماع، ويؤيده أنه لم ينقل عن الصحابة، أنهم حين فتحوا البلاد، اشتغلوا بنصب المنابر والجمع إلا في الأمصار دون القرى، ولو كان لنقل ولو آحاد، كذا في فتح القدير [1]قوله : اختلفوا في تفسير المصر... الخ؛ قال في «البناية» : اختلفوا فيه : فعن أبي حنيفة : هو ما يجتمع فيه مرافق أهله. وعن أبي يوسف : كل موضع فيه أمير وقاض ينفذ الأحكام ويقيم الحدود، وهكذا روى الحَسَنُ عن أبي حنيفة . وقال سفيانُ الثَّوري : المصر الجامع ما يعدُّهُ النَّاسُ المصر عند ذكـر الأمـصـار المطلقة؛ كبُخارا وسَمَرْقَند. وعن أبي حنيفة : هو بلدة كبيرة فيها سكك وأسواق، ولها رساتيق. وفي نوادر ابن شجاع له : إذا كان في القرية عشرة آلاف فهو مصر. وعن بعض أصحابنا : المصرُ ما يعيش فيه كل صانع بصناعته.
And [conditions are] intellect, puberty, soundness of eye, and soundness of leg. So if one lacking these performs it, it counts as obligatory (fard), even if it was not obligatory upon him. And a condition for its performance is: the city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). [1] His saying: 'soundness of eye'; it is not obligatory upon the blind, even if he is able to find a volunteer guide or for hire, in his (Abu Hanifa's) view, because ability is not considered through the ability of another, according to his principle. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he is able to find one, it is obligatory. It is obligatory upon the one-eyed and the weak-sighted. And apparently it is obligatory upon some blind persons who walk in the markets and know the roads without a guide without difficulty, and know which mosque is his without asking anyone; because then he is like a sick person able to go out by himself. As in Radd al-Muhtar. [2] His saying: 'the leg' – with kasra on the ra', it is an adjunct to 'the eye'. It is not obligatory upon the paralyzed, even if he finds a carrier, by agreement. As in al-Khaniyyah. That is because the 'sir' (hastening) commanded in His statement: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah' means walking, which does not exist from the paralyzed. Similarly, it is difficult for the blind. And Allah said: 'And He has not placed upon you in religion any hardship.' His saying: 'so it counts as fard' – it follows from this that it is permissible for a traveler, a slave, and a sick person to lead the Jumu'ah prayer, and the Jumu'ah is valid with their presence even if there is no one else besides them, as in al-Hidayah. His saying: 'not for its performance' – for if these conditions were conditions for performance, it would not be valid from one lacking them, as in the coming conditions. [0] His saying: 'the city' – the basis for it is that His statement: 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' is not unrestricted by consensus of the Ummah, since it is not permissible to establish it in deserts by consensus, nor in every village. So particularity of place is intended by consensus. They differed regarding the interpretation of 'the city' (misr). And it is defined by the city because of the saying of ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'There is no Friday prayer, nor Eid al-Adha prayer, nor Eid al-Fitr prayer, nor al-Duha (Eid) prayer except in an encompassing city or a great town' – narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba and authenticated by Ibn Hazm. According to ‘Abd al-Razzaq from him: 'No Eid nor Friday except in an encompassing city.' It is mawquf but in the ruling of marfu‘ because the evidence of obligation from the Book of Allah indicates it generally, so his proceeding to negate it in some places can only be from hearing (from the Prophet). This is supported by the fact that it is not reported from the Companions that when they conquered lands, they occupied themselves with setting up pulpits and performing Jumu'ah except in the capitals (amsar) and not in the villages. If it had happened, it would have been reported even as isolated reports. So in Fath al-Qadir. [1] His saying: 'they differed in interpreting the city...' He said in al-Binayah: They differed concerning it: From Abu Hanifa: it is (a place) where the residents' needs are gathered. From Abu Yusuf: every place in which there is an amir and a judge who executes judgments and establishes hudud punishments. Similarly, al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa. Sufyan al-Thawri said: The comprehensive city is what people regard as a city when the absolute term 'cities' is mentioned, such as Bukhara and Samarkand. From Abu Hanifa: it is a large town having streets and markets and having cultivated lands (rasatiq). In the Nawadir of Ibn Shuja‘ from him: if a village has ten thousand (people), it is a city. From some of our companions: the city is where every craftsman lives by his craft.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for Jumu'ah prayer, distinguishing between conditions for obligation (wujub) and conditions for performance (ada'). It begins by stating that sanity, puberty, sound eyesight, and the ability to walk are conditions for obligation. If a person lacks these, he is not obligated, but if he performs it anyway, it counts as his fard prayer. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The condition for performance is that one must be in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). The commentary then elaborates on the condition of eyesight: according to Abu Hanifa, a blind person is not obligated even if he can find a guide because ability through another is not considered. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it becomes obligatory if a guide is available. A weak-sighted or one-eyed person is obligated. The text also notes that some blind persons who can navigate independently are obligated. For the leg condition, a paralyzed person is not obligated even if a carrier is available, by consensus, because the Quranic command 'hasten' implies walking. The passage then clarifies that these conditions are for obligation, not for performance; otherwise, a person lacking them could not validly lead or attend Jumu'ah. The text then focuses on the condition of 'misr'. It provides evidence from a hadith of Ali and the practice of the Companions. The definition of misr is disputed among Hanafi scholars: Abu Hanifa gave multiple definitions (gathering of needs, large town with streets and markets), Abu Yusuf defined it by the presence of a ruler and judge, and other opinions mention population size or industrial self-sufficiency. The relied-upon position is that Jumu'ah is valid in any place considered a city by custom ('urf), as long as it meets the conditions of a settled settlement with facilities.

Key Terms
المصر (al-miṣr): A city or large town where Jumu'ah is valid; defined by various criteria such as gathering of needs, presence of ruler and judge, or custom
فناؤه (fanā'uhu): The outskirts or suburbs of a city, considered part of the city for Jumu'ah
فتقع فرضاً (fataqa'u farḍan): The prayer counts as the obligatory (fard) prayer even if the person was not originally obligated

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a paralyzed person is carried to Jumu'ah and prays, what is the ruling?
A) It is not valid because he cannot walk.
B) It is valid and counts as his fard prayer.
C) It is valid only if he pays compensation (dam).
D) It is invalid; he must pray Zuhr later.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the conditions for obligation of Jumu'ah (sanity, puberty, sight, mobility) do not affect validity; a non-obligated person who performs Jumu'ah fulfills his fard prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Definition of the City (Misr) as a Condition for Jumu'ah
Ruling with proof: condition of misr and its intra-madhhab definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of a city (misr) for Jumu'ah, identify the evidence from hadith and practice, and apply the relied-upon criterion of custom ('urf) to determine if a locality qualifies.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires a city or its outskirts; the city is defined by custom, not a fixed population or ruler.

The passage delves into the condition of 'misr' (city) for the performance of Jumu'ah. It establishes that the Qur'anic command to hasten is not unrestricted; consensus requires a specific place. The hadith of 'Ali and the practice of the Companions restrict Jumu'ah to cities. However, Hanafi scholars differed on the precise definition of a city, offering multiple criteria. The lesson explores these definitions and explains why the Hanafi school ultimately relies on custom.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the evidence for the condition of a city
The passage cites the hadith of 'Ali (mawquf but in the ruling of marfu') and the practice of the Companions who only held Jumu'ah in amsar (capitals), not villages.
The hadith: 'There is no Jumu'ah, nor Eid prayers, except in a comprehensive city or great town.'
2
List the intra-Hanafi definitions of misr
The text reports multiple opinions: Abu Hanifa gave two definitions (gathering of needs, large town with streets and markets); Abu Yusuf defined it as a place with a ruler and judge; others mentioned population thresholds or self-sufficiency.
The definitions are not mutually exclusive; they reflect different perspectives.
3
Understand the role of custom ('urf)
Later Hanafi scholars, like those in Fath al-Qadir and Radd al-Muhtar, considered custom as the decisive factor: if a place is customarily considered a city, Jumu'ah is valid.
This reconciles the conflicting definitions.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects whether Jumu'ah is valid in a particular town or village. Under Abu Yusuf's definition, a village with a judge but no ruler would not qualify; under Abu Hanifa's, it might if it has markets and cultivated lands.
The mufta bihi (custom) provides flexibility.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Determine if a suburban area or a large village near a major city qualifies as part of the city's fina' (outskirts) or as a separate misr.
The condition of fina' allows Jumu'ah in suburbs connected to the city.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[0] قوله : المصر؛ الأصل فيه أنَّ قوله : ﴿فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ﴾ ليس على إطلاقه إجماعاً بين الأمة، إذ لا تجوز إقامتها في البراري إجماعاً، ولا في كل قرية، فكان خصوص المكان مراد إجماعاً. اختلفوا في تفسير المصر": وقدر بالمصر لقول علي الله : «لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا صلاة فطر ولا ضحى إلا في مصر جامع أو مدينة عظيمة، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وصححه ابنُ حَزْم. وعند عبد الرزاق عنه : لا تشريق ولا جمعة إلا في مصر جامع)، وهو موقوف في حكم المرفوع؛ لأن دليل الافتراض من كتاب الله يفيده على العموم، فإقدامه على نفيه في بعض الأماكن لا يكون إلا عن سماع، ويؤيده أنه لم ينقل عن الصحابة، أنهم حين فتحوا البلاد، اشتغلوا بنصب المنابر والجمع إلا في الأمصار دون القرى، ولو كان لنقل ولو آحاد، كذا في فتح القدير [1]قوله : اختلفوا في تفسير المصر... الخ؛ قال في «البناية» : اختلفوا فيه : فعن أبي حنيفة : هو ما يجتمع فيه مرافق أهله. وعن أبي يوسف : كل موضع فيه أمير وقاض ينفذ الأحكام ويقيم الحدود، وهكذا روى الحَسَنُ عن أبي حنيفة . وقال سفيانُ الثَّوري : المصر الجامع ما يعدُّهُ النَّاسُ المصر عند ذكـر الأمـصـار المطلقة؛ كبُخارا وسَمَرْقَند. وعن أبي حنيفة : هو بلدة كبيرة فيها سكك وأسواق، ولها رساتيق. وفي نوادر ابن شجاع له : إذا كان في القرية عشرة آلاف فهو مصر. وعن بعض أصحابنا : المصرُ ما يعيش فيه كل صانع بصناعته.

And a condition for its performance is: the city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for Jumu'ah prayer, distinguishing between conditions for obligation (wujub) and conditions for performance (ada'). It begins by stating that sanity, puberty, sound eyesight, and the ability to walk are conditions for obligation. If a person lacks these, he is not obligated, but if he performs it anyway, it counts as his fard prayer. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The condition for performance is that one must be in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). The commentary then elaborates on the condition of eyesight: according to Abu Hanifa, a blind person is not obligated even if he can find a guide because ability through another is not considered. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it becomes obligatory if a guide is available. A weak-sighted or one-eyed person is obligated. The text also notes that some blind persons who can navigate independently are obligated. For the leg condition, a paralyzed person is not obligated even if a carrier is available, by consensus, because the Quranic command 'hasten' implies walking. The passage then clarifies that these conditions are for obligation, not for performance; otherwise, a person lacking them could not validly lead or attend Jumu'ah. The text then focuses on the condition of 'misr'. It provides evidence from a hadith of Ali and the practice of the Companions. The definition of misr is disputed among Hanafi scholars: Abu Hanifa gave multiple definitions (gathering of needs, large town with streets and markets), Abu Yusuf defined it by the presence of a ruler and judge, and other opinions mention population size or industrial self-sufficiency. The relied-upon position is that Jumu'ah is valid in any place considered a city by custom ('urf), as long as it meets the conditions of a settled settlement with facilities.

Key Terms
مصر جامع (miṣr jāmi'): A comprehensive city that encompasses all needs and is a central place for the region
مدينة عظيمة (madīnatun 'aẓīmah): A great town, considered equivalent to a misr for Jumu'ah
الرساتيق (al-rasātīq): Cultivated lands or rural districts attached to a city
الأمصار (al-amṣār): Plural of misr; the capital cities conquered by the Companions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the most relied-upon criterion for defining a city (misr) in the Hanafi school?
A) Presence of an amir and a judge
B) Population of at least 10,000
C) Customary recognition as a city
D) Availability of markets and cultivated lands

Key Takeaway
The condition for Jumu'ah to be performed in a city is defined by custom; any locality customarily considered a city suffices, making the rule adaptable.

Definition of a City (Misr) for Jumu'ah
Defines 'مصر' for Jumu'ah validity and presents Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of 'misr' for Jumu'ah validity and identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) definition, explaining why it is preferred.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a city; Hanafi scholars differ on its precise definition, but the relied-upon view is that the largest mosque cannot hold the residents.

The validity of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) depends on a condition: it must be held in a 'city' (misr). But what exactly constitutes a city for this purpose? This lesson examines the Hanafi ikhtilaf (disagreement) on the definition of misr, ranging from an amir and judge to the capacity of the largest mosque, and identifies the mufta bihi (operative) position used in fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual evidence
Locate the primary dalil for the condition of misr: the hadith of Ali (رضي الله عنه). Understand its status as a mawquf hadith with the ruling of marfu' because it concerns an obligation not deducible by opinion.
The hadith is reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah and authenticated by Ibn Hazm.
2
List the various Hanafi definitions
From the passage, enumerate the different opinions from Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, Sufyan al-Thawri, Ibn Shuja', and others. Note the key elements of each definition.
Definitions range from amenities to amir/judge, to population count, to craftsmen living conditions.
3
Analyze the tarjih (preference) process
See how the author (al-Wiqayah) and later commentators (e.g., al-Karkhi, al-Thalji) weigh the definitions. Understand why al-Thalji's mosque-capacity definition becomes the mufta bihi, despite al-Karkhi's being the zahir al-madhhab.
The commentary states that al-Thalji's definition is the fatwa of most fuqaha.
4
Understand the practical application
Apply the mufta bihi definition to a real scenario: if the largest mosque can hold all residents obligated for Jumu'ah, it is not a misr; if it cannot, it is a misr and Jumu'ah is valid.
The definition focuses on capacity relative to those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory.

Book of Prayer: Friday Prayer

They differed in the interpretation of 'the city (misr)':
And it is defined as 'city' based on the statement of Ali (Allah be pleased with him): 'There is no Friday prayer, no takbir al-tashriq, no Eid prayer, nor al-Duha prayer except in a large city (misr jami') or a great town.' Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, authenticated by Ibn Hazm. And according to Abd al-Razzaq from him: 'No tashriq and no Friday prayer except in a large city (misr jami').' It is a mawquf (stopped) hadith in the ruling of marfu' (raised) because the evidence of obligation from the Book of Allah establishes it generally, so his undertaking to negate it in some places could only be from hearing (from the Prophet). It is supported by the fact that it is not transmitted from the Companions that when they conquered the lands, they busied themselves with setting up pulpits and gathering for Friday except in the large cities (amsar) and not in the villages. Had it been otherwise, it would have been transmitted even as ahad (solitary report). Thus in Fath al-Qadir. [1] His saying: 'They differed in the interpretation of the city (misr)...' etc.; He said in al-Binayah: They differed concerning it:
(3) From Abu Hanifah (Allah have mercy on him): It is that wherein the amenities of its inhabitants are gathered.
(4) From Abu Yusuf (Allah have mercy on him): Every place where there is an amir (prince) and a judge who executes the legal rulings and establishes the hadd punishments.
And thus al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifah.
And Sufyan al-Thawri said: The major city (misr al-jami') is that which people consider a city when cities are mentioned absolutely; like Bukhara and Samarqand.
And from Abu Hanifah (Allah have mercy on him): It is a large town having streets and markets, and having outer districts (rusatiq). And in the Nawadir of Ibn Shuja' from him: When there are ten thousand in a village, it is a city (misr). And from some of our companions: The city (misr) is that wherein every craftsman can live by his craft.
(1) In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (1:439), etc. (2) In Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq (3:167), and 'al-Athar' of Abu Yusuf (303), and 'Mushkil al-Athar' (3:150), and Musnad Ibn al-Ja'd (1:437), and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (3:179). Ibn Hajar said in al-Dirayah (p.213): 'Its chain is authentic.'
(3) Fath al-Qadir (2:51).
(4) al-Binayah (2:790).

'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah
[1] (1) According to some: It is a place having an amir and a judge who executes the legal rulings and establishes the hadd punishments. And according to some: It is a place where, if its inhabitants gather in its largest mosque, it does not contain them. So the author chose this saying, thus he said:
[4] [1] His saying: 'According to some...' etc.; This is the choice of al-Karkhi, and it is the apparent position of the madhhab, and it was chosen in al-Hidayah (2), and authenticated by the commentator of al-Munyah (3) and others.
(2) (2) His saying: 'amir' – what is meant by it is one who protects the people, prevents the corrupters, and strengthens the rulings of the Shari'ah. In sum, he is able to give justice to the oppressed from the oppressor, as explained in al-'Inayah. (3) His saying: 'executes the rulings' – Isma'il al-Nabulsi said in Sharh al-Durar: It does not mean the execution of all rulings in actuality; for Friday prayer was established during the era of the most tyrannical people, al-Hajjaj, and he did not execute all rulings. Rather, the intention is his capability to do so.
[4] His saying: 'and establishes the hadd punishments' – caution is taken regarding the arbitrator (al-muhakkam) and the woman if she is a judge, for they do not establish the hadd punishments even if they execute rulings. He sufficed with mentioning the hadd punishments over qisas (retribution) because whoever has the power to establish them has the power to establish qisas. And what is meant by 'hadd punishments' are the penalties measured by the Shari'ah for crimes; like the hadd for Zina, drinking wine, and the like. Thus in al-Bahr and others. [0] His saying: 'It is a place...' etc.; This interpretation is transmitted from al-Thalji, and upon it is the fatwa of most jurists, as in al-Mujtaba, and in al-Walwaljiyyah: It is the correct view.
[6] His saying: 'If its inhabitants gather' – what is meant by 'inhabitants' are those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory. And regarding 'its largest mosque' – it is said that it is the Jami' mosque (mosque for Friday), and it is said: the largest mosque for the five daily prayers, as in Fatawa al-Zahidi. Thus al-Birjandi mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah.
(1) Among them: al-Thalji, and upon it is the fatwa of most jurists. See: al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:537), al-Fatawa al-Mahdiyya (1:6).
(2) al-Hidayah (1:82). (3) Munyat al-Musalli (p.550).
(4) And chosen by the author of al-Multaqa (p.24), and al-Kanz (p.21), and others.
(5) al-'Inayah (2:52).
(6) al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (2:151).
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling (hukm ta'rifi) addressing the meaning of 'المصر' (the city or large town) as a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. The author begins by citing the hadith of 'Ali (رضي الله عنه) that Jumu'ah is only valid in a 'مصر جامع' (comprehensive city) or 'مدينة عظيمة' (great town). This hadith is the primary textual evidence (dalil) for the condition. The commentary explains that even though it is mawquf (a statement of a Companion), it has the ruling of marfu' because it concerns an obligation that is not deductible by personal opinion.

The passage then presents the ikhtilaf (disagreement) among Hanafi scholars regarding the precise definition of 'مصر'. Several opinions are listed:
1. Abu Hanifah's first opinion: a place where the amenities (مرافق) of its people are gathered.
2. Abu Yusuf's opinion (also narrated from Abu Hanifah by al-Hasan): a place with an amir (ruler) and a qadi (judge) who execute legal rulings (ينفذ الأحكام) and establish hadd punishments (يقيم الحدود).
3. Sufyan al-Thawri: what people customarily consider a city when cities are mentioned, like Bukhara and Samarqand.
4. Another opinion from Abu Hanifah: a large town with streets, markets, and outer districts (رساتيق).
5. From the Nawadir of Ibn Shuja': a village with ten thousand inhabitants is a city.
6. Some Hanafis: a place where every craftsman can make a living by his craft.

The author then mentions that some scholars define it as a place with an amir and judge, while others define it as a place where the largest mosque cannot accommodate the inhabitants. The author (of al-Wiqayah) chooses the latter definition. The super-commentary (from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah) clarifies that the definition of an amir and judge is the choice of al-Karkhi and the apparent position of the madhhab, as chosen in al-Hidayah. It further elaborates on the terms: 'amir' means one who protects and enforces justice; 'executes rulings' does not require actual execution of all rulings but capability; 'establishes hadd punishments' excludes arbitrators and female judges who cannot carry out hadd; 'hadd punishments' are the prescribed penalties for crimes like zina and drinking.

The commentary concludes that the definition based on mosque capacity (that the largest mosque cannot contain the residents) is from al-Thalji and is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to most fuqaha. The term 'أهل' (inhabitants) refers to those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, and 'أكبر مساجده' (largest mosque) is interpreted as either the Jami' mosque or the largest mosque for the five daily prayers.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A large city or urban settlement that meets specific conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah. The precise definition is disputed: it can be a place with an amir and judge, or a place where the largest mosque cannot hold the residents, among others.
الجامع (al-jami'): A large mosque where Friday prayer is held. In the context of defining 'مصر', it can refer to the largest mosque of the town, which is either the Jami' mosque or the biggest mosque for daily prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what condition defines a 'misr' (city) for the validity of Jumu'ah?
A) It must have an amir and a judge who execute rulings and establish hadd punishments.
B) Its largest mosque cannot accommodate all its inhabitants who are obliged to attend Jumu'ah.
C) It must have at least ten thousand inhabitants.
D) Every craftsman must be able to live by his craft.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid in a city; the Hanafi mufta bihi definition is that the largest mosque cannot hold all residents.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Hanafi Definition of 'Misr' for Jumu'ah
Commentary on conflicting definitions of 'مصر' for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi definitions of 'مصر' for Jumu'ah and explain why the mosque capacity definition is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A town for Jumu'ah is where people cannot fit in its largest mosque — not where rulers enforce laws.

What legally defines a 'town' for Friday prayer? The Hanafi school offers two definitions: one based on political authority, another on population density relative to mosque size. This lesson unpacks the dispute, its practical consequences, and why later jurists preferred the second definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Note the first definition (al-Karkhi): a place with an amir and judge who implement rulings and enforce hudud. The second (al-Thalji): a place whose people cannot be accommodated in its largest mosque.
Both are Hanafi views; the first is 'ẓāhir al-madhhab'.
2
Understand the objection to the first definition
If strictly applied, many towns where Jumu'ah is unquestionably obligatory would be excluded because rulers do not actually enforce all laws. The commentator clarifies that 'capability' suffices, not actual enforcement.
The example of al-Ḥajjāj shows that even oppressive rulers can have capability.
3
Analyze the tarjīḥ (preference)
The author of al-Wiqāyah chose the second definition. Reason: laziness in enforcing ḥudūd is widespread, so relying on the first definition would invalidate Jumu'ah in many lands.
This is a pragmatic tarjīḥ based on iḥtiyāṭ (preserving Jumu'ah obligation).
4
Define 'fanā' al-miṣr'
The annexed open area prepared for the town's needs (military, burial, prayer) is considered part of the town. Fixed distance estimations are rejected in favor of a general description.
This expands the scope of where Jumu'ah can be validly performed.

كتاب الصلاة صلاة الجمعة
وما لا يسع أكبر مساجدِهِ أهلَهُ مصر وما اتصل به معداً لمصالحه فناؤُه (وما لا يسع أكبر مساجده أهلَهُ مصر). وإنما اختار هذا دون التفسير الأَوَّل ؛ لظهور الثواني في أحكام الشرع لاسيما إقامة الحدود في الأمصار. وجمع (وما اتصل به مُعداً لمصالحه فناؤُه ) ، مصالح المصر": كركض الخيل ، العساكر، والخروج للرمي، ودفن الموتى، وصلاة الجنازة، ونحو ذلك. 
[ ١ ] قوله : وإنما اختار ... الخ ؛ دفع لما يُقال أن المصنف ترك تفسير الأول مع كونه ظاهر الرواية، ومختار صاحب «الهداية»، وحاصله : أنه إنما اختارَ التَّفسِيرَ الثَّاني دونَ الأول لظهور الكسل في إقامة الحدود وغيرها من الأحكام الشرعية في كثير من الأمصار التي لا يشك أحد في وجوب الجمعة بها. فلو أخذ بذلك التفسير لزم عدم صحة الجمعة في كثير من بلاد الإسلام ؛ لعدم صدق تعريف المصر عليه ، فلذلك اختارَ التَّفسير الثَّاني، وقد يجاب بأنَّ المراد بالتنفيذ والإقامة في ذلك التعريف القدرة على ذلك ، وإن لم يوجد ذلك لاتباع هوى النفس أو غير ذلك ، فلا يلزم خروج أكثر الأمثال من هذا التعريف. 
[٢] قوله : فناؤه ؛ فناء الدار بالكسر : سعة أمامها ولذلك فناء البيت، وفناء المصر، قدَّرَهُ بعضُهم بمساحة، فقدر بغلوة، وبميل، وبميلين، وبثلاثة فراسخ ، وبفرسخين، وبغلوة، وبسماع الصوت وبسماع الأذان، والتعريف أحسن من التحديد ؛ لأنه لا يوجد ذلك في كلِّ مصر، كذا في «تحفة أعيان الغنى بصحة الجمعة والعيدين في الفناء» للشرنبلالي. 
(۳) قوله : مصالح المصر : كركض الخيل ؛ هو بالفتح: اسم جمع للفرس، والركض بالفتح : دوانيدن كما يكون في المسابقة وغيرها. وجمع العساكر ؛ بالفتح جمعُ عسكر: أي جمعها للغزو والاهتمام بها. والخروج للرمي ؛ تيراندازي يعني الخروج من المصر؛ لرمي السهام. ودفن الموتى ؛ كما يكون في أكثر البلادِ أنَّ المقابر تكون خارج البلد. وصلاة الجنازة ؛ كما عُرِفَ في بعض البلاد أنه يُعَدُّ لها خارج المصر موضع. ونحو ذلك ؛ كرمي البنادق، والاصطياد واختبار المصارعين وغير ذلك.
According to some: it is a place that has an amir and a judge who implement legal rulings and enforce the hudud. According to others: it is a place whose people, when they gather in its largest mosque, it cannot accommodate them. The author chose this latter saying. [1] His saying: 'According to some...' etc.; this is the choice of al-Karkhi, and it is the apparent [position] of the madhhab, and it was chosen in al-Hidayah, and verified by the commentator of al-Munyah and others. (2) His saying: 'Amir'; what is meant is one who protects the people, prevents corrupters, and strengthens the rulings of the Shari'ah. Its gist is that he is able to give justice to the oppressed from the oppressor, as explained in al-Inayah. (3) His saying: 'Implements the rulings'; Isma'il al-Nabulusi said in Sharh al-Durar: 'What is meant is not the actual implementation of all rulings; for Jumu'ah was established in the era of the most oppressive of people, al-Hajjaj, and he was not implementing all rulings. Rather, what is meant is his capability to do so.' [4] His saying: 'Enforces the hudud'; He is careful to exclude the arbitrator and the woman if she is a judge, for they do not enforce the hudud even if they implement rulings. He sufficed with mentioning the hudud over qisas because whoever has the power to enforce them has the power to enforce [qisas]. By hudud is meant the fixed punishments prescribed by the Shari'ah for crimes, such as the hadd for zina and drinking wine and the like. This is in al-Bahr and others. [0] His saying: 'It is a place...' etc.; This interpretation is transmitted from al-Thalji, and according to it is the fatwa of most jurists, as in al-Mujtaba, and in al-Walwaljiyyah it is said to be the correct one. [6] His saying: 'When its people gather'; by 'people' are meant those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, and by 'largest mosque' it is said that it is the congregational mosque, and [also] said that it is the largest mosque for the five daily prayers, as in the Fatawa of al-Zahidi, and likewise al-Birjandi mentioned in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah. (1) Among them: al-Thalji, and according to him is the fatwa of most jurists. Cf. al-Mujtaba, and in al-Walwaljiyyah it is said to be correct. Cf. al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:537), al-Fatawa al-Mahdiyyah (1:6). (2) al-Hidayah (1:82). (3) Munyat al-Musalli (p. 550). (4) And it was chosen by the author of al-Multaqa (p. 24) and al-Kanz (p. 21) and others. (5) al-Inayah (2:52). (6) al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (2:151).

Book of Prayer: Jumu'ah Prayer
And [the definition is:] a town whose largest mosque cannot accommodate its people, and what is attached to it prepared for its purposes is its open area (fana'). And [the author] chose this over the first interpretation due to the apparent laziness in [implementing] the rulings of the Shari'ah, especially the enforcement of hudud in towns. And [the definition includes] what is attached to it prepared for its purposes as its open area (fana'), [such as] the purposes of the town: like galloping horses, gathering armies, going out for archery, burying the dead, performing funeral prayer, and the like. [1] His saying: 'And he chose...' etc.; This refutes what might be said that the author abandoned the first interpretation despite it being the apparent [position] of the narration and the choice of the author of al-Hidayah. Its gist is that he chose the second interpretation over the first due to the apparent weakness in enforcing hudud and other Shari'ah rulings in many towns regarding which no one doubts the obligation of Jumu'ah. If he had taken that interpretation, it would entail the invalidity of Jumu'ah in many lands of Islam because the definition of a town would not apply to them. Therefore he chose the second interpretation. It may also be answered that what is meant by 'implementation' and 'enforcement' in that definition is the ability to do so, even if it is not actually found due to following desires or other reasons, so it does not necessitate the exclusion of most such places from this definition. [2] His saying: 'Its open area (fana')'; fana' of a house (with kasrah) means the open space in front of it, similarly the fana' of a house, and the fana' of a town. Some have estimated it by area, estimating it by a bowshot, a mile, two miles, three farsakhs, two farsakhs, a bowshot, the range of sound, and the range of the call to prayer. Definition is better than specifying a fixed measure because that is not found in every town. This is in Tuhfat A'yan al-Ghina bi Sahh al-Jumu'ah wa al-'Idayn fi al-Fana' by al-Shurunbulali. (3) His saying: 'Purposes of the town: like galloping horses'; 'horses' (al-khayl) is a plural noun for a horse (collective), 'galloping' (al-rakd) means running as in racing and other things. 'Gathering armies' (jami' al-'asakir): 'asakir' is plural of 'askar, i.e., gathering them for war and taking care of them. 'Going out for archery': shooting arrows, meaning leaving the town to shoot arrows. 'Burying the dead': as is the case in most towns that the graveyards are outside the city. 'Funeral prayer': as is known in some towns that a place is prepared for it outside the town. 'And the like': such as shooting guns, hunting, and testing wrestlers, and other things.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of 'مصر' (town/city) as a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah (Friday prayer) in the Hanafi school. The author, al-Marghinani, presents two definitions: the first, attributed to al-Karkhi, defines a town as a place with an amir and a judge who implement rulings and enforce hudud (fixed punishments). The second, attributed to al-Thalji, defines a town as a place where the people cannot fit into its largest mosque. The author of 'Umda al-Ri'aya explains that the compiler of al-Wiqayah chose the second definition, and this choice is supported by most later jurists. The reasoning is pragmatic: if the first definition were strictly applied, many places where Jumu'ah is undoubtedly obligatory would be excluded because their rulers do not actually enforce all Shari'ah rulings. The commentary clarifies that 'implementation' in the first definition means capability, not actual enforcement. It then discusses the 'fana'' (outskirts) of a town, which is attached area prepared for the town's purposes such as horse racing, military training, archery, burial, funeral prayer, etc. The commentator notes that defining the fana' by a fixed distance is less preferable than a general definition, as traditions for measurements vary. This passage shows the Hanafi tendency to adopt a practical definition that preserves the obligation of Jumu'ah in existing Muslim lands.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A town or city that is a valid location for Jumu'ah prayer; defined in this passage as a place whose largest mosque cannot accommodate its people.
فناء المصر (fana' al-misr): The open area attached to a town that is prepared for the town's purposes, such as horse racing, military training, burial grounds, etc. It is considered part of the town for Jumu'ah.
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes like zina and drinking wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon definition in this passage, what constitutes a 'مصر' (town) for the validity of Jumu'ah?
A) A place with an amir and a judge who implement all rulings and enforce hudud.
B) A place whose people, when gathered in its largest mosque, cannot be accommodated.
C) A place with a population of at least 10,000.
D) A place that has a market and a school.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi definition of a town for Jumu'ah is based on the inability of the largest mosque to accommodate all residents, not on the presence of enforcing authorities.

Definition of a City (Misr) for Friday Prayer
Definition of misr and fana' for Jumu'ah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a misr according to Hanafi fiqh and explain the criteria for including the fana' as part of the city for Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
A city for Jumu'ah is defined not by population or hudud enforcement, but by the capacity of its largest mosque.

This lesson examines the Hanafi definition of a city (misr) for the obligation of Friday prayer. The text from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses the criteria set by the author of al-Wiqaya and explains why a particular definition was chosen over an alternative. Understanding this definition is crucial for determining when Jumu'ah becomes fard upon a community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being defined? The misr for Jumu'ah. The ruling: Jumu'ah is fard on residents of a misr.
The definition is a condition for the obligation.
2
Understand the two definitions
The first definition (based on hudud enforcement) and the second definition (based on mosque capacity). Why was the second chosen?
The author chose the second to avoid invalidating Jumu'ah in many cities.
3
Analyze the concept of fana'
What is the fana'? How is it determined? The text says it is better defined by description than fixed measurement.
The fana' includes areas connected to the city prepared for its needs.
4
Apply the definition
Identify examples of masalih al-misr that justify including the fana'.
Examples: horse racing, archery, burial grounds.
5
Note the practical consequence
The definition ensures Jumu'ah obligation in cities where hudud may not be strictly enforced.
The commentator emphasizes this rationale.

[ ١ ] قوله : وإنما اختار ... الخ ؛ دفع لما يُقال أن المصنف ترك تفسير الأول مع كونه ظاهر الرواية، ومختار صاحب «الهداية»، وحاصله : أنه إنما اختارَ التَّفسِيرَ الثَّاني دونَ الأول لظهور الكسل في إقامة الحدود وغيرها من الأحكام الشرعية في كثير من الأمصار التي لا يشك أحد في وجوب الجمعة بها. فلو أخذ بذلك التفسير لزم عدم صحة الجمعة في كثير من بلاد الإسلام ؛ لعدم صدق تعريف المصر عليه ، فلذلك اختارَ التَّفسِير الثَّاني، وقد يجاب بأنَّ المراد بالتنفيذ والإقامة في ذلك التعريف القدرة على ذلك ، وإن لم يوجد ذلك لاتباع هوى النفس أو غير ذلك ، فلا يلزم خروج أكثر الأمثال من هذا التعريف. [٢] قوله : فناؤه ؛ فناء الدار بالكسر : سعة أمامها ولذلك فناء البيت، وفناء المصر، قدَّرَهُ بعضُهم بمساحة، فقدر بغلوة، وبميل، وبميلين، وبثلاثة فراسخ ، وبفرسخين، وبغلوة، وبسماع الصوت وبسماع الأذان، والتعريف أحسن من التحديد ؛ لأنه لا يوجد ذلك في كلِّ مصر، كذا في «تحفة أعيان الغنى بصحة الجمعة والعيدين في الفناء» للشرنبلالي. (۳) قوله : مصالح المصر : كركض الخيل ؛ هو بالفتح: اسم جمع للفرس، والركض بالفتح : دوانيدن كما يكون في المسابقة وغيرها. وجمع العساكر ؛ بالفتح جمعُ عسكر: أي جمعها للغزو والاهتمام بها. والخروج للرمي ؛ تيراندازي يعني الخروج من المصر؛ لرمي السهام. ودفن الموتى ؛ كما يكون في أكثر البلادِ أنَّ المقابر تكون خارج البلد. وصلاة الجنازة ؛ كما عُرِفَ في بعض البلاد أنه يُعَدُّ لها خارج المصر موضع. ونحو ذلك ؛ كرمي البنادق، والاصطياد واختبار المصارعين وغير ذلك.
And what its largest mosques do not accommodate its people is a city, and what is connected to it prepared for its needs is its outskirt. (And what its largest mosques do not accommodate its people is a city). And he only chose this over the first interpretation due to the appearance of sluggishness in the rulings of the Shari'ah, especially the execution of hudud in the cities. And he combined (and what is connected to it prepared for its needs is its outskirt) the interests of the city: like the galloping of horses, armies, going out for archery, burying the dead, funeral prayer, and the like. [1] His saying: 'And he only chose...' etc.; a repudiation of what is said that the author left the first interpretation despite it being the apparent riwayah and the choice of the author of al-Hidayah. Its summary: he only chose the second interpretation over the first due to the apparent laziness in establishing hudud and other legal rulings in many cities which no one doubts the obligation of Jumu'ah in them. If he had taken that interpretation, it would necessitate the invalidity of Jumu'ah in many lands of Islam due to the definition of a city not applying to them; therefore he chose the second interpretation. It may be answered that what is meant by execution and establishment in that definition is the ability to do so, even if it does not occur due to following whims or other reasons, so most cities would not exit this definition. [2] His saying: 'its outskirt'; the outskirt of the house (finaa' al-dar) with kasra: the space in front of it, similarly the outskirt of the house, and the outskirt of the city. Some estimated it by area: estimated by a bowshot, a mile, two miles, three farsakhs, two farsakhs, a bowshot, the range of hearing sound, and the range of hearing the adhan. The definition is better than specification because that (specification) is not found in every city. Thus in 'Tuhfat A'yan al-Ghani bi Sihhat al-Jumu'ah wa al-'Idayn fi al-Finaa'' by al-Shurunbulali. (3) His saying: 'interests of the city': like the galloping of horses; it is with fatha: a collective noun for horses, and 'al-rakd' with fatha: running (dawidan) as occurs in racing and other things. And gathering of armies; with fatha, plural of 'askar': i.e., gathering them for war and concern for them. And going out for archery; tirandazi, meaning exiting the city for shooting arrows. And burying the dead; as occurs in most lands that the graveyards are outside the town. And funeral prayer; as is known in some lands that a place is prepared for it outside the city. And the like; like shooting guns, hunting, and testing wrestlers, and other things.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a definition-ruling: it defines what constitutes a city (misr) for the obligation of Friday prayer. The matn states: 'A place whose largest mosques cannot accommodate its people is a city, and what is connected to it prepared for its needs is its outskirt.' The commentator then explains why the author of al-Wiqaya chose this second definition over the first (which defined a city as a place where hudud are enforced). The reason is that many cities clearly obligated for Jumu'ah have slackness in enforcing hudud; adopting the first definition would invalidate Jumu'ah in many Muslim lands. The commentator also discusses the definition of 'fana' (outskirt)' and the various estimates of its extent, concluding that a descriptive definition is better than a fixed measurement. Finally, he lists examples of the 'interests of the city' (masalih al-misr) that justify including the outskirt within the city for Jumu'ah purposes, such as horse racing, military training, archery, burial grounds, funeral prayer spaces, and similar activities.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or town large enough that its largest mosque cannot accommodate all its residents; it is the subject of the obligation of Jumu'ah.
فناء (fana'): The outskirt or surrounding area of a city, prepared for its needs (masalih), included within the city's jurisdiction for Jumu'ah.
مصالح المصر (masalih al-misr): The communal interests and needs of the city, such as military training, burial, and prayer spaces, that justify including the outskirt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this passage, what is the primary criterion for a place to be considered a 'misr' for the obligation of Jumu'ah?
A) That it has a ruler who enforces hudud penalties.
B) That its largest mosque cannot accommodate all its residents.
C) That it has a minimum population of 40 males.
D) That it is within a certain distance from a central mosque.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Jumu'ah depends on a simple criterion: whether the largest mosque can accommodate the city's residents.

Validity of Jumu'ah in Mina During Hajj
Ruling statement with explanatory commentary on Jumu'ah in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which Jumu'ah is valid in Mina during the Hajj season and explain why it is not valid for the Amir of the season or at Arafat.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah in Mina is valid only when authorized by the supreme ruler or the ruler of Hijaz, and only during Hajj when Mina temporarily qualifies as a city.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah clarifies a specific rule about Friday prayer in Mina during Hajj. The ruling hinges on two key factors: the authority of the one leading the prayer and the nature of the location. Understanding this helps you apply the Hanafi condition that Jumu'ah requires a city (misr) and proper authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states that Jumu'ah is 'jaza' (permissible/valid) in Mina during the season, but only for the Khalifa or the Amir of Hijaz. It is not valid for the Amir of the season or at Arafat.
The ruling is about validity (sihha), not obligation.
2
Distinguish the Authorized Authorities
The Khalifa (supreme ruler) and the Amir of Hijaz (regional ruler of Mecca and surrounding areas) have general authority to establish Jumu'ah. The Amir of the season (appointed only for Hajj affairs) does not.
3
Understand the Location Condition
Mina during Hajj season has temporary buildings, streets, and markets, making it a 'misr' (city) at that time, so Jumu'ah is valid. Arafat has no buildings and never qualifies as a misr, so Jumu'ah is never valid there.
4
Apply the Ruling to Analogous Cases
Consider a temporary camp during a large gathering: Jumu'ah would only be valid if the location gains the characteristics of a city and the prayer is led by a properly authorized ruler.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجازت بمنى في الموسم للخليفة ، أو لأمير الحجاز، لا لأمير الموسم ، ولا بعرفات. [ ۱ ] قوله : بمنى ؛ بكسر الميم، وفتح النون في الآخر ألف مقصورة : هو . معروف قرب مكة المشرفة، يقيم فيه الحجَّاجُ يوم التروية، وتؤدى فيه مناسك الحج كالحلق ورمي الجمار والنحر في عاشر ذي الحجة، وثلاثة أيام بعده. وفيه أبنية تعمرُ في أيام الحج، فيكون مصراً في ذلك الوقت فلذا جازت الجمعة فيه في ذلك الوقت دون سائر الأوقات ؛ فإنه يكون فيه في الموسم سلطان وأمير وسكك وأسواق، ولا كذلك عرفات، فإنّها وادٍ ليس فيه بناء، ولا ما يكون به الموضع مصراً، فلا تجوز فيه الجمعة مطلقاً. [٢]قوله : في الموسم ؛ أي موسم الحجاج : بكسر السِّين، وهو سوقهم ومجتمعهم من الوسم، وهو العلامة. كذا في «المغرب» ) ، والمراد بالموسم الزَّمانُ الذي يحل فيه الحجاج بمنى. (۳) قوله : للخليفة ؛ أي السلطان الأعظم إن كان حاضراً. [٤] قوله : أو لأمير الحجاز ، بكسر الحاء المهملة : هو أرض مكة والمدينة وما حولهما من أرض العرب، وأمير الحجاز هو سلطان مكة، أي شريف مكة الحاكم بمكة والمدينة والطائف وما يلي ذلك من أرض الحجاز. (۲) [0] قوله : لا لأمير الموسم ؛ أي لا تجوز إقامة الجمعة بمنى لأمير الموسم : هو أمير الحاج، كما في «مجمع الأنهر ) ، وكانت عادة السلاطين أنهم يرسلون أميراً في كل سنة يولونه أمر الحجاج، وانتظام أمورهم، وإنما لا تجوز له إقامة الجمعة لقصور ولايته ، فإنّه لا يولّى إلا لأمر الحجاج لا لغير ذلك، وإقامة الجمعة إنما هي إلى السلطان أو من أذن له. (٦) قوله : ولا بعرفات ؛ بفتح العين والرَّاءِ المهملتين : اسم الموضع على اثني عشر ميلاً من مكة، يقفُ فيه الحُجَّاجُ يوم التاسع من ذي الحجة، وجمعت وإن كان موضعاً واحداً ؛ لأنَّ كلَّ قطعة منه تسمّى عرفة ؛ ولهذا كانت متصرفة، ويجوز ترك صرفه. (۱) «المغرب»(ص٤٧٦). (۲) (مجمع الأنهر» (۱ : ۱۹۸).
And it is permissible in Mina during the season for the Khalifa, or for the Amir of Hijaz, not for the Amir of the season, nor at Arafat. [1] His saying: 'in Mina'; with kasra on the meem, fatha on noon, alif maqsura at the end: it is a well-known place near honored Mecca. The pilgrims stay there on the Day of Tarwiyah, and the rituals of Hajj such as shaving, stoning the jamarat, and sacrificing are performed there on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and the three days after. It has buildings that are constructed during the days of Hajj, so it becomes a city at that time; therefore Jumu'ah is permissible there at that time, not at other times. Because during the season it has a sultan, an amir, streets, and markets. Not so Arafat, for it is a valley with no buildings and nothing that makes the place a city, so Jumu'ah is absolutely not permissible there. [2] His saying: 'in the season'; i.e., the season of the pilgrims: with kasr on the seen, and it is their market and gathering place, from al-wasm which is the mark. Thus in al-Mughrib. And by 'season' is meant the time when the pilgrims stay in Mina. (3) His saying: 'for the Khalifa'; i.e., the supreme sultan if present. [4] His saying: 'or for the Amir of Hijaz'; with kasr on the ha (muhmala): it is the land of Mecca and Medina and their surroundings of Arab lands, and the Amir of Hijaz is the sultan of Mecca, i.e., the Sharif of Mecca ruling Mecca, Medina, Taif, and adjacent parts of Hijaz. (2) [0] His saying: 'not for the Amir of the season'; i.e., it is not permissible to establish Jumu'ah in Mina for the Amir of the season: he is the amir of the pilgrims, as in Majma' al-Anhur. It was the custom of the sultans that they would send an amir every year to oversee the affairs of the pilgrims and organize their matters. It is not permissible for him to establish Jumu'ah because of the deficiency of his authority, for he is appointed only for the affair of the pilgrims, not for other things, and establishing Jumu'ah is only for the sultan or whoever he authorizes. (6) His saying: 'nor at Arafat'; with fatha on the 'ayn and ra (muhmala): the name of a place twelve miles from Mecca, where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. It is considered plural even though it is a single place, because each part is called 'Arafa; hence it is indeclinable in some respects.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the validity of Friday prayer in Mina during the Hajj season. The matn states that Jumu'ah is permissible (jaza) in Mina during the season for the Khalifa (the supreme ruler) or for the Amir of Hijaz (the ruler of Mecca and its surroundings), but not for the Amir of the season (the amir appointed specifically for the pilgrimage caravan), nor at Arafat. The commentator explains: Mina becomes a city (misr) during the Hajj season because it has buildings, a sultan, an amir, streets, and markets; therefore Jumu'ah is valid there at that time. In contrast, Arafat is a valley without buildings, so it never qualifies as a city and Jumu'ah is not valid there. The limitation of the amir of the season is due to his limited authority—he is only appointed for the affairs of the pilgrims, not for general governance, whereas Jumu'ah is a communal obligation that requires authorization from the sultan or his deputy. The passage also provides linguistic and geographical notes on the terms 'Mina', 'season', 'Khalifa', 'Amir of Hijaz', 'Amir of the season', and 'Arafat'.

Key Terms
منى (Mina): A valley near Mecca where pilgrims stay during Hajj; it becomes a city (misr) during the Hajj season due to temporary buildings and amenities.
الموسم (al-mawsim): The Hajj season, specifically the time when pilgrims are at Mina; it refers both to the market/gathering and the temporal period.
الخليفة (al-khalifah): The supreme ruler (sultan) of the Islamic state, who has authority to establish Jumu'ah.
أمير الحجاز (amir al-Hijaz): The ruler of the Hijaz region (Mecca, Medina, Taif, etc.), typically the Sharif of Mecca.
أمير الموسم (amir al-mawsim): The amir appointed specifically to oversee the pilgrims' caravan; his authority is limited to Hajj matters.
عرفات (Arafat): A valley about 12 miles from Mecca where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; it lacks buildings and does not qualify as a city for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Friday prayer not permissible for the 'Amir of the season' (amir al-mawsim) in Mina according to this passage?
A) Because he is not a resident of Mina.
B) Because his authority is limited to the affairs of the pilgrims and does not extend to establishing Jumu'ah.
C) Because Mina does not have a mosque large enough.
D) Because he is not a descendant of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah in Mina is valid only during the Hajj season and only when led by the supreme ruler or the ruler of Hijaz, due to the requirement of a city and proper authority.

Jumu'ah at Mina and Arafat: Conditions and Proof
Ruling with proof from prophetic practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for Jumu'ah at Mina during Hajj and explain the Hanafi proof for its invalidity at Arafat.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is valid at Mina only with a general ruler; never at Arafat, proven by the Prophet's practice.

Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) has specific conditions for validity, particularly regarding location and authority. During Hajj, Mina becomes a bustling town, while Arafat remains an open plain. The Hanafi school derives its ruling from the actions of the Prophet ﷺ during the Farewell Pilgrimage. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the basic rule: Jumu'ah is valid at Mina in the season, only for the Caliph or Amir of Hijaz, not for the Amir al-Mawsim, and never at Arafat.
2
Understand the geographical distinction
Why does Mina allow Jumu'ah but Arafat does not? Mina has buildings and becomes a town (misr) during Hajj, while Arafat has no buildings.
The Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah is a settled town with a ruler.
3
Classify the authorities
Distinguish the Caliph (supreme ruler) and Amir of Hijaz (local ruler with general authority) from the Amir al-Mawsim (temporary Hajj official). The former have the requisite authority for Jumu'ah; the latter does not.
4
Examine the proof
Analyze the prophetic practice: the Prophet ﷺ and Companions were at Arafat on a Friday and prayed Dhuhr, not Jumu'ah. This is a definitive proof (Sunnah mutawatir) that Jumu'ah is not valid there.
The absence of Jumu'ah despite the day being Friday implies prohibition.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, during Hajj, if a qualified ruler is present at Mina, Jumu'ah is held; at Arafat, even if Friday, Dhuhr is prayed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجازت بمنى في الموسم للخليفة ، أو لأمير الحجاز ، لا لأمير الموسم ، ولا بعرفات. وجازت بمنى في الموسم للخليفة" ، أو لأمير الحجاز، لا لأمير الموسم ، ولا بعرفات [۱] قوله : بمنى ؛ بكسر الميم، وفتح النون في الآخر ألف مقصورة : هو . معروف قرب مكة المشرفة، يقيم فيه الحجَّاجُ يوم التروية، وتؤدى فيه مناسك الحج كالحلق ورمي الجمار والنحر في عاشر ذي الحجة، وثلاثة أيام بعده. وفيه أبنية تعمرُ في أيام الحج، فيكون مصراً في ذلك الوقت فلذا جازت الجمعة فيه في ذلك الوقت دون سائر الأوقات ؛ فإنه يكون فيه في الموسم سلطان وأمير وسكك وأسواق، ولا كذلك عرفات، فإنّها وادٍ ليس فيه بناء، ولا ما يكون به الموضع مصراً، فلا تجوز فيه الجمعة مطلقاً. (۳) قوله : للخليفة ؛ أي السلطان الأعظم إن كان حاضراً. [٤] قوله : أو لأمير الحجاز ، بكسر الحاء المهملة : هو أرض مكة والمدينة وما حولهما من أرض العرب، وأمير الحجاز هو سلطان مكة، أي شريف مكة الحاكم بمكة والمدينة والطائف وما يلي ذلك من أرض الحجاز. [0] قوله : لا لأمير الموسم ؛ أي لا تجوز إقامة الجمعة بمنى لأمير الموسم : هو أمير الحاج، كما في «مجمع الأنهر ) ، وكانت عادة السلاطين أنهم يرسلون أميراً في كل سنة يولونه أمر الحجاج، وانتظام أمورهم، وإنما لا تجوز له إقامة الجمعة لقصور ولايته ، فإنّه لا يولّى إلا لأمر الحجاج لا لغير ذلك، وإقامة الجمعة إنما هي إلى السلطان أو من أذن له. (٦) قوله : ولا بعرفات ؛ بفتح العين والرَّاءِ المهملتين : اسم الموضع على اثني عشر ميلاً من مكة، يقفُ فيه الحُجَّاجُ يوم التاسع من ذي الحجة، وجمعت وإن كان موضعاً واحداً ؛ لأنَّ كلَّ قطعة منه تسمّى عرفة ؛ ولهذا كانت متصرفة، ويجوز ترك صرفه. (۱) «المغرب»(ص٤٧٦). (۲) (مجمع الأنهر» (۱ : ۱۹۸). وقد صح عن النبي الله وأصحابه الله أنهم وقفوا في حجة الوداع به وكان يوم جمعة، فلم يصلوا الجمعة فيه، بل صلوا الظهر على ما هو موجود في الصحاح السنة وغيرها، ولو كانت الجمعة جائزة فيه لما تركوها.
And it is permissible at Mina in the season for the Caliph, or for the Amir of Hijaz, not for the Amir al-Mawsim, nor at Arafat. [1] He said: 'At Mina' – with kasra of the meem and fatha of the noon, and an alif maqsura at the end: it is well-known near Mecca, where pilgrims stay on the day of Tarwiyah, and the rituals of Hajj are performed, such as shaving, stoning the jamarat, and slaughtering on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and the three days after. It has buildings that are inhabited during the days of Hajj, so it becomes a town at that time; therefore Friday prayer is permissible there at that time and not at other times, because during the season there is a sultan, an amir, streets, and markets. But Arafat is not like that; it is a valley with no buildings, nor anything that makes the place a town, so Friday prayer is absolutely not permissible there. [2] He said: 'In the season' – i.e., the season of pilgrims; with kasra of the seen, it is their market and gathering place, derived from wasm (mark). So in al-Mughrib, and what is meant by the season is the time when pilgrims halt at Mina. (3) He said: 'For the Caliph' – i.e., the supreme sultan if he is present. [4] He said: 'Or for the Amir of Hijaz' – with kasra of the ha: it is the land of Mecca and Medina and what surrounds them of the Arab lands, and the Amir of Hijaz is the sultan of Mecca, i.e., the Sharif of Mecca who rules Mecca, Medina, Ta'if, and adjacent lands of Hijaz. [0] He said: 'Not for the Amir al-Mawsim' – i.e., it is not permissible to perform Friday prayer at Mina for the Amir al-Mawsim: he is the commander of the pilgrims, as in Majma' al-Anhur. It was the custom of the sultans to send an amir each year to manage the pilgrims and organize their affairs. It is not permissible for him to lead Friday prayer because his authority is limited; he is only appointed for the affairs of the pilgrims, not for other matters, and Friday prayer is only the responsibility of the sultan or one authorized by him. (6) He said: 'Nor at Arafat' – with fatha of the 'ayn and ra: the name of a place twelve miles from Mecca, where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. It is called 'Arafat in the singular even though it is a single place, because each part of it is called 'Arafa; therefore it is indeclinable, and it is permissible to treat it as such. (1) al-Mughrib (p. 476). (2) Majma' al-Anhur (1:198). And it is authentically reported from the Prophet and his Companions that they stood at Arafat during the Farewell Pilgrimage on a Friday, and they did not perform Friday prayer there, but rather prayed Dhuhr, as is found in the six authentic collections and others. And if Friday prayer had been permissible there, they would not have omitted it.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) and his Companions. The author first states the base ruling: Friday prayer is permissible at Mina during the Hajj season, but only when led by the Caliph (the supreme ruler) or the Amir of Hijaz (the ruler of Mecca and the Hijaz region). It is not permissible when led by the Amir al-Mawsim (the commander of the pilgrimage caravan), and it is never permissible at Arafat. The commentary then explains each term. 'Mina' is a location near Mecca that becomes a town during Hajj due to the presence of buildings, a sultan, amir, and markets; thus it qualifies as a place where Friday prayer is valid during that time. 'Arafat', by contrast, is an open valley with no buildings, so it never qualifies as a town; therefore Friday prayer is never valid there. The term 'season' refers to the time when pilgrims stay at Mina. The 'Caliph' is the supreme ruler, and the 'Amir of Hijaz' is the local ruler of Mecca and its surroundings. The 'Amir al-Mawsim' is a temporary official appointed only for the pilgrimage, so his authority is too limited to lead Friday prayer. The definitive proof is that during the Farewell Pilgrimage, the Prophet (ﷺ) stood at Arafat on a Friday and did not perform Jumu'ah, but instead prayed Dhuhr. If Jumu'ah had been permissible there, he would not have omitted it. This establishes that Friday prayer is not valid at Arafat under any circumstances.

Key Terms
منى (Mina): A location near Mecca where pilgrims stay during Hajj, which becomes a town during the season due to buildings and markets.
عرفات (Arafat): A valley near Mecca where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; it has no buildings and is not considered a town.
الموسم (al-mawsim): The season of Hajj; also the market and gathering of pilgrims.
الخليفة (al-khalifah): The supreme ruler (sultan) who has general authority.
أمير الحجاز (Amir al-Hijaz): The ruler of the Hijaz region (Mecca, Medina, Taif, etc.), i.e., the Sharif of Mecca.
أمير الموسم (Amir al-Mawsim): The commander of the pilgrimage caravan, appointed only for the Hajj season.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because Arafat is not a town (misr) and has no buildings.
C) Because the Prophet and Companions prayed Dhuhr there on a Friday.
D) Because the Amir al-Mawsim does not have authority.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah at Mina during Hajj is valid only with a qualified ruler; at Arafat it is never valid, as established by the Prophet's action.

Condition of the Sultan for Jumu'ah: A Nuanced Hanafi View
Explains the condition of sultanic authorization for Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sultanic authorization for Friday prayer and identify when it is required and when it is not.

Core Idea
The sultan's authorization for Jumu'ah is to prevent disputes, not an absolute condition – when multiple Jumu'ahs exist, it is unnecessary.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a condition often misunderstood: the need for the sultan's permission to hold Friday prayer. The Hanafi school does not treat this as a rigid requirement but as a practical measure to avoid conflict. We'll examine the evidence and the nuanced ruling that balances state authority and communal worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Condition
The act is Jumu'ah prayer. The condition being discussed is the authorization (or presence) of the sultan – the supreme ruler. Note that this is not a pillar (rukn) but a condition of validity under certain circumstances.
Distinguish between conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan).
2
State the Hanafi Position as Given in the Text
According to al-Hidayah and other authorities, Jumu'ah is performed with a large gathering. But disputes over leadership may occur, so the sultan's authorization is needed to avoid hardship. However, this is a matter of preference (ala sabl al-awlawiyyah) when only one Jumu'ah exists; when multiple Jumu'ahs are established without dispute, the condition drops.
Note the shift: it is not an absolute shart.
3
Trace the Proof (Dalil)
The primary dalil is a hadith: 'Whoever abandons it while having an imam, just or unjust, may Allah not unite his affairs.' Though the chains are weak (as noted by Ibn Hajar), the ruling is supported by the practice of the Salaf and the principle of maslaha (public interest). Also cited: al-Hasan al-Basri's statement that Jumu'ah is among the sultan's responsibilities.
Weakness in chain does not always prevent fiqh adoption when supported by other evidence.
4
Analyze the Exceptions and Practical Application
From Jami' al-Rumuz: if the sultan's permission cannot be obtained, the condition is waived. Also, the sultan need not be Muslim. The condition only applies when there is a single Jumu'ah in a city and risk of dispute. If multiple Jumu'ahs are already held without conflict, permission is not needed.
This shows the pragmatic, conflict-avoidance rationale.
5
Conclude with the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the sultan's permission is preferred but not absolutely required. The core principle is preventing fitna (discord).
This aligns with the school's reliance on istihsan and maslaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلطان [١] قوله : والسلطان ; الأصلُ في هذا الاشتراط قوله : «من تركها وله إمامٌ جائر أو عادل، فلا جمع الله شمله ، أخرجه ابن ماجه وغيره. وعن الحسن البصري : «أربع إلى السلطان ؛ وذكر منها إقامة الجمعة والعيدين)، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة. والفقـه فـيـه علـى ما في «الهداية»(۳) ، وغيرها : إنَّ الجمعة تقام بجمع عظيم، وقد تقع المنازعةُ في التَّقدم والتَّقديم ، وفي غيره فلا بُدَّ من السلطان، أو مَن أَذِنَ له بإقامة الجمعة لدفع الحرج، وهذا يرشدك إلى أنَّ اشتراطهُ إنّما هو على سبيل الأولوية حيث لا تتعدد الجمعة، وحيث تعددت فلا حاجة إلى ذلك، وقد كانت إقامة شعائر الإسلام كالجمعة والعيدين في زمان السَّلف مفوضة إلى السلطان ومَن ينوب منابه. وفي «جامع الرموز»: المراد بالسلطان الوالي الذي ليس فوقه وال، عادلاً كان أو أ، والإطلاق مشعر بأنَّ الإسلام ليس بشرط ، وهذا إذا أمكن استئذانه وإلا فالسلطان ليس بشرط ، فلو اجتمعوا على رجل وصلوا جاز كما في صلاة الجنازة جائراً، وغيره. انتهى. جمع (۱) فعن جابر : خطب : ، فقال : «واعلموا أن الله قد افترض عليكم الجمعة في مقامي هذا في يومي هذا في شهري هذا من عامي هذا إلى يوم القيامة، فمن تركها في حياتي أو بعدي وله إمام عادل أو جائر استخفافا بها أو جحودا لها فلا . الله له شمله ولا بارك له في أمره في سنن ابن ماجة» (۱ : ٣٤٣) ، و(المعجم الأوسط (۲) : (٦٤) ، و(مسند عمر بن عبد العزيز» للباغندي (۱ : ۱۰۰ ) ، و (شعب الإيمان (۳) : ١٠٥) ، وقال ابن حجر في «التلخيص»(۲) : ٥٣) : «أخرجه بن ماجة وفيه عبد الله البلوي، وهو واهي الحديث، وأخرجه البزار من وجه ، وفيه علي بن زيد بن جدعان ، قال الدارقطني : إن الطريقين كلاهما غير ثابت ، وقال ابن آخر عبد البر : هذا الحديث واهي الإسناد (۲) فعن الحسن الله قال : أربع إلى السلطان الصلاة والزكاة والحدود، والقضاء» في «مصنف ابن أبي شيبة»(٢ : ٣٨٥). (۳) «الهداية» (۲) : ٥٥) ، وينظر : (المبسوط» (٢ : ٧٦).
And the Sultan [1] He said: 'And the Sultan'; the basis for this condition is his saying: 'Whoever abandons it (Friday prayer) while he has an imam, whether unjust or just, may Allah not unite his affairs' – narrated by Ibn Majah and others. And from al-Hasan al-Basri: 'Four things are the responsibility of the Sultan: the establishment of Friday prayer and the two Eid prayers' – narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah. The fiqh according to al-Hidayah and others is that Friday prayer is performed with a large gathering, and disputes may arise regarding precedence and leadership, so without the Sultan or one he authorizes, it is necessary to avoid hardship. This indicates that the condition is only a matter of preference when Friday prayers are not multiple; when they are multiple, there is no need for that. The establishment of Islamic symbols like Friday and Eid prayers in the time of the Salaf was delegated to the Sultan and his deputies. In Jami' al-Rumuz: what is meant by the Sultan is the ruler who has no ruler above him, whether just or unjust, and the absolute term suggests that Islam is not a condition. If it is possible to seek his permission, (it is required); otherwise, the Sultan is not a condition. If they gather upon a man and pray, it is permissible, as in the funeral prayer and others. [End of commentary] Footnotes: (1) From Jabir: He (the Prophet) gave a sermon saying: 'Know that Allah has made Friday prayer obligatory upon you in this place, on this day, in this month, from this year until the Day of Judgment. So whoever abandons it in my life or after me, having an imam just or unjust, out of disregard or denial, then Allah will not unite his affairs nor bless his matters.' – in Sunan Ibn Majah (1:343), al-Mu'jam al-Awsat (2:64), Musnad Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz (1:100), Shu'ab al-Iman (3:105). Ibn Hajar in al-Talkhis (2:53) said: 'Ibn Majah narrated it and in it is Abdullah al-Balawi, who is weak. And al-Bazzar narrated it from another chain containing Ali ibn Zaid ibn Jud'an. Al-Daraqutni said: Both chains are unproven. Ibn Abd al-Barr said: This hadith is weak in chain.' (2) From al-Hasan: 'Four things are the responsibility of the Sultan: prayer, zakat, prescribed punishments, and judgment' – in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (2:385). (3) al-Hidayah (2:55); see also al-Mabsut (2:76).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition that Friday prayer must be led or authorized by the sultan (or his deputy). The author begins with the base text 'And the Sultan' and then provides the commentary. The primary proof for this condition is a hadith (though weak in chain, but supported by practice) from the Prophet: 'Whoever abandons Friday prayer while having an imam, just or unjust, then Allah will not unite his affairs.' This indicates the importance of the state's role in Jumu'ah. The Hanafi position, as explained in al-Hidayah, is that Jumu'ah requires a large gathering, and without the sultan's authorization, disputes over leadership would arise. Therefore, the condition is to avoid fitna. However, this condition is only 'ala sabl al-awlawiyyah (preferential) when there is only one Jumu'ah in a city. If multiple Jumu'ahs are already established without dispute, then the sultan's authorization is not necessary. This was the practice of the Salaf. From Jami' al-Rumuz, it is added that the sultan is the supreme ruler, and his Islam is not a condition. If his permission cannot be obtained, the condition is waived, and the congregation may choose any imam, similar to funeral prayer. Thus, the condition is pragmatic, not absolute. The commentary also cites al-Hasan al-Basri's statement that four matters fall under the sultan's authority, including Jumu'ah and Eid prayers. The footnotes provide the exact texts of the hadiths and their chain evaluations, noting the weakness of the first hadith but its acceptance in fiqh due to supporting evidence.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or supreme authority who has no ruler above him; his authorization is needed for Jumu'ah in cases where disputes may arise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is the sultan's authorization for Jumu'ah not required according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the sultan is unjust.
B) When the sultan's permission cannot be obtained.
C) When multiple Jumu'ahs are already established without dispute.
D) When the imam is a Companion.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi condition of sultanic authorization for Jumu'ah is pragmatic, aimed at preventing discord, and is not required when multiple Jumu'ahs exist without conflict.

The Condition of the Sultan for Friday Prayer
Ruling with proof on sultan's condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sultan's permission for Jumu'ah and explain why it is a condition of priority (awlawiyyah) rather than a strict condition of validity (shart al-sihhah).

Core Idea
The sultan's permission for Friday prayer is a preferred arrangement, not a strict condition; Jumu'ah is valid without it when necessary.

This passage tackles a crucial question: is the ruler's authorization necessary for Friday prayer to be valid? The Hanafi school has nuanced views, from early texts emphasizing the sultan's role to later fatwas granting flexibility. By examining the proofs and commentaries, you will understand how the school reconciled textual evidence with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed condition
The act is the Friday congregational prayer (Jumu'ah). The disputed condition is whether the sultan's permission (ishtirat al-sultan) is required for its validity.
The passage discusses both the hadith proof and the practical reasoning behind the condition.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith cited as evidence: 'Whoever abandons it while having an imam, whether unjust or just, may Allah not gather his affairs.' Note its chain weakness.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah and is considered da'if (weak) by some muhaddithun.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith mentions an imam (ruler) in the context of abandonment, implying that Jumu'ah is only properly established under a ruler. However, the author shows this interpretation is not definitive.
Later scholars reinterpret the hadith as a threat against those who abandon Jumu'ah despite having a rightful imam, not as a condition for validity.
4
Trace the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school
Note the different views: al-Hidayah suggests the sultan's permission is necessary to avoid disputes, but later scholars like Bahr al-'Ulum argue it is not a condition, citing the Companions' practice during 'Uthman's fitnah.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (disagreement within the school).
5
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
The author of 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah favors the later view that the condition is only a priority (awlawiyyah). The mufta bihi is that Jumu'ah is valid without the sultan's permission when seeking it is impossible or causes hardship.
This tarjih is based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle of facilitating worship.

وفي «رسائل الأركان» لبحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي اللكنوي: لم أطلع على دليل يفيد اشتراط أمر السلطان، وما في «الهداية» رأي لا يثبت به الاشتراط لإطلاق نصوص وجوب الجمعة ، ثمَّ هذه المنازعة تندفع بإجماع المسلمين على تقديم واحد، أو كما في جماعة الصلوات عسى أن تقع المنازعة في تقديم رجل، لكن تندفع بإجماع المصلين، فكذا في الجمعة.
ثم الصحابة أقاموا الجمعة في زمان فتنة أمير المؤمنين عثمان ، وكان هو إماماً حقاً محصوراً، ولم يعلم أنهم طلبوا منه الإذن، بل الظاهر عدم الإذن ؛ لأنَّ هؤلاء الأشقياء من أهل الشَّرِّ لم يرخّصُوا في ذلك.
فعُلِمَ أنَّ إقامة الجمعة غير مشروطة عندهم بالإذن، ولعل لهذه الواقعة رجع المشايخ له عن هذا الشرط فيما تعذر فيه الاستذان من الإمام، وأفتوا بأنه إن تعذر الاستئذان من الإمام فاجتمع الناس على رجـل يـصـلـي بـهـم الجـمـعـة جـاز، كذا في «العالمكيرية» ناقلاً عن «التهذيب». انتهى.
