مسلماً. انتهى.
(۱) من «الهداية (٢) : ٥٥).
Book of Prayer: Friday Prayer. The Sultan. (1) It is authentically reported that the Prophet and his Companions stopped at 'Arafah during the Farewell Pilgrimage on a Friday and did not pray Jumu'ah there, but prayed Zuhr, as found in authentic collections. If Jumu'ah had been permissible there, they would not have left it. [1] His statement: 'The Sultan.' The basis for this condition is his saying: 'Whoever abandons it while having an imam, whether unjust or just, may Allah not gather his affairs.' Ibn Majah and others narrated it. And from al-Hasan al-Basri: 'Four things are with the sultan: establishment of Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids.' Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated it. The fiqh according to al-Hidayah and others: Jumu'ah is established with a large gathering, and disputes may arise about precedence and appointment, so the sultan or his authorized deputy is necessary to prevent hardship. This indicates that its conditioning is a matter of priority where Jumu'ah is not multiplied, but if multiplied, there is no need for it. The establishment of Islamic rituals like Jumu'ah and 'Eids in the time of the Salaf was delegated to the sultan and his deputies. In Jami' al-Rumuz: 'The sultan means the ruler above whom there is no ruler, whether just or unjust, and the absolute term suggests that Islam is not a condition. If permission can be obtained, otherwise the sultan is not a condition. If they gather upon a man and pray, it is permissible, as in the funeral prayer.' End. (1) From Jabir: He addressed saying: 'Know that Allah has obligated Jumu'ah upon you in this place, in this day, in this month, in this year until the Day of Judgment. Whoever abandons it in my lifetime or after, having a just or unjust imam, out of disdain or denial, may Allah not gather his affairs and not bless his matter.' In Sunan Ibn Majah (1:343), al-Mu'jam al-Awsat (2:64), Musnad 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz by al-Baghandi (1:100), Shu'ab al-Iman (3:105). Ibn Hajar said in al-Talkhis (2:53): 'Ibn Majah narrated it and in it is 'Abdullah al-Balawi, a weak narrator. Al-Bazzar narrated it from another chain with 'Ali ibn Zayd ibn Jud'aan. Al-Daraqutni said both chains are unconfirmed. Ibn 'Abd al-Barr said the hadith has a weak chain.' (2) From al-Hasan that he said: 'Four things are with the sultan: prayer, zakat, hudud, and judiciary.' In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (2:385). (3) Al-Hidayah (2:55), and see al-Mabsut (2:76). (Then page 322) 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. In Ma'raj al-Dirayah from al-Mabsut: 'Countries in the hands of unbelievers are lands of Islam, not of war, because they do not manifest the rule of unbelief. Rather, the judges and governors are Muslims who obey them out of necessity or otherwise. Every city that has a deputy from their side, it is permissible for him to establish Jumu'ah, 'Eids, hudud, and appoint judges. If the governors are unbelievers, it is permissible for Muslims to hold Jumu'ah, and the judge becomes a judge by mutual consent of Muslims, and they must seek a Muslim governor.' End. In Fath al-Mannan fi Ta'yid Madhhab al-Nu'man by Shaykh 'Abd al-Haqq Dihlawi, after summarizing al-Hidayah's statement: 'It is not permissible to establish it except for the sultan or one he orders, because it is established with a large gathering, and disputes may arise about precedence and appointment, so it is necessary for completing its matter.' End (1). This is the statement of al-Hidayah. Its apparent meaning indicates priority and precaution rationally, not conditionality, and the impermissibility of prayer without it legally. End summarized. In Rasa'il al-Arkan by Bahr al-'Ulum Mawlana 'Abd al-'Ali al-Lakhnawi: 'I have not come across proof supporting the condition of the sultan's order. What is in al-Hidayah is an opinion that does not establish conditionality due to the absolute texts of the obligation of Jumu'ah. Moreover, this dispute is resolved by the consensus of Muslims on appointing one person, or as in congregational prayers, a dispute may occur about appointing a person but is resolved by the consensus of the worshippers, so too in Jumu'ah.' Then, the Companions established Jumu'ah during the fitnah of 'Uthman, while he was the legitimate imam under siege, and it is not known that they sought permission from him; rather, it is apparent that they did not, because those wicked people did not allow it. So it is understood that Jumu'ah is not conditioned by permission according to them. Perhaps for this incident, the later scholars retracted this condition in cases where permission is impossible, and they gave fatwa that if seeking permission is impossible, people may gather upon a man to lead them in Jumu'ah. As in al-'Alamgiriyyah quoting from al-Tahdhib. End. In Majma' al-Fatawa: 'Muslims are overcome by unbelieving rulers; it is permissible for Muslims to hold Jumu'ah and 'Eids, and the judge becomes a judge by mutual consent of Muslims, and they must seek a Muslim governor.' End. (1) From al-Hidayah (2:55).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the condition of the sultan (ruler) for the validity of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by noting an incident from the Farewell Pilgrimage where the Prophet and Companions did not pray Jumu'ah at 'Arafah on a Friday, which some use to argue that Jumu'ah is not valid without a sultan, but the author implies this is not a strong proof. Then the main discussion starts with a hadith from Ibn Majah threatening severe punishment for abandoning Jumu'ah despite having an imam (ruler), and a statement from al-Hasan al-Basri that four matters (including Jumu'ah) are the sultan's responsibility. The core ruling from al-Hidayah is that Jumu'ah requires the sultan's presence or authorization to prevent disputes in selecting an imam. However, the author clarifies that this is a matter of priority (awlawiyyah), not a strict condition, especially when multiple congregations exist. The passage then cites various commentaries: Jami' al-Rumuz explains that if seeking permission is impossible, the condition drops, and people may appoint their own imam. Ma'raj al-Dirayah and Mabsut discuss the case of Muslim lands under non-Muslim rule, permitting Jumu'ah without the ruler's permission. Fath al-Mannan reiterates that the Hidayah's wording implies priority, not a legal condition. Rasa'il al-Arkan argues forcefully that there is no proof for conditionality, citing the absolute obligation of Jumu'ah and the practice of the Companions during the fitnah of 'Uthman, who held Jumu'ah without the Caliph's permission. Finally, Majma' al-Fatawa confirms the permissibility under non-Muslim rulers. The overall conclusion of the passage is that the sultan's permission is a preferred arrangement to avoid discord, but in cases of necessity or impossibility, Jumu'ah is valid without it. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) to facilitate worship.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or his authorized deputy who has authority over the region where Jumu'ah is held.
اشتراط (ishtirat): The act of making something a condition (shart) for validity; here, the difference between a strict condition and a preferred arrangement (awlawiyyah).
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, a fard 'ayn substitute for Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the ruling on Jumu'ah when the sultan's permission cannot be obtained?
A) Jumu'ah is invalid without the sultan's permission.
B) Jumu'ah is valid if people gather and appoint an imam.
C) Jumu'ah must be replaced by Zuhr prayer.
D) Jumu'ah is only valid if the sultan is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that the sultan's permission is not a condition for Jumu'ah's validity; it is a preferred arrangement to avoid discord, and Jumu'ah is valid without it when necessary.

Salah — Prayer

Sultan's Permission for Jumu'ah in Non-Muslim Lands
Ruling with proof on Jumu'ah permission condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require sultan's permission for Jumu'ah in non-Muslim lands and apply the principle of necessity to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah remains valid without sultan's permission when obtaining it is impossible, as necessity overrides conditionality.

This passage addresses a critical Hanafi debate: does the validity of Jumu'ah prayer depend on the permission of the sultan? The source compiles multiple authorities, from al-Mabsut to al-Durr al-Mukhtar, ultimately concluding that in lands dominated by non-Muslims, the condition is not required due to necessity (darurah) and the practice of the Companions. You will learn how later Hanafi masters resolved this ikhtilaf and the practical implications for Muslims living under non-Muslim rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central legal question
The passage centers on whether the sultan's permission (idhn al-sultan) is a condition (shart) for the validity of Jumu'ah. Note the opposing views: some, like the author of al-Hidayah, assert it as necessary; others deny conditionality.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school, not just between madhhabs.
2
Examine the opposing position (from al-Hidayah)
Al-Hidayah states: 'It is not permissible to establish Jumu'ah except for the sultan or one whom the sultan commands.' This is based on potential disputes in large gatherings. But the commentary explains this is a cautious opinion, not a strict condition.
The phrase 'la tajuuz' can imply impermissibility, but later scholars reinterpret it as caution (ihtiyat).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: absolute texts and historical precedent
The obligation of Jumu'ah is absolute (Qur'an 62:9). The Companions performed Jumu'ah during Uthman's fitna without seeking his permission, showing it is not conditional. The consensus of the congregation resolves disputes, so no need for external authority.
The historical precedent is powerful: if the Companions did not seek permission during a time of fitna, it is not required.
4
Understand the role of necessity (darurah)
When seeking permission is difficult or impossible (e.g., under non-Muslim rule), necessity permits Jumu'ah without permission. This is supported by al-Durr al-Mukhtar and other later texts.
The principle 'al-darurat tubih al-mahzurat' is at work: necessity overrides the cautionary condition.
5
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that Jumu'ah is valid without sultan's permission when it is difficult to obtain. Muslims in non-Muslim lands may establish Jumu'ah by mutual consent, and it is obligatory to seek a Muslim governor where possible.
This is the position of later Hanafi masters (fatawa mutakhkhirin), and contrary fatwas are considered misguided.

طلبوا منه الإذن، بل الظاهر عدم الإذن ؛ لأنَّ هؤلاء الأشقياء من أهل الشَّرِّ لم يرخّصُوا في ذلك. فعُلِمَ أنَّ إقامة الجمعة غير مشروطة عندهم بالإذن، ولعل لهذه الواقعة رجع المشايخ له عن هذا الشرط فيما تعذر فيه الاستذان من الإمام، وأفتوا بأنه إن تعذر الاستئذان من الإمام فاجتمع الناس على رجـل يـصـلـي بـهـم الجـمـعـة جـاز، كذا في «العالمكيرية» ناقلاً عن «التهذيب». انتهى. وفي «مجمع الفتاوى»: غلب على المسلمين ولاة كفار يجوز للمسلمين الجمعُ والأعياد، ويصير القاضي قاضياً بتراضي المسلمين ، ويجب عليهم أن يلتمسوا والياً مسلماً. انتهى. وفي «الدر المختار»: «نصب العامة الخطيب غير معتبر مع وجودِ من ذكر، أما مع عدمهم فيجوز للضرورة. انتهى. ولعلك تتفطن من هذه العبارات ونحوها أنه لا شك في وجوب الجمعة، وصحة أدائها في بلاد الهند التي غلبت عليها النّصارى وجعلوا عليها ولاة كفّار، وذلك باتفاق المسلمين وبتراضيهم، ومن أفتى بسقوط الجمعة لفقد شرط السلطان فقد ضَلَّ وأضل، هذا وللتفصيل موضع آخر.
In 'Miraj al-Diraya' from 'al-Mabsut': The lands that are in the hands of disbelievers are Lands of Islam, not the abode of war; because they have not manifested the rule of disbelief therein, rather the judges and governors are Muslims who obey them out of necessity or without it. And every city where there is a representative from their side, it is permissible for him to perform Jumu'ah, Eid prayers, and hudud, and to appoint judges. If the governors are disbelievers, it is permissible for the Muslims to perform Jumu'ah, and the judge becomes a judge by the mutual consent of the Muslims, and it is obligatory upon them to seek a Muslim governor. End quote. In 'Fath al-Mannan fi Ta'yid Madhhab al-Nu'man' by Sheikh Abd al-Haqq al-Dahlawi, after mentioning the gist of the expression of 'al-Hidayah' which is: 'It is not permissible to establish it except for the sultan or one whom the sultan commands; because it is established with a great congregation, and dispute may occur about precedence and appointment, and about other matters, so it is necessary to complete its affair.' End quote. This is the determination of al-Hidayah, and its apparent meaning indicates priority and caution rationally, not conditionality, and that it is not permissible to pray without it legally. End summarised. In 'Rasa'il al-Arkan' by Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali al-Lakhnawi: I have not come across a proof that indicates the conditionality of the sultan's command, and what is in al-Hidayah is an opinion that does not establish conditionality due to the absoluteness of the texts obligating Jumu'ah. Moreover, this dispute is repelled by the consensus of Muslims on appointing one person, or as in congregational prayers, perhaps dispute may occur about appointing a man, but it is repelled by the consensus of the congregation, so too in Jumu'ah. Then the companions performed Jumu'ah during the time of the fitna of Amir al-Mu'minin Uthman, and he was the true and confined imam, and it is not known that they sought permission from him, rather the apparent is the lack of permission; because those wretched evildoers did not permit that. So it is known that establishing Jumu'ah is not conditional upon permission according to them. Perhaps due to this incident, the mashayikh retracted from this condition when seeking permission from the imam is difficult, and they gave fatwa that if seeking permission from the imam is difficult and the people gather upon a man to lead them in Jumu'ah, it is permissible. Similarly in 'al-Alamgiriyya', quoting from 'al-Tahdhib'. End quote. In 'Majma' al-Fatawa': If non-Muslim governors overcome the Muslims, it is permissible for Muslims to perform Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, and the judge becomes a judge by mutual consent of Muslims, and it is obligatory upon them to seek a Muslim governor. End quote. In 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar': 'The appointment of the general public for the khatib is not considered when those mentioned are present, but if they are absent, then it is permissible due to necessity.' End quote. Perhaps you pay heed from these expressions and the like that there is no doubt about the obligation of Jumu'ah and the validity of its performance in the lands of India that have been dominated by Christians and they made non-Muslim governors over them, and that is by the agreement of Muslims and by their mutual consent. And whoever gives a fatwa of the non-obligation of Jumu'ah due to the lack of the condition of the sultan has gone astray and leads others astray. This, and for detailed discussion there is another place.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings and scholarly discussions on the validity of Jumu'ah prayer in Muslim lands that have come under the control of non-Muslim rulers. The author begins by quoting from 'Miraj al-Diraya' citing 'al-Mabsut', which establishes that lands under non-Muslim rule remain abodes of Islam as long as Islamic rulings (like Jumu'ah, Eid, hudud) are manifest. It is permissible for Muslims to perform Jumu'ah if there is a Muslim representative; if the governors are non-Muslims, Muslims may still perform Jumu'ah with mutual consent and must seek a Muslim governor. Next, from 'Fath al-Mannan', the position of 'al-Hidayah' is quoted, which states that Jumu'ah is only permissible for the sultan or his deputy, due to potential disputes. However, the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' explains that this ruling is based on priority and caution, not a strict condition. 'Rasa'il al-Arkan' argues that there is no evidence for conditionality; the texts obligating Jumu'ah are absolute, and disputes are resolved by consensus. Historical evidence from the time of Caliph Uthman shows that the Companions performed Jumu'ah without seeking his explicit permission during the fitna. Therefore, the condition of sultan's permission is not absolute; when it is difficult to obtain, Muslims may appoint an imam themselves. This is supported by 'al-Alamgiriyya' and 'Majma' al-Fatawa'. Finally, 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' states that the public's appointment of a khatib is disallowed if a capable sultan or deputy exists, but allowed in their absence due to necessity. The author concludes that in lands like India under Christian rule, Jumu'ah is obligatory and valid by consensus and mutual agreement; contrary fatwas are misguided.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultān): The sovereign ruler or his authorized deputy who has authority over public religious affairs.
الاستئذان (al-isti'dhān): Seeking permission from the ruler or his deputy for establishing Jumu'ah.
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): Necessity that permits normally restricted actions; here, allows Jumu'ah without sultan's permission when it is impossible to obtain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the later Hanafi masters allowed Jumu'ah without sultan's permission?
A) The sultan's permission is always impossible to obtain.
B) The texts obligating Jumu'ah are absolute and the Companions did not seek permission during the fitna of Uthman.
C) The Shafi'i school accepted it, so Hanafis followed.
D) The rulers were non-Muslims, so their permission is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is valid without sultan's permission when it is difficult to obtain, especially in non-Muslim lands; the condition is a cautionary opinion, not a binding requirement.

Three Conditions for Jumu'ah: Deputy, Time, and Sermon
Line-by-line commentary on the matn's three conditions for Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school and cite the primary evidence for the time condition.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires three conditions: a ruling authority, the Dhuhr time window, and a sermon — all rooted in clear proof.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah unpacks three essential conditions for Jumu'ah prayer. Each condition — the presence of a sultan or his deputy, the time of Dhuhr after zawal, and the sermon — is directly tied to the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the consensus of the scholars. Understanding these conditions helps you distinguish valid Jumu'ah from invalid assemblies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition: the sultan or his deputy
Note that the deputy is defined broadly as anyone entrusted with general public affairs, even if not explicitly assigned to Jumu'ah.
This is a Hanafi broadening; other schools may have a stricter requirement.
2
Examine the time condition with its proof
Jumu'ah must be performed after zawal (sun's decline after zenith). The passage cites two hadith from Bukhari and Muslim as explicit evidence.
The key phrases 'hina tamīlu al-shams' and 'idhā zālat al-shams' leave no room for pre-zawal Jumu'ah.
3
Understand the uniqueness of the time for Jumu'ah
Unlike other prayers, Jumu'ah is valid only in the Dhuhr time window; it cannot be performed before or after.
Quoting al-Ghunya: 'al-Jumu'ah valid only in this time, unlike other prayers.'
4
Analyze the sermon condition
The sermon (khutbah) is a condition by consensus of the majority, supported by the Prophet's constant practice and a report from al-Zuhri.
The passage does not detail the sermon's content, only that it is required before the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١]قوله : أو نائبه ؛ هو الذي أمرَهُ السُّلطانُ بإقامة الجمعة ونحوها صراحة أو دلالة، فلا خفاء في أنَّ مَن فُوِّضَ إليه أمرُ العامة في مصر له إقامتها، وإن لم يُفوّضها إليه السلطان صريحاً. كما في «الخلاصة»، وغيرها. [٢] قوله : وقت الظهر؛ فلا تجوزُ الجُمُعة قبل الزَّوال، ومَن جَوَّزَ ذلك فقد أخطأ فلم يثبت في حديث صحيح صريح مرفوع صلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه قبل الزوال، وقد أخرج البخاري في صحيحه» : عن أنس له : «كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الجمعة حين تميل الشمس ، وفي صحيح مسلم»: «كنا نجمع مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا زالت الشمس ثم نتبع الفيء» [٣]قوله : الظهر ؛ قال في «الغُنية»: وهو إن كان شرطاً لسائر الصلوات إلا أنَّ الجمعة تختص بأنها لا يصح إلا فيه بخلاف سائر الصلوات. (٤) قوله : والخطبة ؛ كونها شرطاً لصحة الجمعة مما أجمع عليه جمهور الأمة، ويستأنس له بأن النبي ما صلى بدون الخطبة، ذكره البيهقي، وذكر عن الزُّهْرِيِّ الله قال : «بلغنا أنّه لا جمعةَ إلا (خطبة)
[1] His statement: 'or his deputy' – he is the one whom the sultan has commanded to establish Jumu'ah and the like explicitly or implicitly. So there is no obscurity that whoever is entrusted with the general affairs of the people in a city has the authority to establish it, even if the sultan did not explicitly delegate it to him. As in 'al-Khulasa' and others. [2] His statement: 'time of Dhuhr' – so Jumu'ah is not permissible before zawal (declination of the sun), and whoever permitted that has erred; it has not been established in an authentic, explicit, marfu' hadith that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم and his Companions prayed before zawal. Al-Bukhari narrated in his Sahih from Anas: 'The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to pray Jumu'ah when the sun declined.' And in Sahih Muslim: 'We used to pray Jumu'ah with the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم when the sun passed the meridian, then we would follow the shade.' [3] His statement: 'Dhuhr' – He said in 'al-Ghunya': Although it is a condition for other prayers, Jumu'ah is specific in that it is valid only in this time, unlike other prayers. (4) His statement: 'and the sermon' – that it is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah is something upon which the majority of the ummah have agreed. And it is supported by the fact that the Prophet never prayed without a sermon. Al-Bayhaqi mentioned it, and reported from al-Zuhri that he said: 'It has reached us that there is no Jumu'ah except with a sermon.'
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a line-by-line commentary on the matn's conditions for Jumu'ah. First, the term 'or his deputy' (na'ib) refers to anyone explicitly or implicitly appointed by the sultan to manage public affairs. According to 'al-Khulasa', even if not specifically tasked with Jumu'ah, such a person can lead it because he oversees general matters. Second, the time for Jumu'ah is the same as Dhuhr, i.e., after zawal (sun's decline). The commentator refutes those who permit Jumu'ah before zawal, citing authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim that the Prophet and Companions prayed Jumu'ah only after the sun passed the meridian. The unique aspect, as noted in 'al-Ghunya', is that Jumu'ah is confined to this time, unlike other prayers which have a wider window. Third, the sermon (khutbah) is a condition for Jumu'ah by consensus of the majority. Evidence includes the constant practice of the Prophet (never omitting the sermon) and a report from al-Zuhri that Jumu'ah is incomplete without it. This commentary reinforces the standard Hanafi position on these three essentials.

Key Terms
النائب (al-nā'ib): The deputy of the sultan who is entrusted with public affairs, even if not explicitly assigned to Jumu'ah.
الزوال (al-zawāl): The sun's passage across the meridian; the time for Dhuhr and Jumu'ah begins.
الخطبة (al-khuṭbah): The sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer, consisting of praise of Allah, salawat, admonition, and dua.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence that Jumu'ah prayer must be performed after zawal (declining of the sun)?
A) Consensus of all scholars.
B) Narrations from Anas in Bukhari and Muslim that the Prophet prayed Jumu'ah after zawal.
C) The Qur'anic verse on Jumu'ah.
D) The ruling that Jumu'ah replaces Dhuhr.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is valid only with three conditions: a ruling authority (sultan/deputy), the Dhuhr time after zawal, and a sermon.

The Sultan's Deputy for Jumu'ah and Validity Under Non-Muslim Rule
Defines the deputy for Jumu'ah and affirms its validity under non-Muslim rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Sultan's deputy for Jumu'ah and explain the basis for the validity of Jumu'ah under non-Muslim rule using the argument from ijma.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is valid under non-Muslim rule by Muslim consensus, even without a Muslim ruler.

This lesson examines a key fatwa from the Hanafi tradition regarding Friday prayer in lands under non-Muslim sovereignty. The source defines the Sultan's deputy and then argues, based on the consensus (ijma) of Muslims, that Jumu'ah remains obligatory and valid even when a Muslim ruler is absent, provided Muslims mutually agree to perform it. This ruling addresses a critical historical and contemporary concern for Muslims living under non-Muslim governments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Start by noting that Friday prayer is wajib, but its validity requires the presence of the Sultan or his deputy. This is a shart (condition) for Jumu'ah in normal circumstances.
The condition is specific to Jumu'ah, not other prayers.
2
Understand the definition of deputy
The deputy (na'ib) is anyone explicitly or implicitly authorized by the Sultan to establish Jumu'ah and similar functions. Even a general public administrator qualifies, as per al-Khulasah.
Implicit authorization is sufficient; explicit mention of Jumu'ah is not required.
3
Recognize the exception for necessity
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar states that when qualified deputies are absent, common people may appoint a khatib out of necessity (darurah). This is the basis for the fatwa in non-Muslim lands.
Necessity overrides the normal condition.
4
Apply the ijma proof
The author uses the consensus (ijma) of Muslims in India under Christian rule as proof that Jumu'ah is valid. Muslim agreement (ittifaq) and mutual consent establish the ruling.
This is a practical application of ijma as a source of law.
5
Refute the opposing view
The author strongly rejects any fatwa claiming Jumu'ah is invalid due to lack of a Muslim ruler, calling it misguided. The correct position is that the condition is relaxed in necessity.
This refutation is based on the evidence of necessity and consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١]قوله : أو نائبه ؛ هو الذي أمرَهُ السُّلطانُ بإقامة الجمعة ونحوها صراحة أو دلالة، فلا خفاء في أنَّ مَن فُوِّضَ إليه أمرُ العامة في مصر له إقامتها، وإن لم يُفوّضها إليه السلطان صريحاً. كما في «الخلاصة»، وغيرها. وفي «الدر المختار»: «نصب العامة ) الخطيب غير معتبر مع وجودِ من ذكر، أما مع عدمهم فيجوز للضرورة. انتهى (۲) ولعلك تتفطن من هذه العبارات ونحوها أنه لا شك في وجوب الجمعة، وصحة أدائها في بلاد الهند التي غلبت عليها النّصارى وجعلوا عليها ولاة كفّار، وذلك باتفاق المسلمين وبتراضيهم، ومن أفتى بسقوط الجمعة لفقد شرط السلطان فقد ضَلَّ وأضل، هذا وللتفصيل موضع آخر.
[1] His saying: 'or his deputy' – he is the one whom the Sultan has commanded to establish the Friday prayer and the like, explicitly or by implication. There is no obscurity that whoever is entrusted with the affairs of the public in a city has the right to establish it, even if the Sultan did not explicitly delegate it to him, as in al-Khulasah and others. And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: 'The appointment of the common people to the position of khatib is not considered valid in the presence of those mentioned (i.e., eligible persons), but in their absence it is permissible out of necessity.' End. Perhaps you will discern from these expressions and the like that there is no doubt about the obligation of Friday prayer and the validity of performing it in the lands of India that were dominated by the Christians and they appointed over them infidel rulers. That is by the consensus of Muslims and by their mutual consent. Whoever issues a fatwa that Friday prayer is invalid due to the lack of the condition of the Sultan has gone astray and leads astray. This and for detail (there is) another place.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah deals with the condition of the Sultan or his deputy for the validity of Friday prayer. The author first defines 'deputy' (na'ib) as someone explicitly or implicitly authorized by the ruler to lead the Friday prayer and similar religious functions. It clarifies that if a person is appointed to manage public affairs in a city, he is considered a deputy even without explicit mention of the Friday prayer, citing al-Khulasah. Then, quoting al-Durr al-Mukhtar, it states that common people appointing a khatib is invalid when there are qualified deputies, but permitted out of necessity when none exist. The author then draws a practical fatwa: despite India being under Christian rule, Friday prayer is valid because Muslims mutually agree to perform it. Anyone who claims the Sultan's condition is lacking for Jumu'ah in such lands is mistaken. The consensus (ittifaq) of Muslims is the proof (ijma).

Key Terms
نائب (na'ib): A person appointed by the Sultan to establish Friday prayer and similar religious functions, either explicitly or implicitly by being entrusted with public affairs.
سلطان (sultan): The Muslim ruler or authority who has jurisdiction over the territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is Friday prayer valid in a land under non-Muslim rule?
A) Only if a deputy is explicitly appointed by a Muslim sultan.
B) By the consensus and mutual consent of Muslims, even without a Muslim ruler.
C) Only if the ruler is Muslim and the khatib is appointed by him.
D) It is never valid without a Muslim ruler.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is valid under non-Muslim rule by Muslim consensus, overriding the condition of a Muslim ruler when necessity demands.

Time of Friday Prayer: After Zawal
Proves Friday prayer time after zawal using hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of Friday prayer and cite the two hadith proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
Friday prayer before zawal is invalid — no authentic hadith supports it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that Friday (Jumu'ah) prayer is only valid after the sun declines from its zenith (zawal). The author of the text asserts that any view permitting Jumu'ah before zawal is mistaken and lacks authentic prophetic evidence. We will explore the two hadith from Sahih Bukhari and Sahih Muslim that form the basis of this ruling and understand why the time condition is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. Here, the act is Friday prayer (Jumu'ah). The ruling: it is not permissible before zawal; time after zawal is a condition for validity.
The text explicitly says 'لا تجوز الجمعة قبل الزوال' (Friday is not permissible before zawal).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited by the author. The author quotes two hadith: one from Bukhari (from Anas) and one from Muslim. Both describe the Prophet's practice of praying Jumu'ah after zawal.
Hadith texts are provided in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith prove the ruling. The explicit description of the Prophet's action (praying 'when the sun declined') demonstrates that the prescribed time is after zawal. The constancy of this practice implies it is a binding condition.
The author also notes that there is no authentic marfu' hadith showing prayer before zawal.
4
Note the absence of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school is unanimous on this point. The author does not mention any disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or Muhammad al-Shaybani. All agree that Jumu'ah before zawal is invalid.
This strengthens the authority of the ruling within the madhhab.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that any Jumu'ah prayer offered before the sun begins to decline is invalid and must be repeated. This ruling is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) and is consistent across the Hanafi tradition.
Cross-madhhab: some other schools may allow earlier time under necessity, but Hanafis hold firmly to after zawal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : وقت الظهر؛ فلا تجوزُ الجُمُعة قبل الزَّوال، ومَن جَوَّزَ ذلك فقد أخطأ فلم يثبت في حديث صحيح صريح مرفوع صلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه قبل الزوال، وقد أخرج البخاري في صحيحه» : عن أنس له : «كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الجمعة حين تميل الشمس ، وفي صحيح مسلم»: «كنا نجمع مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا زالت الشمس ثم نتبع الفيء»
[2] His saying: 'time of zuhr' – Thus Friday prayer is not permissible before zawal (the sun's decline from zenith). Whoever permits that has erred, for there is no established authentic, clear, marfu' hadith of the Prophet's prayer or his Companions before zawal. Al-Bukhari narrated in his Sahih from Anas: 'The Prophet would pray Friday when the sun began to decline.' And in Sahih Muslim: 'We would pray Friday with the Messenger of Allah when the sun had passed the zenith, then we would follow the shade.'
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof establishing the time condition for Friday prayer. The author asserts that Jumu'ah is not valid before zawal (the sun's peak). It is an error to permit it earlier, as there is no authentic proof of the Prophet or his Companions praying Friday before zawal. The proof comes from two hadith: one in Bukhari from Anas stating the Prophet prayed when the sun declined, and one in Muslim stating they prayed after the sun passed the zenith and then the shade followed. These clearly indicate the time is after noon.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The sun's decline from its zenith, i.e., the beginning of zuhr prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith quoted, when did the Prophet perform Friday prayer?
A) Before the sun reached its zenith.
B) When the sun began to decline (after zawal).
C) At any time after dawn.
D) After the time for 'Asr began.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is only valid after the sun declines from its zenith (zawal); no authentic hadith supports an earlier time.

The Exclusive Time Condition of Friday Prayer
A brief note on the time condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Friday prayer's time condition is more restrictive than other prayers and identify the consequence of missing the zuhr time for Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is uniquely restricted to zuhr time; it has no qada.

In this brief passage from Al-Ghunyab, the commentator clarifies a nuance about the condition of time for Friday prayer. While time is a general condition for all prayers, Friday prayer is distinct because it cannot be performed outside its prescribed slot. This has a practical impact: if you miss Friday prayer, you do not pray it later as a makeup; instead, you pray zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general condition
Recognize that the act under discussion is Salat al-Jumu'ah. The condition (shart) mentioned is time—specifically the time of zuhr after zawal (declination of the sun).
Time is a condition for all obligatory prayers, but here the focus is on a special restriction.
2
Note the special feature: exclusivity
The passage states 'Friday prayer is distinctive in that it is not valid except in it.' This means Jumu'ah is confined to the zuhr time slot; no other time suffices.
The word 'لا يصح إلا فيه' emphasizes exclusivity.
3
Contrast with other prayers
Other prayers, like zuhr itself, can be performed in other times as qada (makeup) if missed. But Jumu'ah has no such option—if the time passes, the obligation to pray Jumu'ah is gone and replaced by the obligation to pray zuhr.
This is the practical difference the passage highlights with 'بخلاف سائر الصلوات'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣]قوله : الظهر؛ قال في «الغُنية»: وهو إن كان شرطاً لسائر الصلوات إلا أنَّ الجمعة تختص بأنها لا يصح إلا فيه بخلاف سائر الصلوات.
[3] His saying: 'zuhr' – It is mentioned in al-Ghunyab: 'Although it is a condition for all prayers, Friday prayer is distinctive in that it is not valid except in it, unlike other prayers.'
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This is a brief definition ruling. The comment on the matn phrase 'zuhr' explains that while the time of zuhr (after zawal) is a condition for all prayers, Friday prayer is unique in that it cannot be performed at any other time—it is specifically restricted to the time of zuhr. Other prayers like zuhr itself can be made up if missed, but Friday prayer has no qada' in its own form; it must be within its time.

Key Terms
ظلم (zuhr): The midday prayer time after zawal; specifically the time slot for Friday prayer.
شرط (shart): A condition; here time is a condition for the validity of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Friday prayer's time condition differ from other prayers according to the passage?
A) It is the same as all prayers; time is a condition for all.
B) It is only valid in the time of zuhr, unlike other prayers which can be performed in other times.
C) It can be performed before zuhr if necessary.
D) There is no time condition for Friday prayer.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is uniquely restricted to the time of zuhr; if missed, it cannot be made up—one must pray zuhr instead.

The Khutbah as a Condition for Friday Prayer
Establishes the khutbah as a condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence that makes the khutbah a condition for Jumu'ah and explain why it is considered a shart rather than a sunnah.

Core Idea
The khutbah is an essential condition for Jumu'ah; without it, the prayer is invalid.

This lesson explores one of the distinctive requirements of Friday prayer: the khutbah. While many Muslims know that a sermon is delivered before Jumu'ah, the Hanafi school, in agreement with the majority, considers it a binding condition (shart), not merely a recommended practice. We'll examine the proofs—both consensus and the Prophet's consistent practice—that establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage to determine what exactly is being ruled upon: the khutbah's status in relation to Friday prayer.
The ruling is that the khutbah is a condition (shart) for validity.
2
Locate the first proof: Ijma
The passage states that the majority of the ummah have agreed (ijma) that the khutbah is a condition. Consider why ijma is a strong source in Hanafi fiqh.
Ijma is a primary source after Quran and Sunnah.
3
Locate the second proof: Sunnah (practice of the Prophet)
The passage notes that the Prophet (peace be upon him) never performed Jumu'ah without a khutbah. This continuous practice (sunnah fi'liyyah) supports the condition.
The report is cited from al-Bayhaqi.
4
Examine the supporting hadith from al-Zuhri
Al-Zuhri's statement: 'It has reached us that there is no Friday prayer except with a khutbah.' This is a mursal hadith, which Hanafis accept under certain conditions.
The text is quoted in the passage.
5
Understand the consequence of omitting the khutbah
If the khutbah is omitted, the Friday prayer is invalid (batil). This distinguishes it from a sunnah, whose omission does not invalidate.
This is the practical implication of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤) قوله : والخطبة ؛ كونها شرطاً لصحة الجمعة مما أجمع عليه جمهور الأمة، ويستأنس له بأن النبي ما صلى بدون الخطبة، ذكره البيهقي، وذكر عن الزُّهْرِيِّ الله قال : «بلغنا أنّه لا جمعةَ إلا (خطبة)» (۱) في الأصل : إمامة، والمثبت من الدر المختار»(٢ : ١٤٣). (۲) من «الدر المختار (٢ : ١٤٣). (۳) في صحيح البخاري (۱ : ۳۰۷) ، و (سنن الترمذي»(۲ : ۳۷۷)، وغيرها. (٤) في (صحيح مسلم (۲ : ٥٨٩)، وغيره. (٥) في سنن البيهقي الكبير»(٣: ١٩٦)، وغيره.
(4) His saying: 'and the khutbah' – it being a condition for the validity of Friday prayer is a matter of consensus (ijma) of the majority of the ummah. Support for it is that the Prophet never prayed without the khutbah, as mentioned by al-Bayhaqi, and he reported from al-Zuhri that he said: 'It has reached us that there is no Friday prayer except with a khutbah.' (Footnote 1: In the original: 'imamah', and it is corrected from al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2:143. (2) From al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2:143. (3) In Sahih al-Bukhari 1:307, and Sunan al-Tirmidhi 2:377, etc. (4) In Sahih Muslim 2:589, etc. (5) In Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir 3:196, etc.)
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage rules that the khutbah is a condition (shart) for the validity of Friday prayer. The proof is twofold: first, consensus (ijma) of the majority of the ummah; second, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) never praying Friday without a khutbah, reported by al-Bayhaqi. A further evidence is a statement from al-Zuhri that 'It has reached us that there is no Friday prayer except with a khutbah.' The footnotes clarify textual variants and sources of hadith. The khutbah is thus an integral part of Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer, considered a condition for its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence is given in the passage for the khutbah being a condition of Jumu'ah?
A) Only the consensus of the majority.
B) Only the hadith of al-Bayhaqi.
C) Both consensus (ijma) and the practice of the Prophet (never without khutbah).
D) A verse from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah, proven by ijma and the Prophet's continuous practice; without it, the prayer is invalid.

Timing and Congregation for the Friday Khutbah
Details timing and congregation conditions for the khutbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions of the Friday khutbah regarding timing and congregation and explain why a weak hadith cannot be used as evidence.

Core Idea
The khutbah must be after zawal, before prayer, and in congregation – conditions based on sound practice, not a weak hadith.

The Friday khutbah is a pillar of Jumu'ah. This lesson clarifies its temporal and social requirements: it must occur after noon, before the prayer, and in the presence of a valid congregation. A weak hadith suggesting otherwise is dismissed by Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing conditions
The khutbah must be after zawal (noon) and before the prayer. If delivered before zawal, it must be repeated.
These are two distinct conditions.
2
Understand the refutation of the weak hadith
A hadith by al-Daraqutni claims the Prophet and caliphs delivered khutbah before zawal. Hanafi scholars (al-Zayla'i, Ibn al-Humam, etc.) rule it weak (da'if) and not hujjah.
3
Determine the congregation requirement
The correct view (al-ashah) is that the khutbah must be in the presence of a group with whom Jumu'ah is valid. Delivering khutbah alone invalidates it.
This is from al-Bahr.
4
Apply these conditions
If any condition is missing, the khutbah is invalid and must be repeated, which in turn affects the validity of the Jumu'ah prayer.
The khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] نحو تسبيحة قبلها في وقتها (۱) ) ولو لم تكن شرطاً لتركه لبيان الجواز ولو مرَّة ، ويشترط أن تكون بعد الزوال، فلو خطب قبله أعادها ، وما روى الدارقطني : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبا بكر وعمر ه كانت خطبتهم قبل الزوال» فسنده ضعيف لا يحتج به، كما ذكرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِي (٢) وابنُ الهُمَام (۳) والعيني وغيرهم. وكذا يشترط كونهما قبلها ؛ لأن شرط الشيء لا يتأخر عنه، وإلى هذين الشرطين أشار المصنف الله بقوله : «قبلها في وقتها»، وهل يشترط كونهما بحضرة جماعة تنعقد بهم الجمعة أو لا؟ الأصحُ : نعم ؛ فلو خطب وحده لم يجزه. كذا في «البحر»(1). ولا يشترط كونها بالعربية ؛ فلو خطب بالفارسية أو بغيرها جاز، كذا قالوا ، والمراد بالجواز هو الجواز في حقِّ الصَّلاة، بمعنى أنه يكفي لأداء الشرطية، وتصح بها الصلاة، لا الجواز بمعنى الإباحة المطلقة، فإنّه لا شك في أنَّ الخطبة بغيرِ العربية خلافُ السنة المتوارثة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والصحابة الله فيكون مكروهاً تحريماً، وكذا قراءة الأشعار الفارسيّةِ الهندية فيها، وقد فصلنا هذا المقامَ في رسالتنا «آكامُ النَّفائس في أداء الأذكار بلسان الفارس. [١]قوله : نحو تسبيحة ؛ هذا بيانُ مقدار الخطبة الشَّرط ، وحاصله : أنه يكفي فيها مقدار التسبيحة أو تحميدة أو تهليلة بنية الخطبة ؛ لإطلاق قوله : إذا نُودِى لِلصَّلَوةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إلى ذكر الله له (0) لكن لا يخلو الاقتصار على هذا من الكراهية. كما في «الدر المختار»، و«جامع الرموز» لكونه مخالفاً السُّنَّة ؛ فإنَّ النَّبي الله كان يخطبُ خُطبتين ويجلس بينهما جلسة خفيفة
[1] 'Such as a tasbihah before it in its time' – Even if it (i.e., the phrase) were not a condition, he would have omitted it to indicate permissibility even once. It is required that it (the khutbah) be after zawal; if he delivers the khutbah before it, he must repeat it. What al-Daraqutni narrated: 'The Prophet, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar used to deliver the khutbah before zawal' – its chain is weak and not hujjah, as mentioned by al-Zayla'i, Ibn al-Humam, al-'Ayni, and others. Likewise, it is required that both (the two khutbahs) be before the prayer, because the condition of a thing cannot be after it. To these two conditions the author (may Allah have mercy on him) pointed by his saying: 'before it in its time.' And is it required that they (the two khutbahs) be in the presence of a group (jama'ah) with whom Friday prayer is valid? The correct view is yes; if he delivers the khutbah alone, it is not valid. Thus in al-Bahr. And it is not required that it be in Arabic; if he delivers the khutbah in Persian or another language, it is permissible. Thus they said. And what is meant by 'permissibility' here is permissibility in relation to the prayer, i.e., it suffices for fulfilling the condition and the prayer is valid with it, not permissibility in the sense of absolute licitness, for there is no doubt that the khutbah in other than Arabic violates the transmitted Sunnah of the Prophet and the Companions, so it is makruh tahrimi. Similarly, reciting Persian or Indian poems in it (the khutbah) is also reprehensible. We have expounded on this topic in our treatise 'Akam al-Nafa'is fi Ada' al-Adhkar bi Lisan al-Faris. [1] His saying: 'such as a tasbihah' – This explains the minimum amount of the khutbah that is a condition. Its summary: it suffices to have the amount of a tasbihah, or a tahmidah, or a tahlilah with the intention of the khutbah, due to the general reference of His saying: 'O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (62:9). However, confining oneself to this amount is not free from karahah (dislike), as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Jami' al-Rumuz, because it contradicts the Sunnah; indeed, the Prophet used to deliver two khutbahs and sit briefly between them.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage details multiple conditions of the khutbah for Friday prayer. It begins by explaining the matn phrase 'نحو تسبيحة قبلها في وقتها' (such as a tasbihah before it in its time). The first condition: the khutbah must be after zawal (noon). If delivered before, it must be repeated. A weak hadith from al-Daraqutni claiming the Prophet and his companions preached before zawal is dismissed as unreliable. Second condition: the khutbah must be before the prayer itself, as the condition precedes the conditioned. These two are referred to by the author's words 'before it in its time'. Third: the khutbah must be in the presence of a valid congregation for Jumu'ah; if one preaches alone, it is invalid (from al-Bahr). Fourth: the khutbah need not be in Arabic; it is permissible in Persian or other languages, but this permissibility is only for the validity of the prayer (i.e., it fulfills the condition) – however, using non-Arabic is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it contradicts the transmitted sunnah. Reciting poems in Persian or Hindi is also disliked. Finally, the minimum content: the khutbah must contain at least the equivalent of a tasbihah (glorification of Allah), a tahmidah (praise), or a tahlilah (declaration of His oneness) with the intention of delivering a khutbah. This is based on the verse 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (62:9), which is general. However, it is disliked to limit the khutbah to this minimum, as the Prophet's practice was to give two longer khutbahs with a sitting between them.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The declination of the sun from the meridian; the beginning of the time for Zuhr prayer.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): A group large enough to constitute a valid Friday congregation (usually minimum 3 or 4, depending on the view).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the Friday khutbah according to the passage?
A) The khutbah must be after zawal.
B) The khutbah must be before the prayer.
C) The khutbah must be delivered in Arabic.
D) The khutbah must be in the presence of a valid congregation.

Key Takeaway
The khutbah must be after zawal, before prayer, and in congregation; a weak hadith cannot overturn these conditions.

Language and Minimum Content of the Friday Khutbah
Details language ruling and minimum content of the khutbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the language of the khutbah and the minimum required content, and distinguish between validity and dislike.

Core Idea
Non-Arabic khutbah is valid but makruh tahrimi; a single tasbihah suffices but is also disliked — the Sunnah is longer and in Arabic.

The khutbah's wording and length have specific guidelines. While Arabic is not a condition for validity, abandoning it contradicts the Sunnah. Similarly, the bare minimum of a short dhikr meets the requirement but is blameworthy. This lesson breaks down these nuanced rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the language ruling
Arabic is not a condition; a khutbah in Persian or any other language is permissible (ja'iz).
This is the Hanafi position.
2
Understand the scope of permissibility
Permissibility here means the prayer is valid with such a khutbah, not that it is absolutely allowed without dislike.
The text distinguishes between permissibility for validity and absolute licitness.
3
Note the karahah of non-Arabic
Using non-Arabic is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it violates the transmitted Sunnah of the Prophet and Companions.
This applies even if the congregation cannot understand Arabic; the khatib should strive to learn.
4
Determine the minimum content
It suffices to have the amount of a tasbihah (e.g., 'Subhanallah'), tahmidah, or tahlilah with the intention of khutbah.
This is based on the general command in Quran 62:9 to 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah'.
5
Recognize the karahah of the minimum
Confining the khutbah to this minimum is disliked because it contradicts the Prophet's practice of delivering two longer khutbahs with a sitting between them.
The karahah is tanzihi? The text says 'does not free from karahah' (dislike). Some scholars say it is tanzihi, but the text says 'makruh tahrimi' for language; for minimum, the karahah is likely tanzihi.

تحميدة (tahmidah): Saying 'Alhamdulillah' (all praise is due to Allah).
تهليلة (tahlilah): Saying 'La ilaha illallah' (there is no god but Allah).

8 min
Minimum Khutbah for Friday Prayer: Ruling, Conditions, and Dispute
States the minimum dhikr for khutbah and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum khutbah according to Abu Hanifa, apply the conditions for its validity, and explain the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding its length.

Core Idea
A single tasbih can fulfill the Friday khutbah — but the prophetic practice demands more.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the minimum requirement of the Friday sermon. While the matn suggests a brief dhikr suffices, the commentary unpacks the conditions, the dispute with the Sahibayn and Shafi'is, and the ruling on language and congregation. Understanding this will help you distinguish between the obligatory minimum and the recommended Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum khutbah according to Abu Hanifa
The matn states 'naw tashiha' meaning a short utterance like tasbih. The commentary confirms that a tasbih, tahmid, or tahlil with the intention of khutbah is sufficient.
This is the fard (obligatory) minimum; anything beyond is Sunnah.
2
Locate the proof
The verse 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (62:9) is cited. The word 'dhikr' is absolute (mutlaq), so any remembrance qualifies.
The Shafi'is consider the verse mujmal, requiring the Prophet's explanation.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn and Shafi'i positions
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a lengthy khutbah customary among people. Shafi'i requires two khutbahs with specific elements (tahmid, recitation, supplication).
The Sahibayn's view is often relied upon in later fatwa.
4
Analyze the conditions
The khutbah must be after zawal, before the prayer, in the presence of a valid congregation, and may be in any language but doing so is makruh tahrimi.
The condition of congregation is agreed upon by the Imams.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a minimal khutbah (one tasbih) is valid for Abu Hanifa but not for Sahibayn or Shafi'i. This affects those unable to deliver a lengthy khutbah.
This highlights the importance of knowing which view one follows in practice.

خطبتهم قبل الزوال» فسنده ضعيف لا يحتج به، كما ذكرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِي وابنُ الهُمَام والعيني وغيرهم. وكذا يشترط كونهما قبلها؛ لأن شرط الشيء لا يتأخر عنه، وإلى هذين الشرطين أشار المصنف بقوله : «قبلها في وقتها»، وهل يشترط كونهما بحضرة جماعة تنعقد بهم الجمعة أو لا؟ الأصحُ : نعم؛ فلو خطب وحده لم يجزه. كذا في «البحر». ولا يشترط كونها بالعربية؛ فلو خطب بالفارسية أو بغيرها جاز، كذا قالوا، والمراد بالجواز هو الجواز في حقِّ الصَّلاة، بمعنى أنه يكفي لأداء الشرطية، وتصح بها الصلاة، لا الجواز بمعنى الإباحة المطلقة، فإنّه لا شك في أنَّ الخطبة بغيرِ العربية خلافُ السنة المتوارثة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والصحابة فيكون مكروهاً تحريماً، وكذا قراءة الأشعار الفارسيّةِ الهندية فيها، وقد فصلنا هذا المقامَ في رسالتنا «آكامُ النَّفائس في أداء الأذكار بلسان الفارس». قوله : نحو تسبيحة؛ هذا بيانُ مقدار الخطبة الشَّرط، وحاصله : أنه يكفي فيها مقدار التسبيحة أو تحميدة أو تهليلة بنية الخطبة؛ لإطلاق قوله : إذا نُودِى لِلصَّلَوةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إلى ذكر الله . لكن لا يخلو الاقتصار على هذا من الكراهية. كما في «الدر المختار»، و«جامع الرموز» لكونه مخالفاً للسُّنَّة؛ فإنَّ النَّبي كان يخطبُ خُطبتين ويجلس بينهما جلسة خفيفة وكان يثني على الله فيهما، ويَذْكُرُ ويُبَيِّنُ الأحكام المناسبة، ويقرأ فيها آيات من القرآن، كما لا يخفى على من وقف على الصحاح الستة وغيرها. قوله : هذا؛ أي كونُ الفرض من الخطبة نحو تسبيحة دون ما زاد عليها. قوله : فلا بد؛ أي يشترط أن تكون الخطبة ذكراً طويلاً مما يعده أهل العرف خطبة، فإنَّ مجرَّدَ التَّحميد ونحوه لا يسمى خطبة. قوله : وعند الشافعي ... الخ؛ استدلال له بأن قوله : فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكرِ اللَّهِ مجمل فالتحق بيان النبي بياناً له، ولم تخلُ خطبة من الخطب النبوية عن التحميل والقراءة والدعاء ونحو ذلك، وكذا توارث عن الصحابة له، وأجيب بأن الآية ليست بمجملة بل مطلقة، فيعمل بإطلاقه، ويجعل أدناه فرضاً، ويعمل بالطريقة المتوارثة فتجعل سنة. قوله : والجماعة؛ كونها شرطاً لصحة الجمعة، مجمع عليه من الأئمة وغيرهم، كما في «الغنية» و«البناية»، والأصل فيه قوله : فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ . هذا عند أبي حنيفة. وأما عندهما فلا بد من ذكر طويل يسمى خطبة. وعند الشافعي لا بد من خطبتين يشتمل كل واحد منهما على الصلاة، والتحميد، والوصية بالتقوى، والأولى على القراءة، والثانية على الدعاء للمؤمنين.
Like a tasbih, before it, in its time. Even if it is not a condition, leaving it is to indicate permissibility even once. It is required that it be after zawal; if he delivers the khutbah before it, he repeats it. What al-Daraqutni narrated: 'The Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar used to deliver their khutbah before zawal' – its chain is weak, not to be relied upon, as mentioned by al-Zayla‘i, Ibn al-Humam, al-‘Ayni, and others. Similarly, it is required that both (khutbah and prayer) be before it? Because the condition of a thing does not come after it. The author referred to these two conditions by his saying: 'before it, in its time.' Is it required that both be in the presence of a congregation with which Jumu‘ah is held or not? The correct view: yes; if he delivers the khutbah alone, it is not sufficient. Thus in 'al-Bahr.' It is not required that it be in Arabic; if he delivers the khutbah in Persian or another language, it is permissible, as they said. And by permissibility is meant permissibility in relation to the prayer, meaning it suffices to fulfill the condition and the prayer is valid with it, not permissibility in the sense of absolute permissibility, for there is no doubt that the khutbah in other than Arabic is contrary to the transmitted Sunnah from the Prophet and the Companions, so it is makruh tahrimi. Similarly, reciting Persian and Indian poems in it. We have detailed this topic in our treatise 'Akam al-Nafa'is fi Ada' al-Adhkar bi Lisan al-Faris.' His statement: 'like a tasbih' – this is an explanation of the amount of the obligatory khutbah, and its summary: that an amount of a tasbih, or tahmid, or tahlil with the intention of khutbah is sufficient in it, due to the generality of His statement: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' But confining to this is not free from karahah (dislike). As in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' and 'Jami‘ al-Rumuz' because it is contrary to the Sunnah; for the Prophet used to deliver two khutbahs and sit briefly between them, and he would praise Allah in them, mention and explain appropriate rulings, and recite verses of the Quran in them, as is not hidden from one who has studied the six authentic collections and others. His statement: 'this' – i.e., that the obligation of the khutbah is something like a tasbih without what is more than it. His statement: 'it is necessary' – i.e., it is required that the khutbah be a lengthy remembrance that people customarily consider a khutbah, for mere tahmid and the like is not called a khutbah. His statement: 'According to al-Shafi‘i...' – a proof for him that His statement: 'Hasten to the remembrance of Allah' is Mujmal, so the Prophet's explanation becomes its explanation, and no khutbah from the prophetic khutbahs was devoid of tahmid, recitation, supplication, and the like. Similarly, this was transmitted from the Companions. It is answered that the verse is not Mujmal but rather absolute (mutlaq), so one acts upon its absolute nature and makes its minimum obligatory, and one acts upon the transmitted method and makes it Sunnah. His statement: 'and congregation' – it being a condition for the validity of Jumu‘ah is agreed upon by the Imams and others, as in 'al-Ghuny' and 'al-Binaya', and its basis is His statement: 'Hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is necessary that it be a lengthy remembrance called a khutbah. According to al-Shafi‘i, two khutbahs are necessary, each containing salutation upon the Prophet, praise of Allah, and admonition of piety; the first also includes a Quranic recitation, and the second includes supplication for the believers.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the chapter of Jumu'ah from al-Wiqayah. The author discusses the minimum requirement of the Friday sermon (khutbah) and its conditions. The matn states 'naw tashiha qablaha fi waqtiha' meaning the khutbah can be as short as a single tasbih (glorification of Allah) and it must be delivered before the prayer and within the time of Zuhr. The commentary clarifies that this is the obligatory minimum (fard) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. However, the author notes that limiting the khutbah to that minimum is makruh tanzihi because it contradicts the prophetic practice. He then discusses three conditions: (1) the khutbah must be after zawal (noon), (2) it must be before the prayer, and (3) it should be in the presence of a congregation that is valid for Jumu'ah. As for the language, the khutbah in a non-Arabic language fulfills the condition but is makruh tahrimi due to being contrary to the Sunnah. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa holds that a minimal dhikr is sufficient, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a lengthy speech that is customarily called a khutbah. The author then mentions the Shafi'i view requiring two khutbahs with specific elements. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i position is that the verse 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' is absolute (mutlaq), so the minimum is fard, and the prophetic practice is Sunnah, not obligatory. Finally, the condition of congregation (jama'ah) for Jumu'ah is affirmed by consensus.

Key Terms
نحو تسبيحة (naḥwa tasbīḥa): Literally 'like a tasbih', meaning a short utterance glorifying Allah, such as 'subhanallah'.
خُطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday prayer; a condition for its validity.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition that must be fulfilled for the prayer to be valid; if omitted, the prayer is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the minimum amount of dhikr that fulfills the condition of khutbah for Jumu'ah according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) A lengthy speech that customarily qualifies as a khutbah
B) A single tasbih, tahmid, or tahlil
C) Two khutbahs with specific elements including praise, recitation, and supplication
D) At least one verse from the Quran

Key Takeaway
A single tasbih fulfills the khutbah condition according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sunnah is longer; the khutbah must be after zawal, before prayer, and in congregation.

The Khutbah in Jumu'ah: Minimal Requirement Dispute
Dispute on minimal khutbah requirement among Hanafi imams and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the minimum khutbah obligation in Jumu'ah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the interpretation of the Qur'anic verse.

Core Idea
The khutbah's fard is just a short dhikr; the Prophet's detailed practice is sunna, not fard.

This passage dives into a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the Friday sermon (khutbah). At stake is what the Qur'anic command 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' actually obligates. The Hanafi school argues it is an absolute (mutlaq) command, so any dhikr fulfills the fard. The Shafi'i school argues it is general (mujmal) and needs the Prophet's practice to specify it, resulting in a detailed two-sermon requirement. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi usul principles to derive fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its internal variant
Note that Abu Hanifa says a short dhikr (like a tasbih) is fard, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require a long speech customarily called a khutbah. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is important for fatwa; the relied-upon position is the minimal one.
2
Understand the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Al-Shafi'i requires two khutbahs each containing praise, thanks, enjoining piety, with the first including recitation and the second including supplication. He argues that the verse 'fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' is mujmal, clarified by the Prophet's consistent practice.
The Shafi'i position derives obligation from the sunnah as a specification of the Qur'anic command.
3
Analyze the linguistic usul distinction: mutlaq vs mujmal
The Hanafi response is that the verse is not mujmal but mutlaq (absolute). In Hanafi usul, a mutlaq text is applied as is without requiring specification. Therefore, the minimum (any dhikr) is fard, and the detailed prophetic practice is sunna.
This distinction is the core of the dispute. Understanding it helps you see how usul principles directly affect fiqh rulings.
4
Trace how each school's usul leads to a different fiqh ruling
Hanafi: because the command is mutlaq, the obligatory part is a short dhikr; anything more is sunna. Shafi'i: because the command is mujmal, the prophetic practice specifies it, making the detailed components obligatory.
Note that both schools use the same primary source (Qur'an and Sunnah) but differ in the usul method of combining them.
5
State the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, a Hanafi can fulfill the khutbah obligation with a very brief dhikr (e.g., 'SubhanAllah'), whereas a Shafi'i must hear the full two sermons with the specific components. This difference affects validity of Jumu'ah for followers of each school.
This is why knowing the mufta bihi position matters: it determines what is sufficient in actual worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

خطبة ، فإنَّ مجرَّدَ التَّحميد ونحوه لا يسمى خطبة.

Book of Prayer: Friday Prayer and Congregation. This is according to Abu Hanifa. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), a long speech called a khutbah is necessary. According to al-Shafi‘i, two khutbahs are necessary, each comprising praise of Allah, thanking, and enjoining piety; the first includes recitation, the second includes supplication for the believers. And he would praise Allah in them, mention and explain appropriate rulings, and recite verses from the Quran, as is clear to one who has studied the six authentic collections and others. His statement: 'this' means that the obligatory part of the khutbah is something like a tasbih without more. His statement: 'necessary' means the khutbah must be a long speech considered a khutbah by custom, for mere praise and the like is not called a khutbah. His statement: 'according to al-Shafi‘i...' is evidence for him that Allah's saying 'so hasten to the remembrance of Allah' is general (mujmal) and the Prophet's explanation clarified it; no prophetic khutbah was devoid of praise, recitation, supplication, etc., and likewise it was transmitted from the Companions. The response is that the verse is not general but absolute (mutlaq), so it is applied according to its absolute sense, and its minimum is considered obligatory, while the transmitted method is made sunna.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the khutbah of Jumu'ah. The text first states Abu Hanifa's position: the obligatory (fard) part of the khutbah is merely a short dhikr such as a tasbih (saying 'SubhanAllah'). Anything beyond that is sunna. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require a long speech that is customarily called a khutbah. Imam al-Shafi‘i requires two khutbahs, each containing specific components: praise of Allah (tahmid), enjoining piety (wasiyya bi al-taqwa), and the first includes a Quranic recitation while the second includes supplication for the believers. The commentary then explains that the Shafi‘i argument is based on treating the command 'fas‘aw ila dhikr Allah' as a general (mujmal) statement clarified by the Prophet's practice. The Hanafi response is that the verse is absolute (mutlaq), not general, so its minimum (any dhikr) is fard, and the detailed practice reported from the Prophet is sunna. This reflects the Hanafi usul principle that a mutlaq text is applied as is without requiring specification.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before Jumu'ah prayer; its obligatory minimum is a short dhikr according to Abu Hanifa.
فرض (fard): Obligatory element; omission invalidates the prayer.
مطلق (mutlaq): An absolute text that does not require specification; applies to all instances of the genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum obligatory (fard) part of the Jumu'ah khutbah?
A) A long speech containing praise, recitation, and supplication
B) A short dhikr such as 'SubhanAllah'
C) Two separate sermons
D) Recitation of a verse from the Quran

Key Takeaway
The khutbah's fard is a short dhikr; the Prophet's detailed practice is sunna, a distinction rooted in the Hanafi usul principle of mutlaq vs mujmal.

Conditions for Jumu'ah: Congregation and Minimal Number
Discusses congregation as a condition and the minimal number of participants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimal number required for Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and apply the rule on participants leaving during the prayer.

Core Idea
Congregation is a condition for Jumu'ah, but its validity is tied to the number at initiation, not continuation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the condition of congregation for Jumu'ah, focusing on the minimal number (three or four) and what happens if participants leave. The commentary expands on the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and introduces the concept of shart in'iqad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that congregation (jama‘ah) is a condition for Jumu'ah by consensus, based on the verse 'fas‘aw ila dhikr Allah'.
This is a shart for validity, not a pillar.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa requires 3 men besides the imam (total 4); Abu Yusuf requires 2 men besides the imam (total 3).
Both views are within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the proofs
Abu Hanifa uses the plural 'fas‘aw' (implies at least three) and excludes the imam from that address. Abu Yusuf analogizes to other congregational prayers (minimum 3 total).
The proof for Abu Hanifa is a direct textual inference; Abu Yusuf uses qiyas.
4
Analyse the response
The commentators prefer Abu Hanifa's proof, as it is directly from the Quran and excludes the imam. This view is affirmed by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha.
Mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Understand the practical implication
If participants leave, the ruling depends on when they leave and how many remain. The distinction between shart in'iqad (condition for initiation) and shart dawam (condition for continuance) explains why leaving after the first rak'ah does not invalidate Jumu'ah.
Shart in'iqad means the condition must be met at the start; it need not persist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والجماعة ؛ كونها شرطاً لصحة الجمعة، مجمع عليه من الأئمة وغيرهم، كما في «الغنية» و«البناية»، والأصل فيه قوله تعالى: { فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ }.
وهم ثلاثة رجال سوى الإمام عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف له اثنان سوى الإمام، فإنّ نفروا قبل سجوده بدأ بالظهر، وإن بقي ثلاثة رجال، أو نفروا بعد سجوده أتمها، والإذن العام (۳۱) ،
وبه استدل محمد للإمام على أنَّ أقل الجماعة في أربعةٍ مع الإمام ؛ لأنَّ الأمر بالسعي وردَ بصيغة الجمع ، وأقله ثلاثة ، وفهم منه أنَّ الذاكر غيرهم. وعند أبي يوسف يكفي ما يكفي بغيرها، وهو الثلاثة مع الإمام، ورَجَّحَ الشارحونَ دليل قول الإمام ، قاله قاسم بن قطلوبغا في «تصحيح القدوري». (۱) قوله : ثلاثة رجال ؛ احترز عن النِّساءِ والصبيان، وفي الإطلاق إشارة إلى أنه لا يشترط كونهم الذين حضروا الخطبة.
[٢]قوله : فإن نفروا ؛ أي فروا وتركوا الاشتراك في الصلاة قبل سجودِ الإمام للركعة الأولى، بدأ بالظهر إلا إذا بقي ثلاثة ، وإن نفروا بعد الركعة الأولى أتم الجمعة، والوجه فيه أنَّ الجماعة وإن كانت شرطاً لصحة الجمعة، لكن لا يلزم بقاؤها إلى آخرها ؛ لأنه شرط انعقاد لا شرط دوام وبقاء ، إلا أنَّ عندهما شرط انعقاد التحريمة، وعنده شرط انعقاد الأداء ، ولا يتحقق الأداء إلا بوجود تمام الأركان، فلذا فرَّق بين النَّفرِ قبل السجودِ وبعده ؛ لأنَّ قبل السُّجودِ لا يكون أداءً للصلاة، فإنَّ أقلها ركعة. كذا في «البحر». [۳] قوله : والإذن العام ؛ هذا الشَّرطُ لم يذكر في «الهداية»، ولا أثر له في ظاهر الرواية، وإنّما هو مذكورٌ في «النوادر» ومشى عليه أصحاب المتون، واستنبط من قوله تعالى: { يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلَاةِ مِن يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ }، فإنَّ النِّدَاءَ لِلِاشْتِهَارِ، وفيه نظر لا يخفى.
His statement: 'and congregation' means that it is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah, agreed upon by the imams and others, as in al-Ghunya and al-Binaya. The basis is His saying: 'so hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' They are three men besides the imam according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf he has two besides the imam. If they leave before his prostration, he begins with Zuhr; if three remain, or if they leave after his prostration, he completes it. And the general permission (general permission). By this Muhammad argued for the imam that the minimum congregation is four with the imam, because the command to hasten came in the plural form, the minimum of which is three, and it is understood that the one remembering (the imam) is other than them. According to Abu Yusuf, what suffices for other prayers is sufficient, i.e., three with the imam. The commentators preferred the evidence of the imam's statement. Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said this in Tashih al-Quduri. His statement: 'three men' excludes women and boys; the absolute expression indicates that it is not required that they be those who attended the khutbah. His statement: 'if they leave' means they flee and abandon participation in the prayer before the imam's prostration for the first rak'ah; he begins with Zuhr unless three remain; if they leave after the first rak'ah, he completes Jumu'ah. The reason is that congregation, although a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah, its continuation to the end is not necessary; it is a condition for initiation, not a condition for continuance. However, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is a condition for the initiation of the tahrima, while according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is a condition for the initiation of performance, and performance is not realized except with the completion of all pillars; hence the distinction between leaving before prostration and after, because before prostration there is no performance of the prayer, since the minimum is a rak'ah. Thus in al-Bahr. His statement: 'the general permission' – this condition was not mentioned in al-Hidaya, nor is it found in Zahir al-Riwayah; rather it is mentioned in al-Nawadir and followed by the authors of the texts. It is derived from His saying: 'O you who believe, when the call to prayer is made on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah', for the call is for publicity, but there is obvious consideration in it.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. First, congregation (jama‘ah) is a condition by consensus, based on the verse 'fas‘aw ila dhikr Allah'. The text then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimal number: according to Abu Hanifa, the congregation must have three men besides the imam (total four), because the verse uses the plural 'fas‘aw' which implies at least three, and the imam is not included in that number. Abu Yusuf holds that three total (including the imam) suffice, as that is the minimum for other congregational prayers. The commentators prefer Abu Hanifa's view. The passage then addresses what happens if some people leave during the prayer: if they leave before the imam's prostration in the first rak‘ah, the imam switches to Zuhr unless at least three remain; if they leave after the first rak‘ah, he continues Jumu'ah. This distinction is due to Abu Hanifa's view that congregation is a condition for the initiation of the actual performance (ada’), which begins with the first rak‘ah. Finally, the condition of general permission (‘idhn ‘amm) is mentioned: the authorities must not prevent anyone who qualifies from attending the mosque. This condition is from the Nawadir transmissions, not from Zahir al-Riwayah, and is derived from the verse implying the call is for publicity.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama‘ah): Congregation; a condition for Jumu'ah meaning a group of adult free men praying together behind an imam.
إذن عام ('idhn 'amm): General permission; the authority must allow all qualified persons to attend Jumu'ah without hindrance.
شرط انعقاد (shart in‘iqad): Condition for the validity of initiation; does not require continuance throughout the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimal number of men required besides the imam for Jumu'ah to be valid?
A) One man
B) Two men
C) Three men
D) Four men

Key Takeaway
Congregation for Jumu'ah requires at least four men (imam + 3) according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, and the condition is for initiation, not continuation.

Validity of a Non-Obligated Person Leading Friday Prayer
Ruling on imam validity for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler, sick person, or slave leading Friday prayer and explain why it is valid despite their exemption.

Core Idea
A non-obligated person can validly lead Jumu'ah because attendance makes it obligatory upon them for that day.

This passage addresses a subtle point: if someone who is not normally required to attend Friday prayer (like a traveler or slave) does attend and acts as imam, is the prayer valid? The Hanafi school says yes, contrary to Zufar. The key is that the exemption is a concession, but once they participate, Jumu'ah becomes binding on them for that day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the people in question
The text mentions a traveler (musafir), a sick person (marid), and a slave ('abd) – those for whom Jumu'ah is not originally obligatory.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that if such a person leads Friday prayer, it is valid (sahih).
3
Follow Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that since Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, they cannot lead an obligatory prayer.
Zufar's view is based on the principle that the imam must be personally obligated.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: when they attend and perform Jumu'ah, it becomes obligatory upon them for that day, so the leadership is valid.
Analogy to a traveler's fast: a traveler may fast voluntarily, and it counts as Ramadan fast.
