[٢] ينكر بعضهم ما يقوم به الحنفية في دول العجم من صلاة الظهر مع الجمعة، وقد ذكر اللكنوي العلة، وفي المسألة تفصيل في المطولات، أقتصر فيه على إيجاز ما ذكره ابن عابدين في هذا المقام إذ قال في رد المحتار (٢ : ١٤٥ ١٤٦): «الاحتياط بمعنى الخروج عن العهدة بيقين؛ لأن جواز التعدد وإن كان أرجح وأقوى دليلاً، لكن فيه شبهة قوية؛ لأن خلافه مروي عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً واختاره الطحاوي والتمرتاشي وصاحب «المختار»، وجعله العتابي الأظهر، وهو مذهب الشافعي والمشهور عن مالك وإحدى الروايتين عن أحمد كما ذكره المقدسي في رسالته «نور الشمعة في ظهر الجمعة»، بل قال السبكي من الشافعية إنه قول أكثر العلماء ولا يحفظ عن صحابي ولا تابعي تجويز تعددها اهـ. وقد علمت قول «البدائع» إنه ظاهر الرواية. وفي شرح المنية عن «جوامع الفقه» أنه أظهر الروايتين عن الإمام قال في النهر وفي الحاوي القدسي وعليه الفتوى. وفي التكملة للرازي وبه نأخذ ا هـ فهو حينئذ قول معتمد في المذهب لا قول ضعيف؛ ولذا قال في شرح المنية الأولى هو الاحتياط؛ لأن الخلاف في جواز التعدد وعدمه قوي وكون الصحيح الجواز للضرورة للفتوى لا يمنع شرعية الاحتياط للتقوى.اهـ. ولو سلم ضعفه فالخروج عن خلافه أولى فكيف مع خلاف هؤلاء الأئمة، وفي الحديث المتفق عليه فمن اتقى الشبهات استبرأ لدينه وعرضه؛ ولذا قال بعضهم فيمن يقضي صلاة لم يفته منها شيء لا يكره لأنه أخذ بالاحتياط. وذكر في القنية أنه أحسن إن كان أنه في صلاته خلاف المجتهدين ويكفينا خلاف من مر، ونقل المقدسي عن المحيط: كل موضع عمره مع
And whoever is valid as an imam in other prayers is valid in it (Friday), and it is disliked to pray Zuhr of an excused person or a prisoner in congregation in a city on its day. And whoever is valid as an imam in other prayers is valid in it: meaning if a traveler, a sick person, or a slave leads in Friday prayer, it is valid, contrary to Zufar. His proof: it is not obligatory upon them. We said: when they attend and perform Friday prayer, it becomes obligatory upon them. And it is disliked to pray Zuhr of an excused person or a prisoner in congregation in a city on its day; because Friday unites the congregations, so it is not permitted except one congregation; and for this reason, according to Abu Yusuf, Friday is not permissible in two places unless the city has two sides, then it becomes in the ruling of two cities like Baghdad, then it is permissible in two places but not three. And the meaning of public permission is that no one from whom congregation is valid is prevented from entering the place where Friday is prayed, and that is achieved by opening the doors of the mosque. If a commander enters a fortress or palace and closes its door and prays with his companions, it is not valid. Thus in al-Kafi and others. [1] His saying: we said; it is a response to Zufar's statement, and its summary: that the dropping of Friday from the mentioned ones is a concession, so when they attend and perform it, it counts as obligatory upon them like the fast of a traveler. [2] His saying: Zuhr; he qualified it because in other than it there is no harm in praying in congregation. Thus in al-Bahr. [3] His saying: in a city; he restricts it to villages and places where Friday is not obligatory. [4] His saying: because Friday...; its summary: Friday is for congregations, and performing Zuhr in congregation before Friday reduces the congregation. [5] His saying: unites; and for this reason it is not reported in the era of the Prophet and the era of the Companions to perform Friday in two or more places, as stated by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani in some of his epistles, and therefore the scholars unanimously agreed that the Sunnah is unification, and they only disagreed on permissibility or impermissibility. [6] His saying: like Baghdad; with a fatha on the ba, a silent ghain, then a dal, and after alif also a dal: the name of a known city, and I have mentioned the reason for its naming and what relates to its spelling in Mudhayyil al-Diraya. Then Muhammad said: there is no harm in praying in two or three places, whether the city has two sides or not, and that is the fatwa. [1] His saying: there is no harm...; Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: the correct view from Abu Hanifa is the permissibility of holding it in one city in two or more mosques, and we take it: because of the absolute permissibility; and because requiring unification is a clear hardship; as it necessitates lengthening the distance for most attendees, and there is no evidence for the impermissibility of multiplicity, and its absence in the prophetic era and the era of the Companions does not necessitate its impermissibility; rather, multiplicity of Eid prayer has been established in his era, as stated by Ibn Taymiyya in Minhaj al-Sunna, and Friday prayer is analogous to it. Then, although the relied-upon in the school is the permissibility of multiplicity, but when strong disagreement occurred among the imams, and disagreement also occurred on the definition of a city, they deemed it good to pray after Friday prayer without congregation four rak'ahs with the intention of the last Zuhr whose time I have reached and have not prayed, and its detail is in the commentaries of al-Hidaya, al-Munya, al-Kanz, and others. [2] Some deny what the Hanafis do in non-Arab lands of praying Zuhr with Friday, and al-Laknawi mentioned the reason, and the issue has detail in longer works. I suffice with summarizing what Ibn Abidin mentioned in this context when he said in Radd al-Muhtar (2:145-146): 'The precaution in the sense of exiting from responsibility with certainty; because the permissibility of multiplicity, although more preponderant and stronger in evidence, yet it contains a strong doubt; because its opposite is narrated from Abu Hanifa also and was chosen by al-Tahawi, al-Tamartashi, and the author of al-Mukhtar, and al-Attabi considered it the more apparent, and it is the school of al-Shafi'i and the famous view from Malik and one of the two narrations from Ahmad as mentioned by al-Maqdisi in his epistle 'Nur al-Sham'a fi Zuhr al-Jumu'a', rather al-Subki from the Shafi'is said it is the statement of most scholars and it is not preserved from any Companion or Follower to permit multiplicity... It is known that al-Bada'i' said it is the apparent narration. In Sharh al-Munya from 'Jawami' al-Fiqh' that it is the more apparent of the two narrations from the Imam, and in al-Nahr and al-Hawi al-Qudsi it is the fatwa. In al-Takmila for al-Razi: and we take it. Thus, it is then a relied-upon statement in the school, not a weak statement; therefore, in Sharh al-Munya the first precaution; because the disagreement on the permissibility and impermissibility of multiplicity is strong, and that the correct is permissibility out of necessity for fatwa does not prevent the legality of precaution for piety. Even if its weakness is conceded, then exiting from its disagreement is better, especially when there is disagreement with these imams, and in the agreed-upon hadith: 'Whoever avoids doubtful matters has protected his religion and honor.' Therefore, some said concerning one who prays a prayer that he has not missed anything of it: it is not disliked because he is taking the precaution. And it is mentioned in al-Quniya that it is best if he is in his prayer contrary to the mujtahids and the disagreement of those mentioned suffices us. Al-Maqdisi narrated from al-Muhit: every place established with
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an extensive commentary on the rulings related to Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah). It begins by stating a general principle: whoever is qualified to lead any prayer is also qualified to lead Friday prayer. This means that a traveler, a sick person, or even a slave—though not obligated to attend Friday—can validly serve as imam if they do attend. The contrary view of Zufar (a Hanafi disciple) is refuted: the concession (rukhsa) of non-obligation does not prevent validity upon performance. The passage then rules that it is disliked (makruh) for an excused person or a prisoner to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city, because the Friday prayer is meant to gather the community. If they pray Zuhr in congregation before Friday, it reduces the attendance for Jumu'ah. The text then transitions to a major intra-Hanafi dispute: Can Friday prayer be held in more than one mosque in the same city? Abu Yusuf restricts it to two places only if the city has two distinct sides (like Baghdad), while Imam Muhammad permits two or three places unconditionally. The correct view according to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is that Abu Hanifa allowed multiplicity outright, based on the absolute imperative (the word 'la' in the hadith indicating permissibility) and the hardship of forcing everyone to one location. The passage acknowledges strong disagreement among Hanafi authorities as well as other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali). To resolve the doubt, the later Hanafis adopted a precaution: after performing Friday prayer, one should pray four rak'ahs of Zuhr silently with the intention of the last Zuhr prayer whose time has entered but not yet been performed. This is not a second prayer but a cautious repetition. The commentary by Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar justifies this ihtiyat (precaution) as a way to exit the disagreement with certainty, citing the hadith about avoiding doubtful matters. The overall message assures that this practice is not bid'a but a sound legal precaution.

Key Terms
صلاة الجمعة (Salat al-Jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces Zuhr for those obligated, with conditions such as city, public permission, and khutba.
إذن عام (al-idhn al-'amm): Public permission: the mosque must be open to all who are valid for congregation, achieved by opening its doors; if a ruler prays in a closed fortress, Jumu'ah is not valid.
تعدد الجمعة (ta'addud al-Jumu'ah): Holding Friday prayer in more than one mosque in the same city; a disputed issue within the Hanafi school and between schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Valid because attendance makes Jumu'ah obligatory upon them that day.
C) Disliked (makruh) because a slave should not lead free men.
D) Valid only if the imam is a free man.

Key Takeaway
A non-obligated person can validly lead Jumu'ah because attendance makes it obligatory upon them for that day.

Dispute on Multiple Friday Prayers (Ta'addud al-Jumu'ah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple Friday prayers and the precaution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on multiple Friday prayers in one city and evaluate the precautionary practice of praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits multiple Jumu'ah prayers in one city, but strong disagreement led to the precaution of praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah to exit the dispute.

The issue of whether Friday prayer can be held in more than one mosque in the same city has been debated within the Hanafi school and with other schools. This passage presents the views of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa, and then discusses the later precaution of praying four rak'ahs of Zuhr after Jumu'ah to ensure certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on Zuhr congregation on Friday
The text says it is disliked (makruh) for an excused person or prisoner to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city, because Jumu'ah unifies the community.
This sets the context that Jumu'ah is meant to gather everyone.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf allows only one Jumu'ah per city, except if the city has two distinct sides (like Baghdad), then two are allowed, but not three.
His condition: a large city with two separate sections.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad sees no harm in two or three places, unconditionally, and this is the fatwa.
This is more permissive.
4
State the correct view from Abu Hanifa
According to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, the correct view of Abu Hanifa is permissibility in two or more mosques, based on the absence of prohibition and the hardship of requiring unity.
Evidence: absolute imperative, hardship, analogy to Eid prayer.
5
Explain the precaution (ihtiyat)
Due to strong disagreement, later scholars recommended praying four rak'ahs of Zuhr after Jumu'ah silently, with the intention of the last Zuhr prayer, to exit the dispute with certainty.
This is not a separate obligation but a precaution to remove doubt.

ومَن صَلَحَ إماماً في غيرها صَلَحَ فيها ، وكُرِه ظهر معذور أو مسجون بجماعة في مصر يومها. ومَن صَلَحَ إماماً في غيرها صَلَحَ فيها : أي إن أم المسافر، أو المريض، أو العبد في الجمعة صحت خلافا لزفر، له : أنها ليست بواجبة عليهم، قلنا : إذا حضروا وأدوا صلاة الجمعة صارت فرضاً عليهم. وكُرِه ظهر معذور أو مسجون بجماعة في مصر يومها؛ لأن الجمعة جامعة الجماعات، فلا يجوز إلا جماعة واحدة؛ ولهذا لا تجوز الجمعة عند أبي يوسف بموضعين إلا إذا كان المصر له جانبان، فيصير في حكم مصرين كبغداد، فيجوز حينئذ في موضعين دون الثلاثة. ومعنى الإذن العام أن لا يمنع أحداً ممن تصح منه الجماعة عن دخول الموضع الذي تُصلى فيه الجمعة، وهو يحصل بفتح أبواب الجامع، فلو دخل أمير حصناً أو قصراً وأغلق بابه وصلّى بأصحابه لم تنعقد. كذا في «الكافي» وغيره. [٦] قوله : كبغداد؛ بفتح الباء الموحدة، وغين معجمة ساكنة، بعدها دال مهملة، وبعد الألف أيضاً دال مهملة : اسم بلدة معروفة، وقد ذكرت وجه تسميته وما يتعلق بضبطه في «مذيلة الدراية». ثم قال محمد : لا بأس بأن يصلي في موضعين، أو ثلاثة سواء كان للمصر جانبان، أو لم يكن، وبه يفتى. [١] قوله : لا بأس ... الخ؛ قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : إن الصحيح من مذهب أبي حنيفة جواز إقامتها في مصر واحد في مسجدين وأكثر، وبه نأخذ : لإطلاق لا؛ ولأن في إلزام التوحد حرجاً بيناً؛ لاستدعائه تطويل السافة على أكثر الحاضرين، ولم يوجد دليل على عدم جواز التعدد، وعدمه في العهد النبوي وعهد الصحابة لا يستلزم عدم جوازه، بل قد ثبت تعدد صلاة العيد في عهد عليه، كما صرح به ابن تيمية في منهاج السنة وصلاة الجمعة نظيرها، ثم المعتبر في المذهب وإن كان جواز التعدد، لكن لما وقع الاختلاف القوي بين الأئمة، ووقع الخلاف في تعريف المصر أيضاً استحسنوا أن يصلوا بعد صلاة الجمعة بغير جماعة أربع ركعات بنية آخر ظهر أدركت وقته ولم أصله بعد، وتفصيله في شروح «الهداية»، و«المنية»، و«الكنز»، وغيرها. [٢] ينكر بعضهم ما يقوم به الحنفية في دول العجم من صلاة الظهر مع الجمعة، وقد ذكر اللكنوي العلة، وفي المسألة تفصيل في المطولات، أقتصر فيه على إيجاز ما ذكره ابن عابدين في هذا المقام إذ قال في رد المحتار (٢ : ١٤٥ ١٤٦): «الاحتياط بمعنى الخروج عن العهدة بيقين؛ لأن جواز التعدد وإن كان أرجح وأقوى دليلاً، لكن فيه شبهة قوية؛ لأن خلافه مروي عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً واختاره الطحاوي والتمرتاشي وصاحب «المختار»، وجعله العتابي الأظهر، وهو مذهب الشافعي والمشهور عن مالك وإحدى الروايتين عن أحمد كما ذكره المقدسي في رسالته «نور الشمعة في ظهر الجمعة»، بل قال السبكي من الشافعية إنه قول أكثر العلماء ولا يحفظ عن صحابي ولا تابعي تجويز تعددها اهـ. وقد علمت قول «البدائع» إنه ظاهر الرواية. وفي شرح المنية عن «جوامع الفقه» أنه أظهر الروايتين عن الإمام قال في النهر وفي الحاوي القدسي وعليه الفتوى. وفي التكملة للرازي وبه نأخذ ا هـ فهو حينئذ قول معتمد في المذهب لا قول ضعيف؛ ولذا قال في شرح المنية الأولى هو الاحتياط؛ لأن الخلاف في جواز التعدد وعدمه قوي وكون الصحيح الجواز للضرورة للفتوى لا يمنع شرعية الاحتياط للتقوى.اهـ. ولو سلم ضعفه فالخروج عن خلافه أولى فكيف مع خلاف هؤلاء الأئمة، وفي الحديث المتفق عليه فمن اتقى الشبهات استبرأ لدينه وعرضه؛ ولذا قال بعضهم فيمن يقضي صلاة لم يفته منها شيء لا يكره لأنه أخذ بالاحتياط. وذكر في القنية أنه أحسن إن كان أنه في صلاته خلاف المجتهدين ويكفينا خلاف من مر، ونقل المقدسي عن المحيط: كل موضع عمره مع
And whoever is valid as an imam in other prayers is valid in it (Friday), and it is disliked to pray Zuhr of an excused person or a prisoner in congregation in a city on its day. And whoever is valid as an imam in other prayers is valid in it: meaning if a traveler, a sick person, or a slave leads in Friday prayer, it is valid, contrary to Zufar. His proof: it is not obligatory upon them. We said: when they attend and perform Friday prayer, it becomes obligatory upon them. And it is disliked to pray Zuhr of an excused person or a prisoner in congregation in a city on its day; because Friday unites the congregations, so it is not permitted except one congregation; and for this reason, according to Abu Yusuf, Friday is not permissible in two places unless the city has two sides, then it becomes in the ruling of two cities like Baghdad, then it is permissible in two places but not three. And the meaning of public permission is that no one from whom congregation is valid is prevented from entering the place where Friday is prayed, and that is achieved by opening the doors of the mosque. If a commander enters a fortress or palace and closes its door and prays with his companions, it is not valid. Thus in al-Kafi and others. [1] His saying: we said; it is a response to Zufar's statement, and its summary: that the dropping of Friday from the mentioned ones is a concession, so when they attend and perform it, it counts as obligatory upon them like the fast of a traveler. [2] His saying: Zuhr; he qualified it because in other than it there is no harm in praying in congregation. Thus in al-Bahr. [3] His saying: in a city; he restricts it to villages and places where Friday is not obligatory. [4] His saying: because Friday...; its summary: Friday is for congregations, and performing Zuhr in congregation before Friday reduces the congregation. [5] His saying: unites; and for this reason it is not reported in the era of the Prophet and the era of the Companions to perform Friday in two or more places, as stated by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani in some of his epistles, and therefore the scholars unanimously agreed that the Sunnah is unification, and they only disagreed on permissibility or impermissibility. [6] His saying: like Baghdad; with a fatha on the ba, a silent ghain, then a dal, and after alif also a dal: the name of a known city, and I have mentioned the reason for its naming and what relates to its spelling in Mudhayyil al-Diraya. Then Muhammad said: there is no harm in praying in two or three places, whether the city has two sides or not, and that is the fatwa. [1] His saying: there is no harm...; Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: the correct view from Abu Hanifa is the permissibility of holding it in one city in two or more mosques, and we take it: because of the absolute permissibility; and because requiring unification is a clear hardship; as it necessitates lengthening the distance for most attendees, and there is no evidence for the impermissibility of multiplicity, and its absence in the prophetic era and the era of the Companions does not necessitate its impermissibility; rather, multiplicity of Eid prayer has been established in his era, as stated by Ibn Taymiyya in Minhaj al-Sunna, and Friday prayer is analogous to it. Then, although the relied-upon in the school is the permissibility of multiplicity, but when strong disagreement occurred among the imams, and disagreement also occurred on the definition of a city, they deemed it good to pray after Friday prayer without congregation four rak'ahs with the intention of the last Zuhr whose time I have reached and have not prayed, and its detail is in the commentaries of al-Hidaya, al-Munya, al-Kanz, and others. [2] Some deny what the Hanafis do in non-Arab lands of praying Zuhr with Friday, and al-Laknawi mentioned the reason, and the issue has detail in longer works. I suffice with summarizing what Ibn Abidin mentioned in this context when he said in Radd al-Muhtar (2:145-146): 'The precaution in the sense of exiting from responsibility with certainty; because the permissibility of multiplicity, although more preponderant and stronger in evidence, yet it contains a strong doubt; because its opposite is narrated from Abu Hanifa also and was chosen by al-Tahawi, al-Tamartashi, and the author of al-Mukhtar, and al-Attabi considered it the more apparent, and it is the school of al-Shafi'i and the famous view from Malik and one of the two narrations from Ahmad as mentioned by al-Maqdisi in his epistle 'Nur al-Sham'a fi Zuhr al-Jumu'a', rather al-Subki from the Shafi'is said it is the statement of most scholars and it is not preserved from any Companion or Follower to permit multiplicity... It is known that al-Bada'i' said it is the apparent narration. In Sharh al-Munya from 'Jawami' al-Fiqh' that it is the more apparent of the two narrations from the Imam, and in al-Nahr and al-Hawi al-Qudsi it is the fatwa. In al-Takmila for al-Razi: and we take it. Thus, it is then a relied-upon statement in the school, not a weak statement; therefore, in Sharh al-Munya the first precaution; because the disagreement on the permissibility and impermissibility of multiplicity is strong, and that the correct is permissibility out of necessity for fatwa does not prevent the legality of precaution for piety. Even if its weakness is conceded, then exiting from its disagreement is better, especially when there is disagreement with these imams, and in the agreed-upon hadith: 'Whoever avoids doubtful matters has protected his religion and honor.' Therefore, some said concerning one who prays a prayer that he has not missed anything of it: it is not disliked because he is taking the precaution. And it is mentioned in al-Quniya that it is best if he is in his prayer contrary to the mujtahids and the disagreement of those mentioned suffices us. Al-Maqdisi narrated from al-Muhit: every place established with
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an extensive commentary on the rulings related to Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah). It begins by stating a general principle: whoever is qualified to lead any prayer is also qualified to lead Friday prayer. This means that a traveler, a sick person, or even a slave—though not obligated to attend Friday—can validly serve as imam if they do attend. The contrary view of Zufar (a Hanafi disciple) is refuted: the concession (rukhsa) of non-obligation does not prevent validity upon performance. The passage then rules that it is disliked (makruh) for an excused person or a prisoner to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city, because the Friday prayer is meant to gather the community. If they pray Zuhr in congregation before Friday, it reduces the attendance for Jumu'ah. The text then transitions to a major intra-Hanafi dispute: Can Friday prayer be held in more than one mosque in the same city? Abu Yusuf restricts it to two places only if the city has two distinct sides (like Baghdad), while Imam Muhammad permits two or three places unconditionally. The correct view according to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is that Abu Hanifa allowed multiplicity outright, based on the absolute imperative (the word 'la' in the hadith indicating permissibility) and the hardship of forcing everyone to one location. The passage acknowledges strong disagreement among Hanafi authorities as well as other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali). To resolve the doubt, the later Hanafis adopted a precaution: after performing Friday prayer, one should pray four rak'ahs of Zuhr silently with the intention of the last Zuhr prayer whose time has entered but not yet been performed. This is not a second prayer but a cautious repetition. The commentary by Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar justifies this ihtiyat (precaution) as a way to exit the disagreement with certainty, citing the hadith about avoiding doubtful matters. The overall message assures that this practice is not bid'a but a sound legal precaution.

Key Terms
صلاة الجمعة (Salat al-Jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces Zuhr for those obligated, with conditions such as city, public permission, and khutba.
إذن عام (al-idhn al-'amm): Public permission: the mosque must be open to all who are valid for congregation, achieved by opening its doors; if a ruler prays in a closed fortress, Jumu'ah is not valid.
تعدد الجمعة (ta'addud al-Jumu'ah): Holding Friday prayer in more than one mosque in the same city; a disputed issue within the Hanafi school and between schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on holding Friday prayer in two different mosques in the same city?
A) It is not permissible under any circumstances.
B) It is permissible only if the city has two distinct sides like Baghdad.
C) It is permissible in two or more mosques, and this is the fatwa.
D) It is permissible but only if the mosques are far apart.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits multiple Friday prayers in one city to avoid hardship, and the precaution of praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah exits the strong disagreement.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Multiple Jumu'ah Prayers and Precautionary Zuhr
Discusses the permissibility of multiple Jumu'ah and the recommended precaution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on multiple Jumu'ah prayers in a single city and evaluate the rationale for the precautionary Zuhr prayer.

Core Idea
Multiple Jumu'ah is permitted in the Hanafi school, but precautionary Zuhr is recommended due to strong ikhtilaf.

This lesson examines a nuanced issue in Hanafi fiqh: the permissibility of holding multiple Jumu'ah prayers in a single city. While the madhhab's relied-upon position allows multiplicity to avoid hardship, a significant internal and cross-madhhab disagreement led later scholars to recommend a precautionary practice: praying four rak'at of Zuhr after Jumu'ah. Understanding why this precaution is recommended, not required, reveals the Hanafi method of balancing strong evidence with piety.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is the main legal question? Is it permissible to hold multiple Jumu'ah prayers in one city? Determine the Hanafi position and the opposing views.
The dispute involves both inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof for permissibility
Analyze the Hanafi arguments: general permission (itlaq), hardship in requiring uniformity, analogy with Eid prayer, and absence of explicit prohibition. Identify the type of proof (dalil aqli).
The analogy with Eid is a key qiyas.
3
Analyze the opposing arguments
Consider the Shafi'i/Maliki/early Hanafi opposition: the practice of the Prophet and Companions was a single Jumu'ah, and the hadith implies unity. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: practical consequence in rulings.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; both sides have evidence.
4
Understand the need for precaution (ihtiyat)
Why did later Hanafi scholars recommend praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah? Because despite the strong Hanafi proof, there is a conflicting narration from Abu Hanifa and disagreement on the definition of a city, creating a shubha. The hadith on avoiding shubuhat motivates the precaution.
The precaution is mustahabb, not wajib.
5
Apply the lesson to practice
In a city with multiple Jumu'ah prayers, what should a Hanafi do? Follow the mufta bihi (permissibility) and optionally pray Zuhr for taqwa. Recognize that this precaution is not a refutation of the madhhab but an extra measure for those who wish to avoid ikhtilaf.
The text warns against doing this openly if it causes public confusion.

He said: 'There is no harm... etc.'; Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: The correct position of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is the permissibility of holding it (Jumu'ah) in one city in two or more mosques, and we adopt it due to the absolute nature of the permission, and because requiring uniformity would cause evident hardship as it would require lengthening the distance for the majority of attendees, and there is no evidence for the impermissibility of multiplicity, and its absence in the prophetic era and the era of the Companions does not necessitate its impermissibility; indeed, the multiplicity of Eid prayer was established in his era, as Ibn Taymiyya stated in Minhaj al-Sunna, and Jumu'ah prayer is analogous. Then, although the relied-upon position in the madhhab is permissibility, because a strong ikhtilaf occurred among the imams and also regarding the definition of a city, they deemed it good to pray after Jumu'ah without congregation four rak'at with the intention of the last Zuhr whose time has arrived and I have not yet prayed it. Its detail is in the commentaries of al-Hidaya, al-Munya, al-Kanz, and others. ... (continued with the lengthy quote from Ibn 'Abidin and others about precaution and the hadith on shubuhat).
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya deals with the controversial issue of holding multiple Jumu'ah prayers in a single city. The author begins by citing al-Sarakhsi, who affirms that the correct Hanafi position is permissibility, based on the general permission for Jumu'ah and the avoidance of hardship. The absence of multiple Jumu'ah in the Prophet's time does not prove prohibition, as it may be due to lack of need; analogy with Eid prayer, which was performed in multiple locations, supports this. However, the author notes that despite this being the madhhab's position, a strong ikhtilaf exists among the imams, including a narration from Abu Hanifa himself that suggests prohibition, adopted by al-Tahawi, al-Timirtashi, and others. This ikhtilaf, along with disagreement on the definition of a city (misr), led later scholars to recommend a precaution: after performing Jumu'ah, one should pray four rak'at of Zuhr individually, intending to make up the last Zuhr in case the Jumu'ah was invalid. This is not for fatwa but for taqwa. The passage cites Ibn 'Abidin's argument that the precaution is to exit the obligation with certainty, as the permissibility of multiplicity, though stronger in evidence, has a strong shubha. The hadith 'Whoever avoids shubuhat has protected his religion and honor' is invoked. The author concludes by warning that if this practice leads to public corruption, it should not be done openly. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing strong evidence (rajih) with precaution (ihtiyat) in cases of ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary practice; in this context, praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah to ensure fulfillment of the obligation in case Jumu'ah is invalid.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity in evidence; here, the shubha is that the permissibility of multiple Jumu'ah is not absolutely certain due to conflicting narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Hanafi scholars recommend praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah?
A) Because Jumu'ah is invalid without the imam's permission
B) Due to a strong ikhtilaf on the permissibility of multiple Jumu'ah and the definition of a city
C) Because the Prophet always prayed Zuhr after Jumu'ah
D) To make up for missed witr prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits multiple Jumu'ah but recommends precautionary Zuhr to avoid ikhtilaf, balancing strong evidence with piety.

Salah — Prayer

Invalidation of Zuhr by Walking to Jumu'ah
Explains the invalidation of Zuhr before Jumu'ah and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding invalidation, and determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Walking to Jumu'ah after praying Zuhr invalidates it according to Abu Hanifa, because the act takes on the ruling of Jumu'ah as a precaution.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a person without a valid excuse prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah while in the city, then walks to the mosque while the imam is still engaged in Jumu'ah. The Hanafi school has an internal difference on whether this act invalidates the earlier Zuhr. Understanding this ruling is crucial for proper Friday observance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The person prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, then walks to Jumu'ah while the imam is still in prayer. The matn states that this invalidates the Zuhr regardless of whether he catches up.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that it invalidates; the Sahibayn hold that only joining the imam invalidates.
This difference is within the same school.
3
Analyze the proof for each view
Abu Hanifa: walking (sa'y) is a characteristic of Jumu'ah, so it takes its ruling as a precaution. Sahibayn: walking is less than Zuhr and does not invalidate a completed act; only joining changes intention.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as supported by al-Hidaya and adopted in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظهر من لا عُدْرَ له فيه قبلها ثم سعيه إليها، والإمام فيها يبطله أدركها أو لا ومدركها في التشهد ، أو في سجود السهو يتمها الأولى.
[۱]

[٤]
( ومدركها في التشهد ، أو في سجود السهو يتمها
[1 قوله : علم ؛ فإنّه لَمَّا كانَ ظهرُ المعذور مع عجزه عن حضور الجمعة بالجماعة مكروهاً يوم الجمعة، تكون ظهـر غـيـر المعذور مكروها بالضرورة، وأشار به إلى أنَّ التقييد بالمعذور في المتن ليس باحترازي، بل لبيان حكم ما يحتاج إلى ذكره وترك ما هو أجلى.
(٢)

[٤] قوله : إلا أن يقتدي ؛ أي بالإمام، فإنَّ السَّعي دون الظهر، فلا ينقض بعد تمامه، والجمعة فوقه فتنقضه ، وله أنَّ السَّعي إلى الجمعة من خصائص الجمعة، فيَنْزِلُ منزلتها احتياطاً، بخلاف ما إذا سعى بعد فراغ الإمام من الجمعة ؛ لأنه ليس بسعي إليها. كذا في «الهداية» (۳). [0]قوله : ومدركها...الخ ؛ يعني من أدرك مع الإمام شيئاً من صلاة الجمعة
And the Zuhr of one who has no excuse in it (the city) before it (Jumu'ah) then his going to it while the imam is in it invalidates it, whether he catches up or not. And one who catches up in the tashahhud or in sajdat al-sahw completes it as Jumu'ah. [Commentary:] It is understood from what was mentioned about the ruling of the excused that the Zuhr of the non-excused is disliked. His statement: 'in it' means in the city. Then his going to it while the imam is in it invalidates it, whether he catches up or not. This is according to Abu Hanifa. As for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it does not invalidate his Zuhr unless he joins (the imam). And one who catches up in the tashahhud or in sajdat al-sahw completes it (as Jumu'ah). [Commentary on 'he said: knew'] Because the Zuhr of the excused, due to his inability to attend Jumu'ah with the congregation, is disliked on Friday, so the Zuhr of the non-excused is necessarily disliked. This indicates that the restriction to the excused in the text is not exclusive but to clarify the ruling that needed mention. [Commentary on 'dislike of Zuhr'] Means with congregation, and likewise without it, as in al-Hidaya. [Commentary on 'Zuhr...'] Means if the non-excused person, while in the city, prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, then walks to it while the imam is not yet finished, his Zuhr is invalidated whether he catches the imam or not. [Commentary on 'unless he joins'] Means the imam, because walking (to Jumu'ah) is less than Zuhr, so it does not invalidate Zuhr after completion, but Jumu'ah is above it, so it invalidates it. And because walking to Jumu'ah is a characteristic of Jumu'ah, so it takes its place as a precaution, unlike if he walks after the imam finishes Jumu'ah, because that is not walking to it. As in al-Hidaya. [Commentary on 'one who catches up'] Means one who catches up with the imam during any part of Jumu'ah prayer.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains two intertwined rulings from the matn of al-Wiqaya. First, a person who has no excuse (i.e., not a traveler or sick) and is within the city prays Zuhr before going to Jumu'ah, then walks to Jumu'ah while the imam is still engaged in the prayer: according to Abu Hanifa, his Zuhr is invalidated (batil) whether he catches any part of Jumu'ah or not. The reasoning is that walking to Jumu'ah is a specific characteristic of Jumu'ah, so it takes the ruling of Jumu'ah by way of precaution, and since Jumu'ah is superior, it overrides the invalid Zuhr. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), his Zuhr is only invalidated if he actually joins the imam in Jumu'ah (because then his intention shifts from Zuhr to Jumu'ah, but if he doesn't join, his Zuhr stands). The commentary notes that the matn's mention of 'excused' (ma'dhur) is not exclusive; it implies that the Zuhr of a non-excused person is even more clearly disliked (makruh). Second, if a person catches any part of Jumu'ah with the imam, such as the tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw, he completes his prayer as Jumu'ah (not Zuhr). This applies to the latecomer who joins the congregation after the ruku' of the second rak'ah. The passage also clarifies that if the person walks to Jumu'ah after the imam has already finished, it does not invalidate his Zuhr because it is no longer 'going to Jumu'ah'.

Key Terms
السعي إلى الجمعة (al-sa'y ila al-jumu'a): Walking or going to attend Jumu'ah prayer; in this context, it refers to the act of heading to the mosque after having prayed Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what invalidates the Zuhr prayer on Friday?
A) Only joining Jumu'ah
B) Walking to Jumu'ah while the imam is in prayer
C) Not attending Jumu'ah
D) Praying Zuhr after Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is invalidated if one then walks to Jumu'ah while the imam is still in prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Catching Jumu'ah in the Tashahhud or Sajdat al-Sahw
Explains that catching any part of Jumu'ah makes it valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that catching any part of Jumu'ah, even the tashahhud, suffices to complete it as Jumu'ah, and apply this to situations including sajdat al-sahw.

Core Idea
If you catch even the tashahhud of Jumu'ah with the imam, your prayer is a valid Jumu'ah.

One of the distinctive features of the Hanafi school is that a latecomer to Jumu'ah can catch a valid Jumu'ah by joining the imam in any part of the prayer, even the final tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw. This lesson clarifies that ruling and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The latecomer (mudrik) catches the imam during any part of Jumu'ah, such as tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw. He completes his prayer as Jumu'ah.
2
Understand the basis
The ruling is based on the principle that catching any part of the congregational prayer makes one part of the congregation.
3
Note the minimal requirement
Even catching the final tashahhud suffices. This is different from other schools.
Shafi'is require at least one rak'ah.
4
Apply the ruling
The latecomer then continues his prayer after the imam's salam, completing his Jumu'ah with two rak'ahs (if he caught the tashahhud, he will pray two rak'ahs after).
He follows the imam for what he catches, then completes the rest.

Zuhr Before Friday: Effect of Subsequent Attendance
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidation of Zuhr by subsequent Friday attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of Zuhr prayed before Friday and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) depending on whether the person joins the imam.

Core Idea
Proceeding to Friday prayer after praying Zuhr invalidates that Zuhr (Abu Hanifa) unless you join the imam (Sahibayn).

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person who prays Zuhr before Friday and then heads to the mosque. The ruling hinges on whether the act of proceeding (sa'y) alone nullifies the Zuhr or only joining the congregation. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes Friday prayer over Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
Read the text to identify the case: a non-excused person prays Zuhr alone before Friday, then proceeds to the mosque while the imam is still in the Friday prayer. Note Abu Hanifa's ruling (Zuhr invalidated) and the Sahibayn's ruling (not invalidated unless he joins the imam).
2
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Abu Hanifa argues that sa'y (proceeding) is a special characteristic of Friday that takes precedence over Zuhr out of caution. The Sahibayn argue that proceeding alone is not an act of worship that nullifies a completed prayer; only actual participation (iqtida') does.
The text explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning in the commentary.
3
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Determine what each ruling means for the person: Under Abu Hanifa, he must pray Friday with the imam and his Zuhr is void. Under the Sahibayn, his Zuhr remains valid as long as he does not join the imam.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view. This is the position students should apply in fatwa.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah confirms this tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظهر من لا عُدْرَ له فيه قبلها ثم سعيه إليها، والإمام فيها يبطله أدركها أو لا (وما ذَكَرَ حُكْمَ المعذور ، عُلِمَ منه كراهة ظُهْرِ غير المعذور) بالطريق (وظُهْرُ مَن لا عُدْرَ له فيه قبلها ، قوله : فيه ، أي في المصر، (ثم سعيه إليها، والإمام فيها يبطله أدركها أو لا) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له، وأما عندهما فلا يبطل ظهرُهُ إلا أن يقتدي [1] قوله : علم؛ فإنّه لَمَّا كانَ ظهرُ المعذور مع عجزه عن حضور الجمعة بالجماعة مكروهاً يوم الجمعة، تكون ظهر غير المعذور مكروها بالضرورة، وأشار به إلى أنَّ التقييد بالمعذور في المتن ليس باحترازي، بل لبيان حكم ما يحتاج إلى ذكره وترك ما هو أجلى. [2] قوله : كراهة ظهر؛ أي بالجماعة، وكذا بدونها. كما في «الهداية». [3] قوله : ظهر ... الخ؛ يعني إذا صلّى غير المعذور وهو في المصر صلاة الظهر قبل الجمعة، ثم مشى إليها حال كون الإمام فيها غير فارغ عنها، بطل ظهره سواء أدركَ الإمام أم لم يدرك. [4] قوله : إلا أن يقتدي؛ أي بالإمام، فإنَّ السَّعي دون الظهر، فلا ينقض بعد تمامه، والجمعة فوقه فتنقضه، وله أنَّ السَّعي إلى الجمعة من خصائص الجمعة، فيَنْزِلُ منزلتها احتياطاً، بخلاف ما إذا سعى بعد فراغ الإمام من الجمعة؛ لأنه ليس بسعي إليها. كذا في «الهداية».
And the Zuhr of one who has no excuse before it (Friday prayer) then his proceeding to it, and the imam being in it invalidates it, whether he catches the imam or not. (And what he mentioned of the ruling of the excused person, it is understood from it the dislike of the Zuhr of the non-excused) by way of (And the Zuhr of one who has no excuse before it, his saying: 'therein' meaning in the town, (then his proceeding to it, and the imam being in it invalidates it, whether he catches the imam or not), this according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) his Zuhr is not invalidated unless he follows [the imam]. [1] His saying: 'understood'; because when the Zuhr of the excused person due to his inability to attend Friday congregation is disliked on Friday, then the Zuhr of the non-excused is necessarily disliked, and he indicated by this that the restriction to the excused in the text is not exclusive, but rather to clarify the ruling that needs mentioning and to leave what is more obvious. [2] His saying: 'dislike of Zuhr' meaning in congregation, and likewise without it, as in al-Hidayah. [3] His saying: 'Zuhr...etc.' meaning if a non-excused person prays Zuhr prayer in the town before Friday, then goes to it (the mosque) while the imam is in it and has not finished, his Zuhr is invalidated, whether he catches the imam or not. [4] His saying: 'unless he follows' meaning the imam, because proceeding (to the mosque) is not like Zuhr, so it does not break it after its completion, and Friday is above it so it breaks it, and he has the argument that proceeding to Friday is a special characteristic of Friday, so it takes its place out of caution, unlike the case when he proceeds after the imam has finished Friday prayer, because that is not proceeding to it. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on a person who has no valid excuse (such as illness or travel) and prays the Zuhr prayer alone at home or elsewhere before the Friday prayer, and then proceeds to the mosque while the imam is still engaged in the Friday prayer. The author explains that the text's mention of the excused person is not exclusive; rather, it is used to highlight the ruling for the non-excused by way of primary implication (al-tariq al-awla). If the non-excused person's Zuhr is disliked, then the non-excused's is even more disliked. The commentator notes that this dislike applies whether the Zuhr is prayed in congregation or individually. The core ruling: according to Abu Hanifa, the Zuhr prayer of such a person is invalidated by his subsequent attendance at the Friday prayer, regardless of whether he catches the imam or not. The reason given is that the act of proceeding to the Friday prayer is a distinctive feature of Friday that carries the same weight as the Friday prayer itself, thus it overrides the previous Zuhr out of caution. However, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), the Zuhr is not invalidated unless the person actually joins the imam (i.e., becomes a follower). Their view is that proceeding alone does not nullify the Zuhr; only actual participation in the Friday prayer does. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, as stated in al-Hidayah. The commentator also clarifies that if the person proceeds after the imam has finished the Friday prayer, his Zuhr remains valid, because that proceeding is not considered 'proceeding to Friday' since the prayer is over.

Key Terms
عذر (‘udhr): A valid excuse that exempts one from the obligation of Friday prayer, such as illness or travel.
سعي (sa‘y): Proceeding or walking to the mosque for Friday prayer after the call to prayer.
إقتداء (iqtidā’): Following the imam in prayer by joining the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a non-excused person prays Zuhr alone before Friday and then proceeds to the mosque while the imam is still in the Friday prayer, what happens to his Zuhr?
A) It remains valid and he prays Friday with the imam.
B) It is invalidated and he must pray Friday with the imam.
C) It is invalidated only if he joins the imam.
D) It remains valid and he prays Zuhr again after Friday.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that a non-excused person's Zuhr is invalidated if they proceed to Friday prayer while the imam is still in it, regardless of joining.

Catching the Imam in Tashahhud or Sajdat al-Sahw
Ruling with proof for the mudrik in tashahhud/sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer who catches the imam in tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw in Friday prayer and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Catching the imam in tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw counts – no Zuhr needed.

What happens if you join the Friday prayer when the imam is already sitting for tashahhud or performing the prostrations for forgetfulness? This lesson clarifies that, according to the Hanafi school, such a person completes his prayer as a follower and does not need to pray Zuhr separately. The key evidence is the well-known hadith instructing us to pray what we catch with the imam and complete what we miss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The mudrik (latecomer) joins the imam during the final tashahhud or during sajdat al-sahw. The question is whether this counts as attending the Friday prayer and what he must do afterward.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The text cites the hadith: 'Whatever you catch, pray, and whatever you miss, complete.' This is a general command that applies to any part of the prayer caught with the imam.
The hadith is narrated by the authors of the six major hadith collections.
3
Derive the ruling
Since the latecomer caught something of the prayer (even just the tashahhud), he is considered a follower (muqtadi). After the imam says salam, he stands up and completes the remaining rak'ahs on his own. He does NOT pray Zuhr because his Friday prayer is valid.
This is the established Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah).
4
Address the precautionary aside
The commentary mentions a precautionary measure: if there is doubt about residency, some scholars recommend praying four rak'ahs of Zuhr after Jumu'ah to be safe, but this is only for advanced scholars and done discreetly. The main ruling remains clear.
Do not confuse this exceptional opinion with the standard ruling.

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a person who joins the Friday prayer after the imam has already completed the greater part of the prayer, specifically catching him in the tashahhud (final sitting) or in the sajdat al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness). The core ruling is that such a person completes his prayer as a follower; he does not need to pray Zuhr separately. The hadith 'Whatever you catch, pray, and whatever you miss, complete' is cited as the primary evidence. The commentary includes a lengthy discussion about a precautionary measure: if there is doubt about whether the person is a resident (making Friday obligatory) or a traveler (making Zuhr obligatory), some scholars recommend praying four rak'ahs after Friday with the intention of Zuhr to ensure the obligation is fulfilled. However, the commentator notes that this should only be done privately to avoid confusion among the common people, and only for the elite scholars. The main ruling remains that one who catches the imam in tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw should count that as his prayer and does not pray Zuhr.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): One who catches the imam in any part of the prayer, even if only the tashahhud.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting during which one recites the tashahhud (attestation of faith).

Obligation to Stop Selling and Proceed at the First Adhan for Friday
Ruling with proof and response to objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that it is wajib to leave selling and proceed to the mosque upon hearing the first adhan for Friday prayer, and explain the Quranic dalil and the response to the historical objection.

Core Idea
The Quranic command for Friday prayer applies to every adhan – even the first one added later by ‘Uthman.

This passage addresses a practical question: when exactly does the obligation to stop work and go to the mosque for Jumu'ah begin? The commentator explains that the first adhan, added by Caliph ‘Uthman due to the increase in population, now triggers the same duty as the original adhan. We will see how the Quranic verse is interpreted to cover both calls, and how a potential objection based on historical practice is resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is leaving selling and other worldly occupations, and proceeding to the mosque for Friday prayer. The ruling is wajib (obligatory).
The act is not a pillar of prayer itself but a precondition for attending.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites Quranic verse 9 of Surah al-Jumu'ah as the primary evidence. The verse contains two imperatives: 'fas‘aw' (proceed) and 'dharu' (leave).
The verse is decisive in transmission (qat‘i al-thubut) but interpretive (zanni al-dalala) regarding the scope of 'nudiyya' (call).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'nūdiya' (call) is general in Arabic. According to Hanafi usul, a general command (amr) indicates obligation unless specified otherwise. The verse orders leaving business and proceeding when a call is made, so it applies to any call for Friday prayer.
The historical context: at revelation, only one adhan existed, but the general wording allows inclusion of later adhans.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The objector argues that the first adhan did not exist at the time of revelation, so the verse only applies to the second adhan. The commentator responds that the verse does not specify which adhan; it simply says 'when the call is made'. When the first adhan was introduced, it falls under the same general command.
This is a clear application of the usul principle that a general text (amm) remains general until a specific exception (takhsis) is proven.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if one follows the objection, the obligation would only begin at the second adhan. According to the Hanafi position, it begins at the first adhan, giving a longer period to prepare and proceed.
This ruling reflects the Hanafi school's reliance on the general application of Quranic commands.

Source Text

And when the first call to prayer is made, they should leave selling and proceed. [1] His saying: 'And when the first adhan...etc.'; its summary: it is obligatory to walk to the Friday prayer and leave selling and other worldly occupations that hinder proceeding from the first adhan for Friday, due to His saying: 'When the call to prayer is made on Friday, then proceed to the remembrance of Allah and leave off business' (al-Jumu‘ah 9). If you say: it is established in the authentic books and others that there was only one adhan in the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and ‘Umar, which is the second adhan that is called at the beginning of the sermon. Then, in the time of ‘Uthman, when the people increased, he added the first adhan, and the ummah adopted it without objection. So the call mentioned in the verse at the time of revelation was only the second, so the obligation to proceed and leave selling applies at that time, not before it. I say: there is no mention in the Quran of the first or second adhan; rather, it says: 'When the call to prayer is made on Friday', and that applied at that time only to the second adhan. So when the first adhan was added, it enters the verse, and its ruling necessarily applies to it.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation to cease transactions and proceed to the mosque when the first adhan for Friday prayer is called. The commentator explains that the Quranic verse (al-Jumu‘ah 9) commands believers to do so. A possible objection is raised: in the time of the Prophet and the first two caliphs, there was only one adhan (the one just before the sermon). The first adhan was added by ‘Uthman due to the increase in population. If the verse only referred to that single adhan, then the obligation to leave selling and proceed should apply only at the time of that adhan (the second). The commentator responds that the verse does not specify the number of adhans; it simply says 'when the call to prayer is made'. The original call was the second adhan, but when the first adhan was introduced, it rightly falls under the same command, and thus its ruling applies. Therefore, from the moment the first adhan is called, the obligation to stop selling and go to the mosque begins.

البيع (al-bay‘): Selling and buying transactions.
سعي (sa‘y): Walking/proceeding to the mosque for Friday prayer.

The Hanafi school holds that the obligation to leave selling and proceed to Friday prayer begins at the first adhan because the Quranic command uses the general term 'call', which includes any adhan for Friday prayer.

Prohibition of Prayer When the Imam Comes Out for Friday Sermon
Ruling with proof: prohibition of prayer when imam appears

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that all prayers are prohibited when the imam comes out for Friday sermon, identify the proof from athar, and explain the scope of the prohibition.

Core Idea
The imam's appearance for Friday sermon severs prayer, even supererogatory acts like tahiyyat al-masjid.

This lesson examines a specific ruling regarding Friday prayer: once the imam comes out or ascends the minbar, engaging in any prayer becomes prohibited. The commentary clarifies that this includes sunnah and nafl prayers, such as the mosque greeting. We will explore the proof from the statements of al-Zuhri and the companions, and understand the reasoning behind this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the imam's coming out (or climbing the minbar) for the Friday sermon. The ruling is 'haruma al-salah' — prayer becomes prohibited.
Note the phrase 'haruma al-salah' indicates a strict prohibition (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites al-Zuhri's statement: 'His coming out severs prayer, and his speech severs speech.' And narrations from ‘Ali and Ibn ‘Abbas: 'When the imam sits on the minbar, there is no prayer.'
These are athar (narrations from companions and tabi‘in), not direct Quran or hadith from the Prophet.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'severs' (yaqta‘) indicates that the imam's appearance cuts off the permissibility of prayer. The phrase 'no prayer' (la salata) indicates a general prohibition.
The legal implication: once the imam appears, any prayer becomes invalid or impermissible.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools allow tahiyyat al-masjid as long as the sermon has not begun, but the Hanafi school prohibits it from the moment the imam appears.
The Hanafi position is stricter: even supererogatory prayers are prohibited.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the general wording of the athar and the principle that listening to the sermon takes priority over supererogatory prayers.
The mufta bihi is the prohibition of all prayers once the imam comes out.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[3] قوله : حرم الصلاة؛ ولو كان سنة أو نفلاً، كتحية المسجد يدل عليه قول الزهري : «خروجه يقطع الصلاة، وكلامه يقطع الكلام»، أخرجه مالك في «الموطأ». وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة في «مصنفه» عن علي وابن عباس أخرج عن عروة له قال : «إذا قعد الإمام على المنبر فلا صلاة».

[2] His saying: 'And when he comes out' meaning from his house or from the preacher's room, and it is said the intended meaning is his climbing the minbar. Thus in al-Binayah. [3] His saying: 'prayer is prohibited' even if it is a sunnah or nafl, such as salutation of the mosque, as indicated by the saying of al-Zuhri: 'His coming out severs prayer, and his speech severs speech.' Commentary
This passage establishes that once the imam comes out for the Friday sermon (either from his house or from the preacher's room, or when he ascends the minbar), it becomes haram (prohibited) to engage in any prayer, even if it is a supererogatory act like the greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid). The proof is the statement of al-Zuhri (a prominent tabi‘i) that the imam's coming out severs prayer, meaning it cuts off the time for prayer. Additionally, a narration from ‘Ali and Ibn ‘Abbas states that when the imam sits on the minbar, there is no prayer. This ruling is strict: one should not start any prayer once the imam appears, and one must break off if already started? The text says 'haruma al-salah' implying it is forbidden to begin or continue. The hadith evidence supports the prohibition.

Key Terms
خرج الإمام (kharaja al-imām): The imam leaving his place or ascending the minbar to deliver the sermon.
تحية المسجد (taḥiyyat al-masjid): A two-rak'ah sunnah prayer performed upon entering the mosque.

Obligation to Proceed to Friday Prayer Upon the First Adhan
Clarifying the ruling of the first adhan and its application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation to leave trade upon the first adhan and explain the Quranic evidence and the response to the historical objection.

Core Idea
The general Quranic command applies to the first adhan, making it obligatory to leave trade and hasten to prayer.

Friday prayer is preceded by two adhans. While the second adhan is directly before the sermon, the first was added later. This lesson clarifies how the Hanafi school applies the Quranic verse to the first adhan, demonstrating the principle that a general text includes later innovations accepted by the ummah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being judged and what the ruling is. The act is 'proceeding to Friday prayer upon hearing the first adhan'. The ruling is 'wajib' (obligatory).
The ruling applies to leaving trade and hastening.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited by the author. It is the Quranic verse 62:9: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off selling.'
The verse is general (amm) and does not specify which adhan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the dalil proves the ruling. The imperative 'fas'aw' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul. The verse commands abandoning selling and hastening when the call is made.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Analyze the historical objection
Consider the objection: the verse was revealed when only one adhan existed, so it should apply only to that adhan. Recognize that this objection challenges the inclusion of the first adhan.
The objection is based on historical specificity (sabab al-nuzul).
5
Examine the Hanafi response
The commentator responds that the Quranic text is general ('amm). When the first adhan was added by Uthman with consensus, it falls under the general command. The ruling applies to any adhan that is part of the Friday call.
This illustrates the Hanafi position that 'amm remains general until there is specific exclusion (takhsis).

Source Text

And when the first adhan is called, they abandon selling and hasten. He said: his saying 'and when the first adhan is called'... summary: that it is obligatory to walk to Friday prayer, and to abandon selling and other worldly preoccupations that hinder hastening from the first adhan for Friday; due to His statement: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off selling.' If you say: it is established in the authentic books and others that in the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and Abu Bakr and Umar there was only one adhan, which is the second adhan called at the beginning of the sermon; then when the time of Uthman came and people increased, he added the first adhan, and the ummah accepted it without denial. So the call for Friday at the time of revelation of the verse was only the second, so hastening and leaving selling are required at it, not before. I say: The Quran does not mention the first or second adhan; rather it says: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday,' and that was applicable at that time only to the second adhan. But when the first adhan was added, it becomes included in the verse, and its ruling necessarily applies.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling related to the first adhan for Friday. The author explains that upon hearing the first adhan, it becomes obligatory (wajib) to abandon all worldly engagements, especially buying and selling, and to proceed to the mosque for the Friday prayer. The evidence is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9). However, an objection is raised: historically, in the time of the Prophet and the first two caliphs, there was only one adhan—the one that precedes the sermon. The addition of the first adhan was an innovation by Caliph Uthman due to the increase of people. Thus the verse originally applied only to the second adhan. The commentator responds that the Quranic text is general (amm) regarding 'the call to prayer,' and although it was originally applicable to the single adhan, when Uthman added the first adhan, it also falls under the same general command. Therefore, the obligation to hasten and leave trade applies to the first adhan as well. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that a general text applies to all individuals that fall under its literal meaning, even if the specific cause of revelation was particular. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
الأذان الأول (al-adhan al-awwal): The first of the two calls to prayer on Friday, introduced by Caliph Uthman.
السعي (al-sa'y): Hastening to the Friday prayer, including turning away from worldly affairs.

D) When the sun reaches its zenith

Key Takeaway
The Quranic command is general and covers any adhan that is part of the Friday prayer, thus the obligation begins with the first adhan.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Prohibition of Speech and Prayer During the Friday Khutbah: Ruling, Proof, and Intra-Hanafi Differences
Commentary on the ruling of speech and prayer during the Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speech and prayer during the Friday khutbah, distinguish between worldly and religious speech, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding the timing of prohibition, and determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Listening to the Friday sermon is wajib; speech and prayer are prohibited during the sermon, but there are differences over when and to what extent.

The Friday khutbah is a central pillar of Jumu'ah. The Hanafi school emphasizes attentive listening (insat) and prohibits any action that distracts. However, there is a nuanced distinction between worldly and religious speech, and an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the prohibition—especially concerning the light sitting (jalsa khafifa) between the two sermons. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the supporting hadiths, and the positions of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
From the commentary, determine the default ruling for speech and prayer during the Friday khutbah. Speech is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) and prayer is haram (forbidden) because the evidence for prohibition is from ahad hadiths, making speech less than haram but prayer more severe due to greater distraction.
The ruling applies from the moment the imam ascends the minbar for prayer, and for speech, only after the sermon begins (worldly speech).
2
Distinguish between types of speech
Identify the categories: worldly speech (duniyawi) is only disliked after the sermon begins, while religious speech (like dhikr, answering adhan) is also disliked after the sermon begins, except for specific acts like answering the adhan before the preacher, which is permitted based on the practice of Mu'awiyah.
This distinction is from Abu Hanifah.
3
Analyze the proof
The commentator cites numerous hadiths indicating the obligation of insat (listening). The apparent conflict with the hadith allowing a brief greeting prayer (tahiyyat al-masjid) is resolved by prioritizing the listening hadiths as a precaution. The greeting prayer hadith is seen as an exception or abrogated.
The key hadith: 'When one of you comes on Friday while the Imam is delivering the sermon, let him pray two rak'ahs and make them brief.' The Hanafis argue that the general evidence for insat overrides this.
4
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
Contrast Abu Hanifah's view with that of the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifah holds that prayer is prohibited from the imam's ascent; worldly speech is only disliked after the sermon begins; and the light sitting between sermons is part of the khutbah (prohibition applies). The Sahibayn hold that worldly speech is not disliked before the sermon or after the sermon, and the light sitting does not carry prohibition.
The dispute is based on whether the prohibition is tied to the act of listening (which is only during the actual delivery) or to the broader khutbah session.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is a combination: before the sermon, the stricter view of Abu Hanifah (prohibition from imam's ascent) is taken; after the sermon and during the light sitting, the more lenient view of the Sahibayn is taken (no prohibition). This is implied by the text's reference to al-Khulasah.
This synthesis is common in later Hanafi fatwa works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكلام حتى يتم خطبته. وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة دالة على وجوب الإنصات لاستماع الخطبة، وأن كل ما يشغله عنه ممنوع قولاً وفعلاً، وبهذا ثبت حرمة الصلاة أيضاً لأن الإخلال بالاستماع فيها أكثر. نعم يشكل على هذا قوله : إذا جاء أحدكم يوم الجمعة والإمام يخطب فليركع ركعتين وليتجوز فيها فإنه دال على الرخصة بهذا المقدار، وأصحابنا عملوا بالأخبار الموجبة لاستماع الخطبة الدالة على وجوب الإنصات احتياطاً. قوله : والكلام؛ الفرق بين الكلام والصلاة أن الصلاة يمنع منها من عند صعود الإمام على المنبر مطلقاً نفلاً كان أو سنة أو غير ذلك إلا فائتة الصبح لمن وجب عليه الترتيب. وأما الكلام فإنما يكره منه قبل شروع الخطبة الدنيوي لا الديني كالأذكار والتسبيح بعد الشروع فيها يكره مطلقاً، هذا هو الأصح، كما في النهاية وغيره، فلا تكره إجابة الأذان الذي يؤذن بين يدي الخطيب، وقد ثبت ذلك من فعل معاوية في صحيح البخاري، ولا دعاء الوسيلة المأثور بعد ذلك الأذان، هذا عند أبي حنيفة. وعندهما لا بأس بالكلام أي الدنيوي إذا خرج الإمام قبل أن يشرع في الخطبة وإذا نزل قبل أن يكبر، لأن الكراهة للإخلال بالاستماع والاستماع هاهنا بخلاف الصلاة، فإنها قد تمتد، كذا في الهداية. ثم كما يكره الكلام يكره الأكل والشرب والعبث والالتفات والتخطي وغيرها مما يمنع في الصلاة، وإنما خص الكلام بالذكر لكونه أكثر وقوعاً. كذا في جامع الرموز. قوله : حتى يتم؛ قال في جامع الرموز: فيه إشارة إلى أنهما يحرمان عند جلسة الخفيفة، وفيه خلاف، ولا يحرمان بعد الخطبة، وهذا عندهما. بالذي قال أبي، فقال رسول الله : صدق أبي في سنن ابن ماجة وصحيح ابن خزيمة ومسند أحمد وغيرها. وأما عنده: فيحرمان، كما في المضمرات، لكن في الخلاصة: يكره الصلاة في هذا الوقت إجماعاً، وكأنه اختار قوله قبل الخطبة، وقولهما بعدها.
And speech until he completes his sermon. In this chapter, there are many hadiths indicating the obligation of listening attentively to the sermon, and that everything that distracts from it is prohibited in word and deed, and by this, the prohibition of prayer is also established because the lack of listening is greater in it. Yes, this is challenged by his statement: 'When one of you comes on Friday while the Imam is delivering the sermon, let him pray two rak'ahs and make them brief.' This indicates permission to this extent, and our companions acted upon the hadiths that necessitate listening to the sermon, which indicate the obligation of listening attentively, out of caution. His statement: 'and speech'; the difference between speech and prayer is that prayer is prohibited from the time the Imam ascends the minbar absolutely, whether voluntary or sunnah or otherwise, except for the dawn missed prayer for one who is required to make it up in order. As for speech, only worldly speech is disliked before the start of the sermon, not religious speech like dhikr and tasbih; after the start of the sermon, it is disliked absolutely. This is the soundest view, as in al-Nihayah and others. Thus, answering the adhan that is given in front of the preacher is not disliked, and this is proven by the action of Mu'awiyah in Sahih al-Bukhari, nor the supplication of al-Wasilah that is reported after that adhan. This is according to Abu Hanifah. According to the two companions, there is no harm in worldly speech if the Imam leaves before he starts the sermon and if he descends before he says the takbir, because the dislike is for neglecting listening, and listening here is unlike prayer, for prayer may be prolonged. This is in al-Hidayah. Then, just as speech is disliked, so too are eating, drinking, playing, turning away, stepping over others, and other things that are prohibited in prayer, but speech is specified because it occurs more often. This is in Jami' al-Rumuz. His statement: 'until he completes'; he said in Jami' al-Rumuz: It indicates that both are prohibited during the light sitting, and there is a difference of opinion, and they are not prohibited after the sermon, and this is according to the two companions. By what my father said, the Messenger of Allah [SAW] said: 'My father spoke the truth' in Sunan Ibn Majah, Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah, Musnad Ahmad, etc. As for according to him [Abu Hanifah], they are prohibited, as in al-Mudmarat, but in al-Khulasah: prayer is disliked at this time by consensus, and it is as if he [the author of al-Khulasah] chose his [Abu Hanifah's] view before the sermon, and theirs after it.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on a statement from the matn regarding the prohibition of speech and prayer during the Friday khutbah. The commentator begins by affirming the prohibition based on numerous hadiths that require attentive listening (insat). He then addresses a potential conflict with a hadith allowing a brief greeting prayer (tahiyyat al-masjid) during the sermon, explaining that the Hanafi school prioritizes the hadiths about listening as a precaution. Next, he distinguishes between speech and prayer: prayer is absolutely prohibited from the moment the imam ascends the minbar, with the sole exception of making up a missed Fajr prayer if one is legally obligated to maintain order in his prayers (tartib). Speech, however, is categorized: worldly speech is disliked only after the sermon begins; religious speech (e.g., dhikr) is disliked after the sermon begins. However, answering the adhan given before the preacher and reciting the du'a al-wasilah after it are not disliked, as these are religious acts. This is the view of Abu Hanifah (ra). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), there is no blame in worldly speech if the imam comes out before starting the sermon or descends the minbar before starting the prayer, because the dislike stems from missing the listening, and listening is not obligatory at those times. The commentator then notes that other actions like eating, drinking, fidgeting, turning away, and stepping over shoulders are also disliked. Finally, he addresses the light sitting (jalsa khafifa) between the two sermons: according to the Sahibayn, prayer and speech are not prohibited during this sitting or after the sermon; according to Abu Hanifah, they are. The text cites a hadith from Ibn Majah and others as evidence for the Sahibayn's view, but notes that al-Khulasah suggests prayer is disliked by consensus during this time, as if the author accepted Abu Hanifah's view for before the sermon and theirs for after.

Key Terms
الإنصات (al-insāt): Listening attentively and silently to the Friday sermon, which is wajib.
الكراهة (al-karāhah): In this passage, refers to a prohibition that is less than haram (makruh tahrimi) due to zanni evidence.
الجلسة الخفيفة (al-jalsah al-khafīfah): The brief sitting between the two Friday sermons; its status is disputed regarding prohibition of speech and prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, when is worldly speech during Friday prayer permissible?
A) During the imam's ascent of the minbar
B) Before the sermon starts
C) During the light sitting between the two sermons
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits prayer during the Friday khutbah from the imam's ascent and dislikes worldly speech after the sermon begins, with an intra-Hanafi difference on the exact timing.
