The Second Adhan and Sunnah Actions of the Imam on Friday
Commentary on the sunnah of the second adhan and the imam's actions on the minbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions of the imam on Friday and explain the historical basis of the second adhan.

Core Idea
The second adhan on Friday is a sunnah established by 'Uthman with consensus of the Companions.

The Friday prayer has several sunnah actions that enhance its completeness. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the second adhan, the imam's sitting on the minbar, and the brief sitting between the two sermons. Understanding these practices helps us follow the prophetic model and appreciate how the Companions adapted to changing circumstances while preserving the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah actions
List the actions described: second adhan when imam sits on minbar, sitting at that time, sitting between sermons, standing during sermon, and being on the minbar.
All are sunnah muakkadah.
2
Understand the historical development
Trace the narration from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: originally one adhan at the Prophet's time, then 'Uthman added a third (counting iqamah) due to increased crowd.
The second adhan is actually the third in count if iqamah is included.
3
Define the minbar
Note the linguistic derivation and purpose: from 'nabr' (sign/raised mark), it is a raised platform for the preacher's voice to reach.
4
Note the permissibility of religious speech
Religious speech (dhikr, du'a) is not disliked during the two sittings (during adhan and between sermons) for anyone.
This is a relaxation for those present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا جلس على المنبر أذن ثانياً بين يديه. هذا الجلوس عند الأذان، والجلوس بين الخطبتين خفيفاً سنتان متوارثتان عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه، كما أن القيام حال الخطبة سنة، وكونه على المنبر سنة أيضاً، ثبت كل ذلك من فعل النبي على ما هو مخرج في الصحيحين وكتب السنن والمسانيد، ولا يكره الكلام الديني في هاتين الجلستين لا من الخطيب ولا من غيره. قوله : على المنبر؛ بكسر الميم: هو ما يصنع للجلوس الخطيب والواعظ عليه عند الخطبة والوعظ ليصل صوته إلى بعيد، مأخوذ من النبر، وهو العلامة. قوله : أذن؛ بصيغة المجهول، ويمكن أن يكون معروفاً، والضمير إلى المؤذن، وهذا الأذان لاطلاع الحاضرين، وإحضار الغائبين عن المسجد. قوله : بين يديه؛ أي مستقبل الإمام في المسجد كان أو خارجه، والمسنون هو الثاني؛ ففي سنن أبي داود بسنده عن السائب بن يزيد: إن الأذان كان أوله حين يجلس الإمام على المنبر يوم الجمعة في عهد النبي وأبي بكر وعمر، فلما كان خلافة عثمان وكثر الناس أمر بالأذان الثالث وأذن به على الزوراء، فثبت الأمر على ذلك. والمراد بالأذان الثالث: هو الأول، وجعله ثالثاً بإطلاق الأذان على الإقامة أيضاً. والزوراء: اسم سوق بالمدينة.
And when he sits on the minbar, the second adhan is called in front of him. This sitting at the time of the adhan, and the light sitting between the two sermons, are two sunnahs transmitted from the Messenger of Allah and his Companions, just as standing during the sermon is sunnah, and being on the minbar is also sunnah; all of this is established by the action of the Prophet as recorded in the Sahihs and books of Sunan and Musnads. Religious speech is not disliked during these two sittings, neither from the preacher nor from others. His statement: 'on the minbar'; with kasra on the mim: it is what is made for the preacher and admonisher to sit upon during the sermon and admonition so that his voice may reach far; it is derived from al-nabr, which is the sign. His statement: 'adhdhana (announced)'; in the passive form, and it could be active, and the pronoun refers to the mu'adhdhin, and this adhan is for the information of those present and to bring those absent from the mosque. His statement: 'in front of him'; i.e., facing the imam whether inside the mosque or outside, and the sunnah is the second; for in Sunan Abi Dawud with its chain from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: The adhan was initially when the imam sits on the minbar on Friday during the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar. When 'Uthman became caliph and the people increased, he ordered a third adhan and it was called at al-Zawra', and the matter was established upon that. By the third adhan is meant the first, and it was called third by applying the term adhan also to the iqamah. And al-Zawra' is the name of a market in Madinah.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah actions of the imam on Friday and the second adhan. The commentator first notes that when the imam sits on the minbar, a second adhan (in addition to the first call) is given. The imam's sitting at that moment and the brief sitting between the two sermons are both established sunnahs from the Prophet and his companions. Similarly, standing during the sermon and being on the minbar are sunnah. Religious speech (like dhikr, du'a) is not disliked during these two sittings for anyone. The term 'minbar' is defined as a raised structure for the preacher's voice to carry. The adhan is given in front of the imam to inform attendees and call those outside. The commentator clarifies the historical development: originally, only one adhan was given when the imam sat on the minbar. During 'Uthman's time, due to the increased number of people, he ordered an additional adhan (called the 'third' because the iqamah was counted as one) to be given at a place called al-Zawra', and this practice remained. Thus, the second adhan is a sunnah established by the caliph 'Uthman with the approval of the Companions.

Key Terms
الأذان الثاني (al-adhān al-thānī): The second call to prayer given on Friday when the imam sits on the minbar, distinct from the first adhan before the khutbah.
المنبر (al-minbar): A raised platform from which the sermon is delivered, derived from nabr (raised mark).
الزوراء (al-Zawrā'): A specific marketplace in Madinah where the second adhan was called during 'Uthman's time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the second adhan on Friday was introduced by which caliph?
A) Abu Bakr
B) 'Umar
C) 'Uthman
D) 'Ali

Key Takeaway
The second adhan, sitting on the minbar, and sitting between sermons are sunnah muakkadah established by the Prophet and the rightly-guided caliphs.

Salah — Prayer

The Sunan of the Friday Khutbah
Commentary expanding on the matn regarding Friday khutbah sunan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of the Friday khutbah and explain their proof from hadith, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding prayer during the adhan.

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah has established sunan: sitting, standing, leaning, two sermons with a light sitting, and facing the khatib.

The Friday prayer is a cornerstone of the week for Muslims, and its khutbah (sermon) comes with a set of recommended practices (sunan) derived from the Prophet's ﷺ consistent action. This lesson unpacks those sunan as explained in a classical Hanafi commentary, supported by authentic hadith. You'll learn not only what to do but also the proof behind each sunnah, and how the Hanafi school navigates a subtle difference of opinion regarding prayer during the adhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah act
Read the passage and list the specific actions described as sunnah: sitting on the minbar, giving the adhan, standing for the khutbah, leaning on a staff, delivering two sermons with a light sitting in between, and the listeners facing the khatib.
These are all labeled as sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the proof for each
For each sunnah, find the hadith cited in the commentary. Note the source (e.g., Sahih Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud) and the specific wording that establishes the practice.
The hadith of al-Sa’ib ibn Yazid proves the adhan timing; the hadith of Shu’ayb al-Ta’ifi proves leaning.
3
Analyze the commentary's expansion
The commentary expands on the matn by explaining the derivation of 'minbar', the purpose of the adhan, and the historical context of the third adhan by Uthman. Understand how the commentary clarifies the text.
Also note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about prayer during the adhan.
4
Distinguish the mufta bihi
Identify which positions are relied upon. For the adhan, the original practice (second adhan) is sunnah; for the dislike of prayer, the commentators lean toward the view that it is disliked at that time by consensus.
Al-Sarakhsi’s reasoning about preparation being like commencement is key.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Imagine you are attending Friday prayer. Based on this lesson, state what the khatib and listeners should do, and what should be avoided (e.g., praying during the adhan).
Consider the current common practice of facing qiblah and why it is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صلاة الجمعة
وإذا جلس على المنبر أذن ثانياً بين يديه
[٢] وإذا جلس على المنبر (٢) أذن ثانياً بين يديه 
وأما عنده : فيحرمان، كما في «المضمرات»، لكن في «الخلاصة»: يكره الصلاة في هذا الوقت إجماعاً، وكأنه اختار قوله قبل الخطبة، وقولهما بعدها.
[١] قوله : وإذا جلس؛ هذا الجلوس عند الأذان، والجلوس بين الخطبتين خفيفاً سنتان متوارثتان عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه، كما أن القيام حال الخطبة سنة، وكونه على المنبر سنة أيضاً، ثبت كل ذلك من فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على ما هو مخرج في «الصحيحين» وكتب السنن والمسانيد، ولا يكره الكلام الديني في هاتين الجلستين لا من الخطيب ولا من غيره.
[٢] قوله: على المنبر؛ بكسر الميم: هو ما يصنع الجلوس الخطيب والواعظ عليه عند الخطبة والوعظ؛ ليصل صوته إلى بعيد، مأخوذ من النبر، وهو العلامة.
[٣] قوله: أذن؛ بصيغة المجهول، ويمكن أن يكون معروفاً، والضمير إلى المؤذن، وهذا الأذان لاطلاع الحاضرين، وإحضار الغائبين عن المسجد.
[٤] قوله: بين يديه؛ أي مستقبل الإمام في المسجد كان أو خارجه، والمسنون هو الثاني؛ ففي سنن أبي داود بسنده عن السائب بن يزيد: «إن الأذان كان أوله حين يجلس الإمام على المنبر يوم الجمعة في عهد النبي وأبي بكر وعمر، فلما كان خلافة عثمان، وكثر الناس أمر بالأذان الثالث وأذن به على الزوراء، فثبت الأمر على ذلك» والمراد بالأذان الثالث: هو الأول، وجعله ثالثاً بإطلاق الأذان على الإقامة أيضاً. والزوراء: اسم سوق بالمدينة.
فعن ابن عمر قال: كان رسول الله لا يخطب يوم الجمعة قائماً ثم يجلس ثم يقوم في «صحيح مسلم» وغيره.
لكن قال السرخسي في المبسوط: (إن الإمام إذا صعد المنبر ليخطب كان مستعداً لها فيجعل كالشارع فيها من وجه ألا ترى أن في كراهة الصلاة جعل الاستعداد لها كالشروع فيها، فكذلك في كراهة الكلام ووجوب الإنصات غير مقصور على حال تشاغله بالخطبة، حتى يكره الكلام في حالة الجلسة بين الخطبتين).
واستقبلوه مستمعين، ويخطب خطبتين بينهما قعدة.
[١] قوله: واستقبلوه؛ هذا هو السنة، أي يستقبل السامعون الخطيب بوجوههم، سواء كانوا أمامه أو يمينه أو يساره، لكن الرسم الآن أنهم يستقبلون القبلة، ولا يؤمرون بتركه لما يلحقهم من الحرج بتسوية الصفوف بعد الخطبة على ما قال السرخسي، وهذا أحسن، كما في «المحيط». ويخيرون بين الجلوس محتبياً أو متربعاً أو غير ذلك مما تيسر له. كذا في «جامع المضمرات».
[٢] قوله: ويخطب؛ متوكناً على عصا أو قوس، كما ثبت في سنن أبي داود، وهذا نص على أنه لم يكن يضع في حال الخطبتين إحدى يديه على الأخرى كوضع الصلاة كما جرت به عادة كثير من خطباء زماننا، والأولى فيه أنه إن لم يتوكأ على شيء أن يرسل يديه إرسالاً، فإن وضع إحدى يديه على الأخرى استراحة لا بأس به. كما في «إحياء العلوم» للغزالي.
[٣] قوله: قعدة؛ أي خفيفة مقدار ثلاثة آيات، وبقدر ما يستقر كل عضو موضعه.
The Book of Prayer: Friday Prayer. And when he sits on the minbar, a second call to prayer is made before him. And according to him (Abu Hanifa): both are disliked (makruh), as in al-Mudmarat, but in al-Khulasa: prayer at this time is unanimously disliked, and it seems he chose his statement before the khutbah and their statement after it. His statement: 'And when he sits': this sitting at the time of the adhan, and the light sitting between the two khutbahs are two established sunnas transmitted from the Messenger of Allah and his Companions, just as standing during the khutbah is sunnah, and being on the minbar is also sunnah. All of that is established from the action of the Prophet as narrated in the Sahihayn and Sunan works. Religious speech is not disliked during these two sittings, neither from the khatib nor from others. His statement: 'on the minbar' – with a kasrah on the meem: it is what the khatib and preacher sit on during the khutbah and sermon so that his voice reaches far; derived from al-nabr, which means sign. His statement: 'is called' – in the passive voice, and it can be active, and the pronoun refers to the mu'adhdhin. This adhan is to inform those present and to summon those absent from the mosque. His statement: 'before him' – meaning facing the imam, whether in the mosque or outside, and the sunnah is the second. For in Sunan Abi Dawud with his chain from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: 'Indeed the adhan originally was when the imam sat on the minbar on Friday in the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar. When Uthman became caliph and the people increased, he ordered the third adhan and it was performed on al-Zawra', and the matter remained upon that.' The meaning of 'third adhan' is the first, and he made it third by also calling the iqamah an adhan. Al-Zawra' is the name of a market in Madinah. From Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah would not deliver the Friday khutbah while standing, then he would sit, then stand' – in Sahih Muslim and elsewhere. But al-Sarakhsi said in al-Mabsut: 'When the imam ascends the minbar to deliver the khutbah, he is prepared for it and is considered as having begun it in a sense. Do you not see that in the dislike of prayer, preparation for it is considered as starting it? Similarly, the dislike of speech and the obligation of listening are not limited to the time of engaging in the khutbah, such that speech is disliked during the sitting between the two khutbahs.' And they face him listening, and he delivers two khutbahs with a sitting between them. His statement: 'And they face him' – this is the sunnah, i.e., the listeners face the khatib with their faces, whether they are in front of him, to his right, or his left. However, the current practice is that they face the qiblah, and they are not commanded to abandon it due to the difficulty they would face in straightening the rows after the khutbah, as al-Sarakhsi said, and this is better, as in al-Muhit. They are given a choice between sitting with knees drawn up, cross-legged, or otherwise according to what is easy. Thus in Jami' al-Mudmarat. His statement: 'and he delivers the khutbah' – leaning on a staff or bow, as established in Sunan Abi Dawud. This is a text that he did not place one hand on the other as in prayer, as is the custom of many of our contemporary khatibs. The preferred way is that if he does not lean on anything, he lets his hands hang loosely. If he places one hand on the other for rest, there is no harm, as in Ihya' Ulum al-Din by al-Ghazali. His statement: 'a sitting' – i.e., a light sitting, to the extent of three verses, and such that each limb settles in its place.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn regarding the Friday prayer, specifically the sunan of the khutbah. The commentator begins by explaining that when the imam sits on the minbar, a second adhan is given. He notes an intra-madhhab disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa, both the adhan before the khutbah and after it are disliked (makruh) for prayer at that time, but the relied-upon position (as indicated by the text) is that prayer is disliked unanimously. The commentary then explains the sunan of the khutbah: the imam sits briefly at the start, then stands for the khutbah, and sits lightly between the two khutbahs. These are established from the Prophet's practice. The minbar is defined as an elevated seat to project the voice. The adhan is given to inform those present and summon those absent. The second adhan (the one before the khutbah) is established by the hadith of al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid in Sunan Abi Dawud, which traces the development from one adhan to the addition of a second by Uthman. The commentator then discusses the listeners' orientation: they should face the imam, but the current practice of facing the qiblah is accepted due to practical difficulty. The imam should lean on a staff or bow while delivering the khutbah, and he should not place his hands on each other like in prayer, though if he does so for rest it is permissible. The sitting between the two khutbahs should be brief, approximately the time to recite three verses. All these rulings are based on the Prophetic practice as recorded in authentic hadith sources.

Key Terms
المنبر (al-minbar): An elevated structure upon which the khatib sits or stands to deliver the Friday sermon, derived from 'nabr' meaning a sign or elevation.
الأذان الثالث (al-adhan al-thalith): The first adhan (before the khutbah) is called the third adhan because the iqamah is considered an adhan; hence the sequence: first adhan (before khutbah), second adhan (the call at the beginning of the khutbah?), but in the hadith, it refers to the adhan introduced by Uthman.
القعدة (al-qa'dah): The brief sitting between the two Friday sermons, described as light (khafif) and approximately the duration of reciting three verses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many adhans are considered part of the Friday prayer sunnah?
A) One adhan (before the khutbah)
B) Two adhans: one before the khutbah (when imam sits) and the iqamah
C) Three adhans: two before the khutbah and the iqamah
D) Only the iqamah

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah has specific sunan including sitting, standing, leaning, and two sermons, all established by hadith; prayer during the adhan is disliked, and listeners should face the khatib (or accept qiblah due to ease).

The Historical Foundation of the Friday Adhan
Narration of the adhan practice from Prophet's time to Banu Umayyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of the adhan for Friday prayer and identify the historical evidence from the Prophet and the early caliphs.

Core Idea
The adhan for Friday is sunnah before the sermon, established by the practice of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar.

This passage traces the historical development of the adhan on Friday, showing that the original practice was to give the adhan when the Imam sat on the pulpit, before the sermon. The narration confirms that this was the consistent practice of the Prophet and the first two caliphs, providing the basis for the Hanafi ruling that the adhan for Jumu'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah and should be given before the sermon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prophetic Practice
The passage states: 'He used to give the adhan in front of the Messenger of Allah when he sat on the pulpit on Friday at the door of the mosque.' Pinpoint the act: the adhan was given at the door of the mosque as the Prophet ascended the pulpit.
This is the original Sunnah.
2
Confirm Continuity with the Caliphs
The narration explicitly extends this practice to Abu Bakr and Umar: 'and Abu Bakr and Umar.' This shows the early caliphs adhered to the same method.
No change in the first two caliphates.
3
Note the Later Change
The passage then references Hisham ibn 'Abd al-Malik who implemented the adhan on the minaret, a departure from the earlier practice. This change is recorded as a later development.
The original practice remained the standard for Sunnah.
4
Extract the Ruling
From the historical evidence, the Hanafi school derives that the adhan for Friday is sunnah mu'akkadah and must be performed before the sermon, as the Prophet and his companions did.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply to Contemporary Practice
In a Hanafi mosque, the adhan on Friday is given either inside the mosque or on the minaret before the khatib ascends. This lesson confirms that this timing is rooted in the prophetic model.
Variations in number of mu'adhdhins are later accommodations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستقبلوه مستمعين، ويخطب خُطبتين بينهما قعدة. وبسند آخر عنه: «كان يؤذن من بين يدي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا جلس على المنبر يوم الجمعة على باب المسجد، وأبي بكر وعمر. [؟] وفي كتاب «المدخل» لابن الحاج محمد المالكي: «السنة في أذان الجمعة إذا صعد الإمام على المنبر أن يكون المؤذِّنُ على المنار، كذلك كان في عهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على المنار، والخطيب على المنبر إذ ذاك، ثم إنه لما تولى هشام بن عبد الملك أخذ الأذان الذي فعله عثمان وجعله على المنار، وكان المؤذِّنُ واحداً يؤذن بعد الزوال، ثم ثقل الأذان الذي كان على المنار بين صعود الإمام على المنبر على عهد النبي وأبي بكر وعمر، [؟] وصدر من خلافة عثمان له بين يديه، وكانوا يؤذنون ثلاثة فجعلهم يؤذن جماعة». انتهى (۱)
And they face him listening, and he delivers two sermons with a sitting between them. And with another chain from him: 'He used to give the adhan in front of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he sat on the pulpit on Friday at the door of the mosque, and Abu Bakr and Umar.' In the book 'al-Madkhal' by Ibn al-Hajj al-Maliki: 'The Sunnah in the adhan of Friday when the Imam ascends the pulpit is that the mu'adhdhin be on the minaret; likewise it was in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, on the minaret, and the khatib on the pulpit at that time. Then when Hisham ibn 'Abd al-Malik came to power, he took the adhan that 'Uthman had made and placed it on the minaret, and the mu'adhdhin was one person giving adhan after zawal. Then the adhan that was on the minaret between the ascension of the Imam on the pulpit became heavy, in the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar, and at the beginning of 'Uthman's caliphate [the adhan was] before him, and they used to give three adhans, so he made them give adhan collectively.' End.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a historical narration about the adhan on Friday. The commentator begins by citing the matn words 'and they face him listening' and 'he delivers two sermons with a sitting between them' to introduce the discussion. Then he provides a supporting narration that the adhan was given at the door of the mosque when the Prophet sat on the pulpit, and this practice continued with Abu Bakr and Umar. Then he quotes from Ibn al-Hajj al-Maliki's al-Madkhal detailing the development: originally the mu'adhdhin stood on the minaret while the khatib was on the pulpit. During Hisham ibn 'Abd al-Malik's rule, he implemented the adhan that 'Uthman had established, with a single mu'adhdhin after zawal. Later, the adhan on the minaret became too burdensome, so it was moved to before the khatib's ascent, and three mu'adhdhins were made to give adhan collectively. This historical account shows the evolution of the practice and indicates that the Sunnah is for the adhan to be before the sermon. The passage does not present a new ruling but provides evidence for the established practice.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): Here it refers to the established practice of the Prophet and the early caliphs regarding the adhan on Friday, as transmitted in the narration.
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer, specifically on Friday before the sermon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He reduced it to one mu'adhdhin
B) He moved the adhan to the minaret
C) He added a second adhan
D) He made the adhan after the sermon

Key Takeaway
The adhan for Friday is established by the practice of the Prophet and the early caliphs, and should be given before the sermon as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Facing the Khatib and Sitting Postures During Friday Sermon
Ruling on audience orientation and seating during Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the khatib during the Friday sermon and identify the permissible sitting postures.

Core Idea
Facing the khatib is Sunnah but hardship makes facing qibla acceptable; any comfortable sitting posture is allowed.

The Friday sermon is a central part of Jumu'ah. This lesson explains two aspects of proper conduct for the audience: which direction to face and how to sit. While the ideal is to face the khatib, practical considerations have led the Hanafi school to permit facing the qibla. Similarly, various sitting postures are allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling from the matn
The matn phrase 'and they face him' indicates a recommended act. Recognize that the commentator identifies this as Sunnah.
2
Understand the Sunnah status and the exception
The text states that current practice is to face qibla, and people are not commanded to change it due to hardship. Note that the original ruling is overridden by a valid excuse (al-haraj).
This is an application of the principle that hardship brings ease.
3
Recognize the reasoning of hardship as a basis for the exception
Al-Sarakhsi's reasoning: forcing the congregation to face the khatib would cause difficulty in straightening rows after the sermon. This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) based on custom and necessity.
The commentator calls this 'ahsan' (better view).
4
Note the permissibility of various sitting postures
The audience is given a choice between sitting with knees drawn up, cross-legged, or any comfortable position. This is not regulated strictly.
The source cites Jami' al-Mudmarat for this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : واستقبلوه ؛ هذا هو السنة ، أي يستقبل السامعون الخطيب بوجوههم، سواء كانوا أمامه أو يمينه أو يساره ، لكنَّ الرَّسم الآن أنهم يستقبلون القبلة، ولا يؤمرونَ بتركه لما يلحقهم من الحرج بتسوية الصفوف بعد الخطبة على ما قال السرخسي، وهذا أحسنُ، كما في «المحيط». ويخيرون بين الجلوس محتبياً أو متربعاً أو غير ذلك مما تيسر لـه. كذا في «جامع المضمرات».
His statement: 'and they face him' – this is the Sunnah, meaning the listeners should face the khatib with their faces, whether they are in front of him, to his right or left. But the current custom is that they face the qibla, and they are not commanded to abandon it due to the hardship that would befall them in straightening the rows after the sermon, as al-Sarakhsi said. And this is better, as in al-Muhit. And they are given a choice between sitting with knees drawn up (muhtabiyan) or cross-legged (mutarabbi'an) or any other way that is easy for them. Likewise in Jami' al-Mudmarat.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'and they face him' regarding the audience's orientation during the Friday sermon. The commentator states that the Sunnah is for the listeners to face the khatib directly, regardless of their position relative to him. However, the prevailing practice in his time was for the audience to face the qibla. He cites al-Sarakhsi's reasoning that this practice is not to be changed because forcing the congregation to face the khatib would cause hardship in rearranging the rows after the sermon. Therefore, it is permissible to remain facing qibla, and this is considered the better view (ahsan). Regarding sitting posture, the audience is free to choose between various permissible positions such as sitting with knees drawn up (ihtiba') or cross-legged (tarbi'), or any comfortable position.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): Here it refers to the recommended act of facing the khatib during the sermon.
الجلوس محتبياً (al-julus muhtabiyan): Sitting with the knees drawn up to the chest and wrapping the arms around them.
الجلوس متربعاً (al-julus mutarabbi'an): Sitting cross-legged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because facing the khatib is not Sunnah.
B) Because of the hardship in straightening rows after the sermon.
C) Because the khatib prefers facing qibla.
D) Because it is wajib to face qibla.

Key Takeaway
Facing the khatib is recommended but may be abandoned due to hardship; any comfortable sitting posture is permissible.

Leaning on a Stick and Hand Placement During Friday Sermon
Ruling on the khatib leaning on a staff and placement of hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions for the khatib during the Friday sermon and identify the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Leaning on a staff and letting hands hang are sunnan for the khatib; folding is permissible but not preferred.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the proper posture for the khatib during the Friday sermon. It clarifies that the Prophet ﷺ would lean on a staff or bow and would not place his hands one over the other as in prayer. The text distinguishes between the recommended practice and what is merely permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being described? For the khatib during the sermon: leaning on a staff and hand placement. The ruling is sunnah (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from Sunan Abi Dawud: the Prophet stood leaning on a staff or bow.
This is a hadith ahad, so zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action indicates it is a Sunnah act for the khatib. The way he stood informs the recommended posture.
4
Understand the nuance on hand placement
The text also addresses hand placement: the Sunnah is to let hands hang; folding for rest is permissible but not the best.
This is derived from the Prophet's practice and the statement 'no harm'.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In practice, the khatib should lean on something if available and avoid folding hands like in prayer; if not leaning, let hands hang.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ويخطب ؛ متوكناً على عصا أو قوس (۳) ، كما ثبت في سنن أبي داود»، وهذا نص على أنه لم يكن يضع في حال الخطبتين إحدى يديه على الأخرى كوضع الصَّلاةِ كما جرت به عادةً كثير من خطباء زماننا ، والأولى فيه أنه إن لم يتوكأ على شيء أن يرسل يديه إرسالاً ، فإن وضع إحدى يديه على الأخرى استراحة لا بأس به. كما في «إحياء العلوم» للغزالي.
His statement: 'and he delivers the sermon' – leaning on a staff or bow, as is established in Sunan Abi Dawud. And this is a text indicating that he would not place one hand over the other during the two sermons like the position in prayer, as is the custom of many of our contemporary khatibs. The preferable thing is that if he does not lean on anything, he should let his hands hang loosely. If he places one hand over the other for rest, there is no harm in it, as in Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din by al-Ghazali.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn word 'he delivers the sermon,' specifying that the khatib should lean on a staff or bow, citing a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud as proof. The commentator clarifies that this indicates the Prophet did not place his hands one over the other as in prayer, contrary to the practice of many contemporary khatibs. The recommended (awla) action is to let the hands hang loosely if not leaning. However, folding the hands for rest is permissible.

Key Terms
متوكئاً (mutawakki'an): Leaning for support, here on a staff or bow.
إرسال اليدين (irsal al-yadayn): Letting the hands hang loosely at the sides.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Brief Sitting Between the Two Friday Sermons
Definition and duration of the sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and duration of the brief sitting between the two Friday sermons and identify its status as Sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The brief sitting between Friday sermons is Sunnah, not wajib, and lasts approximately three verses.

In this lesson, we examine a definition from the Hanafi fiqh commentary 'Umdat al-Ri'aya. The text clarifies the meaning and duration of the brief sitting between the two Friday sermons, a Sunnah act often misunderstood. We will see how the commentator expands on the original matn term 'qad'da' to provide practical guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
The term 'qad'da' refers to a sitting between the two Friday sermons. In the Hanafi school, this sitting is a Sunnah act, meaning it is recommended but not obligatory.
The act is part of the Friday prayer ritual.
2
Understand the duration
The commentator describes it as 'khafifa' (brief) and gives two measures: the time to recite approximately three short Quranic verses, and the time for each limb to settle in its place.
The three-verse approximation is an example, not a strict requirement.
3
Recognize the expansion from the base text
The base matn only mentioned 'qad'da'. The commentator expands by defining its length, providing clarity for practice.
This is typical of sharh literature: explaining ambiguous terms.
4
Note the scope
This ruling is specific to the Friday prayer (Salat al-Jumu'ah), not to other prayers.
The sitting is unique to the Friday khutbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : قعدة ؛ أي خفيفة مقدار ثلاثة آيات ، وبقدر ما يستقر كل عضو موضعه.
His statement: 'a sitting' – meaning a brief sitting, approximately the length of three verses, and to the extent that each limb settles in its place.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage explains the matn term 'qad'da' (a sitting) referring to the brief pause between the two Friday sermons. The commentator specifies that it should be light (khafifa), measured by the time it takes to recite approximately three short Quranic verses, or enough time for the limbs to settle. This is a definition of the duration, not a strict requirement, as it is a Sunnah act.

Key Terms
قعدة (qad'da): The brief sitting between the two sermons on Friday.
خفيفة (khafifa): Brief, light, not prolonged.

The Khatib Must Stand During the Friday Sermon
Ruling on the khatib being standing during the sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the khatib must stand for the Friday sermon and identify when sitting is makruh (disliked).

Core Idea
A khatib must stand for the Friday sermon; sitting without excuse is makruh but does not invalidate the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the posture of the khatib (preacher) during the Friday khutbah. The Hanafi school holds that standing is a sunnah mu'akkadah, and delivering the sermon while sitting without a valid excuse is makruh tanzihi. Understanding this distinction is important for both khutabā' and those who attend Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on standing
The passage states that the khatib should be qā'im (standing) for the sermon. This is a required condition for the preferred practice.
The matn simply says 'qa'iman' as a condition.
2
Note the consequence of sitting
The passage says 'if he sits without an excuse, it is disliked (makruh).' This indicates that sitting without reason is not a nullifier but a disliked act.
The term 'kariha' in Hanafi fiqh usually means makruh tanzihi.
3
Understand the Hukm level
Standing is a sunnah mu'akkadah. Leaving it without excuse is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), not sinful. The prayer remains valid.
This is a milder ruling than considering standing fard or wajib.
4
Consider the exception
The phrase 'min ghayri 'udhr' (without an excuse) implies that if there is a valid excuse (e.g., illness), sitting is not disliked.
The excuse must be genuine; fatigue or laziness does not count.

Source Text

قوله : قائماً ؛ فإن خطب جالساً من غير عذر كره.
His statement: 'standing' – for if he delivers the sermon while sitting without an excuse, it is disliked (makruh).
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage explains the matn condition that the khatib should deliver the sermon while standing (qa'iman). The commentator states that if the khatib sits during the sermon without a valid excuse (like illness), the action is considered makruh (disliked). This implies that standing is a Sunnah mu'akkadah, and leaving it without reason is contrary to the proper practice. The ruling is based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

Key Terms
قائماً (qa'iman): Standing, here referring to the khatib's posture during the sermon.
كره (kariha): It is disliked (makruh tanzihi).

Purity of the Khatib During the Friday Sermon
Ruling on purity of the khatib in Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the khatib's state of purity during the Friday sermon and explain why impurity is makruh.

Core Idea
Purity for the khatib is recommended; an impure sermon is valid but disliked.

The Friday sermon (khutbah) has specific etiquettes and conditions. One such etiquette concerns the khatib's state of ritual purity. This passage clarifies that while the Prophet ﷺ would deliver the sermon in a state of purity, it is not a binding condition—rather, it is a recommended practice (Sunnah). Departing from it is disliked (makruh) but does not invalidate the sermon.

Guided Path
1
Locate the key term
Identify the word 'tahir' in the matn and understand its scope: it includes freedom from both minor and major impurity.
The commentary expands on the matn's brief phrase.
2
Determine the ruling when absent
Read what happens if the khatib is not pure: the sermon is still valid but the act is disliked (makruh).
The term 'karaha' here indicates tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited).
3
Identify the reason for dislike
The dislike is because it contradicts the Sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ, who would be in a state of purity during the khutbah.
The basis is the action of the Prophet, not a textual command.
4
Classify the ruling in Hanafi fiqh
Purity is a Sunnah mu'akkadah for the khatib; impurity is makruh tanzihi.
This distinguishes it from the prayer, where purity is a shart (condition) for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : طاهراً ؛ أي من الحدث الأصغر والأكبر، فإن خطب محدثاً كره لكونه خلافُ السُنَّة.
His statement: 'pure' – meaning from minor and major impurity, for if he delivers the sermon while in a state of impurity, it is disliked because it contradicts the Sunnah.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage explains the matn requirement that the khatib be tahir (pure) from both hadath asghar (minor impurity, like needing wudu) and hadath akbar (major impurity, like janabah). If the khatib delivers the sermon while in a state of impurity, it is makruh (disliked) because it goes against the practice (Sunnah) of the Prophet. The ruling indicates that purity is a recommended condition, not a requirement for validity, as the sermon does not have the same conditions as prayer.

Key Terms
طاهراً (tahir): In a state of ritual purity, free from both minor and major impurity.
حدث أصغر (hadath asghar): Minor impurity that necessitates wudu, e.g., passing wind, urine, etc.
حدث أكبر (hadath akbar): Major impurity that necessitates ghusl, e.g., janabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a khatib delivers the Friday sermon while in a state of minor impurity, the sermon is:
A) Invalid
B) Valid but disliked
C) Invalid and must be repeated
D) Forbidden

Key Takeaway
Purity for the khatib is Sunnah; impurity makes the sermon valid but disliked.

The Two Rak'ahs of Friday Prayer and Recommended Recitation
Ruling on the number of rak'ahs and sunnah recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of rak'ahs for Friday prayer and identify the sunnah recitation options along with the ruling that other recitations are permissible.

Core Idea
Friday prayer: two rak'ahs, recited aloud; specific surahs are sunnah, but others are valid.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the basic ruling of Friday prayer's two rak'ahs. While the number and jahr are clear, the specific surahs for recitation have transmitted options. The key is to understand that these are sunnah, not obligatory, and reciting other surahs does not harm the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses the Friday prayer, stating it consists of two rak'ahs. The ruling is that it is a fard prayer, and the recitation must be aloud (jahr).
The number of rak'ahs is fixed by ijma.
2
Locate the sunnah recitation options
The text lists two combinations: (1) first rak'ah: Surah al-Jumu'ah, second: Surah al-Munafiqun or al-Ghashiyah; (2) first: Surah al-A'la, second: al-Ghashiyah. These are transmitted from the Prophet.
These are sunnah, not wajib.
3
Understand the basis (dalil)
The authority is the practice of the Prophet as recorded by the compilers of Sunan. The text cites 'the report from the Messenger of Allah'.
The dalil is ahad, zanni al-thubut, but its meaning is clear.
4
Note the permissibility of other recitations
The passage ends with 'if he recites other than that, there is no harm.' This indicates that while the listed surahs are recommended, other Quranic recitations are valid.
The prayer remains valid even if different surahs are recited.
5
Evaluate the hukm level
The specific recitation is sunnah, not wajib. Omission does not invalidate the prayer, but following the sunnah is meritorious.
The hanafi_position_box confirms hukm_level: sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ركعتين ؛ يجهر فيهما بالقراءة، يقرأ في الأولى سورة الجمعة، وفي الثانية : إِذَا جَاءَكَ الْمُنَافِقُونَ ) ، أو هَلْ أَتَنكَ حَدِيثُ الْغَاشِيَةِ ) ، أو في الأول سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى (٣) ، وفي الثانية : هَلْ أَتَنكَ حَدِيثُ الْغَاشِيَةِ ) ، هذا هو المنقول عن رسول الله ) عند أصحاب السنن وغيرهم، ولو قرأ غيرها لا بأس به.
His statement: 'two rak'ahs' – he recites aloud in them. He recites in the first rak'ah Surah al-Jumu'ah, and in the second: 'If the Hypocrites Come to You' or 'Has there come to you the narration of the Overwhelming'. Or in the first: 'Glorify the Name of your Lord, the Most High' and in the second: 'Has there come to you the narration of the Overwhelming'. This is what is reported from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, by the compilers of the Sunan and others. And if he recites other than that, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn specifying that the Friday prayer consists of two rak'ahs. The commentator notes that the recitation is to be aloud (jahr). He then gives the proven sunnah options for the recitation: either Surah al-Jumu'ah in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun or Surah al-Ghashiyah in the second, or Surah al-A'la in the first and al-Ghashiyah in the second. All these combinations are transmitted from the Prophet. However, reciting other surahs is also permissible without any blame.

Key Terms
يجهر (yajharu): He recites aloud (jahr) in the Friday prayer.
سورة الجمعة (Surat al-Jumu'ah): Surah 62 of the Quran, recommended to be recited in the first rak'ah of Friday prayer.
سورة المنافقون (Surat al-Munafiqun): Surah 63, recommended for the second rak'ah.
سورة الغاشية (Surat al-Ghashiyah): Surah 88, another option for the second rak'ah.
سبح اسم ربك الأعلى (Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la): Surah 87 (al-A'la), recommended for the first rak'ah as an alternative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Fatiha only
B) Al-Jumu'ah
C) Al-Munafiqun
D) Al-Ghashiyah

Key Takeaway
The Friday prayer consists of two rak'ahs recited aloud; the recommended surah recitations are sunnah, and reciting other surahs is permissible.

Standing and Purity in the Friday Sermon
Commentary on standing and purity in the Friday sermon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing and purity during the Friday sermon and explain why omitting them is makruh tanzihi.

Core Idea
Standing and purity during the Friday sermon are sunnah muakkadah; omitting them without excuse is makruh tanzihi, not invalidating.

The Friday sermon (khutbah) has specific etiquettes that the Hanafi school regards as sunnah muakkadah rather than conditions. This lesson focuses on two key aspects: the imam's standing and his state of ritual purity. Understanding their legal weight helps distinguish between what invalidates the sermon and what merely detracts from its perfection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the imam should deliver the sermon 'standing' (qa'iman) and 'pure' (tahiran). The commentary clarifies that delivering it sitting without excuse is disliked (makruh), and delivering it while impure is also disliked, as it contradicts the sunnah.
These are not conditions for validity (shurut) but recommended practices (sunan).
2
Locate the basis for the ruling
The Hanafi school bases this on the general practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), who always delivered the sermon standing and in a state of purity. The text explicitly states 'because it is contrary to the sunnah' (khilaf al-sunnah).
No specific hadith is quoted here; the ruling rests on the established sunnah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent practice (fi'l) indicates a recommended act (sunnah). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action is a dalil for istihbab (recommendation) unless there is evidence of obligation.
The absence of a command makes it sunnah, not fard or wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools, particularly the Shafi'is, consider standing a condition (shart) for the sermon's validity. They base this on a different interpretation of the Prophet's practice and other narrations.
The Hanafi position is that if the imam sits, the sermon is valid but disliked.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school follows the principle that an act is not wajib unless there is a clear command. Since the narrations do not explicitly require standing or purity, they are categorized as sunnah muakkadah.
The mufta bihi is that the sermon is valid without them, but the imam should avoid omitting them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صلاة الجمعة
قائماً طاهراً، وإذا تمت الخطبة أقيم وصلى الإمام بالناس ركعتين قائماً طاهراً، وإذا تمت الخطبة أقيم وصلى الإمامُ بالنَّاس ركعتين).
[ ۱ ] قوله : قائماً ؛ فإن خطب جالساً من غير عذر كره.
[٢] قوله : طاهراً ؛ أي من الحدث الأصغر والأكبر، فإن خطب محدثاً كره لكونه خلافُ السُنَّة.
[٣] قوله : ركعتين ؛ يجهر فيهما بالقراءة، يقرأ في الأولى سورة الجمعة، وفي الثانية : إِذَا جَاءَكَ الْمُتَفِقُونَ ) ، أو هَلْ أَتَنكَ حَدِيثُ الْغَشِيةِ ) ، أو في الأول سَبِّحِ اسْمَ رَبِّكَ الْأَعْلَى (٣) ، وفي الثانية : هَلْ أَتَنكَ حَدِيثُ الْغَشِيَةِ ) ، هذا هو المنقول عن رسول الله ) عند أصحاب السنن وغيرهم، ولو قرأ غيرها لا بأس به.
(۱) المنافقون : من الآية ١.
(۲) الغاشية : ١ .
(۳) الأعلى : ۱.
(٤) فعن ابن أبي رافع الله قال : «صلى بنا أبو هريرة الله يوم الجمعة فقرأ بسورة الجمعة، وفي الركعة الآخرة : إِذَا جَاءَكَ الْمُتَفِقُونَ ) قال فأدركت أبا هريرة له حين انصرف فقلت له : إنك قرأت بسورتين كان علي الله يقرأ بهما بالكوفة قال أبو هريرة : فإني سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ بهما يوم الجمعة في سنن أبي داود (۱) : (٣٦١) ، و(سنن ابن ماجة»(١ : ٣٥٥)، وغيرها.
Book of Prayer: Friday Prayer. Standing, pure; when the sermon is completed, the iqamah is made and the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs, standing and pure. [Commentary:] [1] His saying: 'standing' – if he delivers the sermon sitting without an excuse, it is disliked. [2] His saying: 'pure' – meaning from minor and major impurity; if he delivers the sermon in a state of impurity, it is disliked because it is contrary to the sunnah. [3] His saying: 'two rak'ahs' – he recites aloud in them; he recites in the first rak'ah Surah al-Jumu'ah, and in the second 'When the Hypocrites come to you' or 'Has there come to you the narration of the Overwhelming?' or in the first 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High' and in the second 'Has there come to you the narration of the Overwhelming?' – this is what is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ according to the authors of the Sunan and others; and if he recites other than that, there is no harm. (1) Al-Munafiqun: from verse 1. (2) Al-Ghashiyah: 1. (3) Al-A'la: 1. (4) On the authority of Ibn Abi Rafi' who said: 'Abu Hurairah led us in prayer on Friday and recited Surah al-Jumu'ah and in the last rak'ah 'When the Hypocrites come to you.' He said: I caught up with Abu Hurairah when he finished and said to him: You recited two surahs that 'Ali used to recite in Kufah. Abu Hurairah said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ reciting them on Friday.' [Narrated in Sunan Abi Dawud (361), Sunan Ibn Majah (1:355), and others.]
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of Friday prayer from the matn of Al-Wiqayah. It addresses the conditions of the sermon (khutbah) and the prayer itself. The commentator explains that the imam must deliver the sermon standing; sitting without excuse is makruh tanzihi (disliked). Purity from both minor and major hadath is required; delivering the sermon while impure is also makruh tanzihi as it violates the sunnah. For the two rak'ahs, the imam recites aloud. The recommended practice from the Prophet ﷺ is to recite Surah al-Jumu'ah in the first rak'ah and Surah al-Munafiqun or al-Ghashiyah in the second. Alternatively, one may recite Surah al-A'la in the first and al-Ghashiyah in the second. The commentator notes that this is the transmitted practice, citing a hadith where Abu Hurairah did so. However, it is permissible to recite other surahs. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abi Rafi' reported in Sunan Abi Dawud and Ibn Majah.

Key Terms
قائماً (qa'iman): Standing; the imam must deliver the sermon while standing.
طاهراً (tahiran): Pure from both minor and major impurity for the sermon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an imam delivers the Friday sermon while in a state of minor impurity (without wudu), what is the ruling?
A) The sermon is invalid and must be repeated after purification.
B) The sermon is valid but it is makruh tanzihi.
C) The sermon is valid and there is no dislike because the imam has a valid excuse.
D) The sermon is invalid because purity is a condition.

Key Takeaway
Standing and purity during the Friday sermon are sunnah muakkadah; omitting them without excuse is makruh tanzihi, but the sermon remains valid.

Recommended Recitation in Friday Prayer
Commentary on the recitation in Friday prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended surahs for the Friday prayer and explain the Hanafi position that reciting other surahs is permissible.

Core Idea
The Prophet ﷺ recited specific surahs on Friday, but reciting other surahs is permissible; the practice is sunnah, not wajib.

The Friday prayer consists of two rak'ahs with audible recitation. The commentator provides the transmitted practice of the Prophet ﷺ regarding which surahs to recite. This lesson examines the recommended recitation and the legal weight of following this practice within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its recommended practice
The passage describes the recitation for the two rak'ahs of Friday prayer: in the first rak'ah, Surah al-Jumu'ah (62) or Surah al-A'la (87); in the second, Surah al-Munafiqun (63) or Surah al-Ghashiyah (88).
Two options are given; the imam may choose either combination.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites a hadith from Ibn Abi Rafi' where Abu Hurairah led Friday prayer reciting Surah al-Jumu'ah and al-Munafiqun, and reported that the Prophet ﷺ recited these surahs on Friday. This hadith is found in Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan Ibn Majah.
The hadith is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's actual recitation of these surahs indicates that this is a recommended practice (sunnah). The passage explicitly states 'this is what is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah'.
The proof is fi'li (action), not qawli (statement), so it indicates istihbab.
4
Note the ruling on alternative recitation
The commentator adds 'and if he recites other than that, there is no harm' (لا بأس به). This clearly shows that reciting other surahs is permissible and does not invalidate the prayer.
The Hanafi position is that following the transmitted surahs is sunnah, but it is not wajib.
5
Determine the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that reciting these specific surahs on Friday is sunnah muakkadah. If the imam recites other surahs, the prayer is valid and there is no sin.
No ikhtilaf is noted on this within the Hanafi school; the difference is with other schools on the level of recommendation.

Recommended Acts Before Eid Prayer
Commentary on recommended sunan before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five recommended acts before Eid prayer, identify their ruling (sunnah muakkadah vs mustahabb), and cite the Hanafi proof for each.

Core Idea
Eating odd dates, miswak, ghusl, perfume, and best clothes are sunnah for Eid—confirmed by the Prophet's practice.

The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the acts beloved before Eid prayer. It clarifies that the term 'hubba' covers both confirmed sunnah acts like ghusl and recommended acts like eating. Each act is supported by a hadith or general principle.

Guided Path
1
List the five recommended acts
Identify the five acts mentioned: eating before prayer (for Fitr), using miswak, performing ghusl, applying perfume, and wearing best clothes.
2
Classify the ruling of each act
According to the commentary, ghusl is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), while the other acts are mustahabb (recommended) or generally sunnah. Note that 'hubba' encompasses both levels.
The Hanafi position: ghusl is sunnah muakkadah; eating, miswak, perfume, and clothing are mustahabb but still strongly recommended.
3
Identify the proof for each act
Match each act with its evidence: eating dates – hadith of Anas in Bukhari; ghusl – hadith of Ibn Abbas in Ibn Majah; miswak – general sunnah at every prayer; perfume – analogized from Friday; wearing best clothes – hadith of Ibn Abbas in Al-Mu'jam al-Awsat.
The proofs are ahad hadith, but their collective indication is strong enough for desirability.
4
Understand the Hanafi rationale
The commentator argues that acts like miswak and perfume are sunnah at every prayer, so for the greater occasion of Eid they are even more emphasized. Similarly, eating before prayer for Fitr confirms the end of fasting.
This is based on qiyas awla (more deserving analogy).
5
Apply to both Eids
These acts are recommended for both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, with the exception that eating before prayer is specifically for Fitr. For Adha, it is recommended to eat after prayer from the sacrifice.
The text focuses on Fitr, but the same general principles apply.

Chapter of the Two Eids. It is made beloved on the day of Fitr to eat before the prayer, to use the miswak, to perform ghusl, to apply perfume, and to wear the best of his clothes. [Commentary:] [1] His saying: 'Chapter of the Two Eids' – its connection to what preceded is that Friday is also a festival for the believers, and since it recurs every week, it was appropriate to precede it over what recurs yearly. [2] His saying: 'It is made beloved' – in the passive form from tahbib, and what is meant is more general than the confirmed sunnah and the recommended; for some of the mentioned matters are counted among the confirmed sunnahs like ghusl and others. [3] His saying: 'to eat before his prayer' – meaning dates, three or five or seven or less or more, provided it is an odd number – that is what is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, as in Sahih al-Bukhari and others; if there are no dates, then something else sweet. [4] His saying: 'to use the miswak' – this is from the general sunnahs at every wudu, and recommended at every prayer; so it is recommended and sunnah in the two Eids as well, by primary reasoning. [5] His saying: 'to perform ghusl' – because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ used to perform ghusl on the two Eids; Ibn Majah recorded it. [6] His saying: 'to apply perfume' – meaning he uses perfume on his clothes and body; encouragement to it has come in many hadiths from the authors of the Sunan and others for Friday, and it is known that the day of the two Eids is more important than it. [7] His saying: 'to wear' – because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ used to wear a red cloak on every Eid. (1) On the authority of Anas who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten some dates. [Bukhari (1:325), Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah (2:342), and others.] (2) On the authority of Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ would perform ghusl on the day of Fitr and the day of Adha. [Sunan Ibn Majah (1:417), and others.] (3) On the authority of Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to wear a red cloak on the day of Eid. [Al-Mu'jam al-Awsat (7:316); al-Haythami said in Majma' al-Zawa'id (p. 198): 'Its narrators are trustworthy.']
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the recommended acts before the Eid prayer. The commentator explains the chapter heading and its placement after Friday because Friday is a weekly 'eid'. The term 'hubba' indicates desirability, and the acts range from confirmed sunnah (like ghusl) to mere mustahabb. Specifically for Eid al-Fitr, it is recommended to eat an odd number of dates before the prayer; if dates are unavailable, any sweet food. Using miswak is recommended generally and especially for Eid. Ghusl on Eid is a confirmed sunnah based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas. Applying perfume and wearing one's best clothes are also recommended, with evidence from the Prophet's practice of wearing a red cloak. The proofs cited include hadith from Bukhari, Ibn Majah, and others.

Key Terms
حُبب (hubba): It is made desirable; a passive form indicating that the act is recommended (mustahabb) or sunnah.
يستاك (yastaku): Use the miswak (tooth-stick) for oral hygiene.
يغتسل (yaghtasilu): Perform ghusl (full body wash) on the day of Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's ﷺ practice establishes these acts as recommended (sunnah/mustahabb) for Eid, with ghusl being confirmed sunnah.

Recommended Personal Preparations for Eid Prayer
Lists recommended personal acts before Eid prayer with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts of personal preparation for Eid prayer and identify which are sunnah mu'akkadah and which are mustahabb.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice on Eid includes eating dates, ghusl, perfume, and fine clothes.

Before the Eid prayer, we are encouraged to follow several sunan that enhance the spirit of the day. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah lists the acts of personal grooming and preparation, each supported by hadith. Understanding these acts and their legal weight helps us practice the Sunnah with proper awareness.

Guided Path
1
Identify each recommended act
Read the list: eating before prayer (preferably odd dates), using miswak, performing ghusl, applying perfume, wearing the best clothes.
The text uses the phrase 'hubbiba' (it is beloved), indicating recommendation.
2
Classify each act's ruling level
Determine for each act whether it is sunnah mu'akkadah (stressed) or mustahabb (recommended). The commentator notes that ghusl is among the mu'akkadah sunan.
Eating dates is based on the Prophet's practice; miswak is sunnah at all prayers.
3
Cite the hadith evidence
For each act, locate the proof from the Sunnah. For example, ghusl is proven by the hadith 'The Prophet used to perform ghusl on the two Eids' (Ibn Majah).
The commentator provides sources for each act.
4
Explain the Hanafi principle behind the ruling
The Prophet's continuous practice without prohibition indicates recommendation (sunnah) according to Hanafi usul. The wording 'hubbiba' covers both mu'akkadah and mustahabb.
This distinction affects the reward and blame for omission.

[١] قوله : ويؤدي فطرته ؛ بالكسر : أي صدقة الفطر، وهو إن كان أداؤها واجباً لكن أداءه قبل الخروج إلى المصلى مسنون، هو المنقول عن ابن عمر ، قال : «أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم الفطر أن نؤدِّيها قبل خروج النَّاسِ إلى الصَّلاة»، أخرجَهُ البُخَارِيُّ ومسلم. Chapter of the two Eids. It is beloved on the day of Fitr to eat before his prayer, use miswak, perform ghusl, apply perfume, and wear his best clothes. Commentary: 'Qala: Chapter of the two Eids' - its connection to what preceded is that Friday is also a festival for the believers, and since it recurs every week, it was appropriate to precede what recurs annually. 'Qala: It is beloved' - in the passive form from tahbib, and by it is meant more general than sunnah (mu'akkadah) and mustahabb, for some of the mentioned acts are counted among the mu'akkadah sunan like ghusl and others. 'Qala: to eat before his prayer' - meaning dates, three or five or seven or less or more, odd numbers being transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, as in Sahih al-Bukhari etc., and if no dates then something else sweet. 'Qala: and use miswak' - this is from the general sunan at every wudu, and mustahabb at every prayer, so it is mustahabb and sunnah in the two Eids as a priority. 'Qala: perform ghusl' - due to what was narrated that the Prophet used to perform ghusl on the two Eids, reported by Ibn Majah. 'Qala: and apply perfume' - meaning use perfume on clothes and body, for encouragement to it has come in many ahadith from the authors of Sunan and others on Friday, and it is known that the day of the two Eids is more important. 'Qala: and wear' - due to what was narrated: 'The Prophet used to wear a red cloak on every Eid', from Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah would not set out on the day of Fitr until he ate dates' in al-Bukhari and Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah etc. And from Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah performed ghusl on the day of Fitr and the day of Adha' in Sunan Ibn Majah etc. And from Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah used to wear a red cloak on the day of Eid' in al-Mu'jam al-Awsat; al-Haythami said in Majma' al-Zawa'id: 'Its narrators are trustworthy.' And he gives his Fitr sadaqah and goes out to the musalla. Commentary: 'Qala: and he gives his Fitr sadaqah' - with kasra: meaning sadaqat al-fitr; although paying it is obligatory, paying it before going out to the musalla is sunnah, transmitted from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah ordered us on the day of Fitr to give it before the people go out to prayer' - narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. 'Qala: and goes out to the musalla' - in the passive form; it is a place in the desert where the Eid prayer is performed, called al-jabbana; and the absolute going out from his house to the prayer, although it is wajib based on the principle that what completes a wajib is itself wajib, but going out to the jabbana is sunnah mu'akkadah. If the congregational mosque accommodates them and they pray in the city mosques without an excuse, their prayer is valid but they have abandoned the sunnah; this is the correct view as in al-Zahiriyyah. And in al-Khulasah and al-Khaniyyah: 'The sunnah is that the imam goes out to the jabbana and appoints someone else to pray in the city with the weak, based on the fact that Eid prayer in two places is permissible by agreement.' End. The basis for it is that the Prophet used to go out to the musalla and did not pray Eid in his mosque despite its honor except once due to the excuse of rain, as expanded by Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad and al-Qastalani in al-Mawahib al-Ladunniyyah and others. The ahadith on this chapter are extracted in books of Sunan and others. And a dispute occurred among scholars in our time whether going out to the musalla is sunnah mu'akkadah or mustahabb? Most gave fatwa that it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and this is the fair statement agreeing with the books of usul and furu' and consistent with the majority. And from Nafi': 'Ibn Umar used to wear his best clothes on the two Eids' in Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir; Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari: 'Its chain is authentic.'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of the two Eids (al-‘idayn). The author presents a series of recommended acts (sunan and mustahabbat) for the day of Eid al-Fitr, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The first part lists: eating before the Eid prayer (preferably odd numbers of dates or something sweet), using miswak, taking a bath (ghusl), applying perfume, and wearing the best clothes. Each of these is supported by hadith evidence. The commentator notes that the phrase 'it is beloved' (hubbiba) covers both sunnah mu'akkadah and mustahabb acts, and he clarifies that some acts like ghusl are considered mu'akkadah. The second part adds two more acts: giving the sadaqat al-fitr (fitr sadaqah) before going out to prayer, and going out to the musalla (prayer ground) rather than praying in the mosque. The commentator explains that while giving sadaqah is obligatory, performing it before the prayer is sunnah. Regarding the musalla, he cites multiple sources to affirm that the Sunnah is to go to an open place (jabbana), and that praying in a mosque without an excuse, though valid, abandons the sunnah. He mentions a later dispute among scholars whether going to the musalla is sunnah mu'akkadah or mustahabb, and states that the majority opinion (and the one consistent with the school's principles) is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage ends with an additional narration about wearing the best clothes.

Key Terms
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A stressed sunnah that the Prophet regularly performed and rarely omitted; omitting it is blameworthy but not sinful.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): Recommended act; performing it brings reward, omitting it is not sinful.
التحبيب (al-taḥbīb): Making something beloved; here used in passive form 'hubbiba' to indicate recommendation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following acts is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah?
A) Eating dates before prayer
B) Using miswak
C) Performing ghusl
D) Wearing red cloak

Key Takeaway
Personal preparation for Eid prayer includes eating, miswak, ghusl, perfume, and fine clothes; ghusl is sunnah mu'akkadah, the rest are mustahabb.

Recommended Acts of Charity and Location for Eid Prayer
Discusses sunan related to fitrana timing and location of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the sunnah timing of sadaqat al-fitr from its obligatory nature, and state the ruling on going to the musalla for Eid prayer, including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Give fitrana before the prayer, and go to the musalla — not the mosque — for the true sunnah.

After personal preparation, two further acts complete the Eid Sunnah: paying sadaqat al-fitr before the prayer and going to an open prayer ground (musalla). This passage explains that while fitrana is itself obligatory, performing it before the prayer is sunnah. For the location, there is a later dispute whether going to the musalla is sunnah mu'akkadah or merely mustahabb; the text concludes in favor of mu'akkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two additional acts
The passage adds giving sadaqat al-fitr (fitrana) before the prayer, and going out to the musalla (open prayer ground).
These are separate from the personal acts.
2
Analyze the ruling for fitrana timing
Understand that giving fitrana is wajib, but the Sunnah is to give it before going out to the Eid prayer. The hadith from Ibn Umar commands giving it before people go out.
The text says 'though paying it is obligatory, paying it before going out is sunnah'.
3
Examine the dispute over the musalla
Some Hanafi scholars considered going to the musalla as mustahabb, but the majority (and the text's tarjih) holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah. The evidence: the Prophet never prayed Eid in his mosque except due to rain.
The commentator cites al-Zahiriyyah, al-Khulasah, and al-Khaniyyah, and notes the fair statement is mu'akkadah.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that going to the musalla is sunnah mu'akkadah. Praying in the mosque without excuse is valid but leaves the sunnah.
This affects whether one should make an effort to go to an open area.

قوله : باب العيدين ؛ مناسبتُهُ بما سبق أنَّ الجمعة أيضاً عيد للمؤمنين، ولَمَّا كان متكرراً في كل أسبوع ناسب تقديمه على ما يتكرر في سنته. [٢]قوله : حُبب ؛ بصيغة المجهول من التحبيب ، والمراد به أعم من السنة والمؤكدة والمستحب، فإن بعض الأمور المذكورة عدُّوه من السُنَن المؤكّدة كالغُسل وغيره. (۳) قوله : أن يأكل قبل صلاته ؛ أي تمرات ثلاثاً أو خمساً أو سبعاً أو أقل أو أكثر، بعد أن يكون وتراً هو المنقول عن رسول الله ). كما في «صحيح البخاري»، وغيره، فإن لم تكن تمرات فشيء آخر حلو. (٤) قوله : ويستاك ؛ هذا من السنن العامة عند كل وضوء، ومستحب عند كل صلاة، فيكون مستحباً وسُنَّة في العيدين أيضاً بالطريق الأولى. [٥] قوله : يغتسل ؛ لما روي أنَّ النبي كان يغتسل في العيدين، أخرجه ابن ماجة. [٦]قوله : ويتطيب ؛ أي يستعمل طيباً في الثوب والبدن، فقد ورد الترغيب إليه في أحاديث كثيرة عند أصحاب السنن وغيرهم يوم الجمعة ، ومن المعلوم أن يوم العيدين أهم منه. [۷]قوله : ويلبس ؛ لما روي : «أَنَّ النَّبي الله كان يلبس بردة حمراء في كلِّ عيد» فعن أنس الله قال : كان رسول الله الله لا يغدو يوم الفطر حتى يأكل تمرات في «البخاري»، و «صحيح ابن خزيمة»، وغيرها. فعن ابن عباس له قال : كان رسول الله الله لا يغتسل يوم الفطر ويوم الأضحى» في «سنن ابن ماجة»، وغيره. فعن ابن عباس له قال : كان رسول الله يلبس يوم العيد بردة حمراء» في «المعجم الأوسط»، قال الهيثمي في مجمع الزوائد : «رجاله ثقات».
ويُؤدِّي فطرته ويخرج إلى المصلى
[١] قوله : ويؤدي فطرته ؛ بالكسر : أي صدقة الفطر، وهو إن كان أداؤها واجباً لكن أداءه قبل الخروج إلى المصلى مسنون، هو المنقول عن ابن عمر ، قال : «أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم الفطر أن نؤدِّيها قبل خروج النَّاسِ إلى الصَّلاة»، أخرجَهُ البُخَارِيُّ ومسلم. [۲]قوله : ويخرج إلى المصلّى ؛ بصيغة المجهول، هو موضع في الصحراء يُصلّى فيه صلاة العيدين ، ويقال له : الجبانة، ومطلق الخروج من بيته إلى الصلاة، وإن كان واجباً بناء على أن ما يتم به الواجب واجب، لكن الخروج إلى الجبانة سُنَّةٌ مؤكدة، وإن وسعهم المسجد الجامع فإن صلوا فيه في مساجد المصر من غير عذر جازت صلاتهم وتركوا السنة، هذا هو الصحيح، كما في «الظهيرية». وفي «الخلاصة» و«الخانية»: السُّنَّةُ أن يخرج الإمامُ إلى الجَبَّانَةِ ويستخلف غيرَهُ ليصلي في المصر بالضعفاء بناءً على أنَّ صلاة العيدين في موضعين جائزة بالاتفاق. انتهى والأصل فيه أنَّ النبي له الله كان يخرج إلى المصلى ولم يصل صلاة العيد في مسجده مع شرفه إلا مرة بعذر المطر، كما بسطه ابن القيم في «زاد المعاد»، والقسطلاني في مواهب اللدنية»، وغيرهما. والأحاديث في هذا الباب المخرَّجة في كتب السنن وغيرها ، وقد وقع النزاع بين العلماء في عصرنا أنَّ الخروج إلى المصلى هل هو سنة مؤكدةً أم مستحبة ؟ فأفتى أكثرهم بأنه سنةٌ مؤكدة وهذا هو القولُ المنصف الموافق لكتب الأصول والفروع المطابق لما عليه الجمهور
وعن نافع : إن ابن عمر » كان يلبس في العيدين أحسن ثيابه» في «سنن البيهقي الكبير»، قال ابن حجر في فتح الباري: «إسناده صحيح».
Chapter of the two Eids. It is beloved on the day of Fitr to eat before his prayer, use miswak, perform ghusl, apply perfume, and wear his best clothes. Commentary: 'Qala: Chapter of the two Eids' - its connection to what preceded is that Friday is also a festival for the believers, and since it recurs every week, it was appropriate to precede what recurs annually. 'Qala: It is beloved' - in the passive form from tahbib, and by it is meant more general than sunnah (mu'akkadah) and mustahabb, for some of the mentioned acts are counted among the mu'akkadah sunan like ghusl and others. 'Qala: to eat before his prayer' - meaning dates, three or five or seven or less or more, odd numbers being transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, as in Sahih al-Bukhari etc., and if no dates then something else sweet. 'Qala: and use miswak' - this is from the general sunan at every wudu, and mustahabb at every prayer, so it is mustahabb and sunnah in the two Eids as a priority. 'Qala: perform ghusl' - due to what was narrated that the Prophet used to perform ghusl on the two Eids, reported by Ibn Majah. 'Qala: and apply perfume' - meaning use perfume on clothes and body, for encouragement to it has come in many ahadith from the authors of Sunan and others on Friday, and it is known that the day of the two Eids is more important. 'Qala: and wear' - due to what was narrated: 'The Prophet used to wear a red cloak on every Eid', from Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah would not set out on the day of Fitr until he ate dates' in al-Bukhari and Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah etc. And from Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah performed ghusl on the day of Fitr and the day of Adha' in Sunan Ibn Majah etc. And from Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah used to wear a red cloak on the day of Eid' in al-Mu'jam al-Awsat; al-Haythami said in Majma' al-Zawa'id: 'Its narrators are trustworthy.' And he gives his Fitr sadaqah and goes out to the musalla. Commentary: 'Qala: and he gives his Fitr sadaqah' - with kasra: meaning sadaqat al-fitr; although paying it is obligatory, paying it before going out to the musalla is sunnah, transmitted from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah ordered us on the day of Fitr to give it before the people go out to prayer' - narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. 'Qala: and goes out to the musalla' - in the passive form; it is a place in the desert where the Eid prayer is performed, called al-jabbana; and the absolute going out from his house to the prayer, although it is wajib based on the principle that what completes a wajib is itself wajib, but going out to the jabbana is sunnah mu'akkadah. If the congregational mosque accommodates them and they pray in the city mosques without an excuse, their prayer is valid but they have abandoned the sunnah; this is the correct view as in al-Zahiriyyah. And in al-Khulasah and al-Khaniyyah: 'The sunnah is that the imam goes out to the jabbana and appoints someone else to pray in the city with the weak, based on the fact that Eid prayer in two places is permissible by agreement.' End. The basis for it is that the Prophet used to go out to the musalla and did not pray Eid in his mosque despite its honor except once due to the excuse of rain, as expanded by Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad and al-Qastalani in al-Mawahib al-Ladunniyyah and others. The ahadith on this chapter are extracted in books of Sunan and others. And a dispute occurred among scholars in our time whether going out to the musalla is sunnah mu'akkadah or mustahabb? Most gave fatwa that it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and this is the fair statement agreeing with the books of usul and furu' and consistent with the majority. And from Nafi': 'Ibn Umar used to wear his best clothes on the two Eids' in Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir; Ibn Hajar said in Fath al-Bari: 'Its chain is authentic.'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of the two Eids (al-‘idayn). The author presents a series of recommended acts (sunan and mustahabbat) for the day of Eid al-Fitr, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The first part lists: eating before the Eid prayer (preferably odd numbers of dates or something sweet), using miswak, taking a bath (ghusl), applying perfume, and wearing the best clothes. Each of these is supported by hadith evidence. The commentator notes that the phrase 'it is beloved' (hubbiba) covers both sunnah mu'akkadah and mustahabb acts, and he clarifies that some acts like ghusl are considered mu'akkadah. The second part adds two more acts: giving the sadaqat al-fitr (fitr sadaqah) before going out to prayer, and going out to the musalla (prayer ground) rather than praying in the mosque. The commentator explains that while giving sadaqah is obligatory, performing it before the prayer is sunnah. Regarding the musalla, he cites multiple sources to affirm that the Sunnah is to go to an open place (jabbana), and that praying in a mosque without an excuse, though valid, abandons the sunnah. He mentions a later dispute among scholars whether going to the musalla is sunnah mu'akkadah or mustahabb, and states that the majority opinion (and the one consistent with the school's principles) is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage ends with an additional narration about wearing the best clothes.

Key Terms
المصلى (al-musallā): An open place in the desert where Eid prayer is performed, also called al-jabbānah.
الفطر (al-fiṭr): sadaqat al-fitr, the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan; here refers to paying it before the Eid prayer.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A stressed sunnah that the Prophet regularly performed and rarely omitted; omitting it is blameworthy but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on paying sadaqat al-fitr before the Eid prayer?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah
C) It is mustahabb
D) It is not recommended

Key Takeaway
Give fitrana before the prayer (sunnah timing) and strive to pray in the open musalla (sunnah mu'akkadah) to fully follow the Prophet's practice.
