Giving Fitr Sadaqa Before the Eid Prayer: Ruling and Recommended Time
Commentary on the timing of fitr sadaqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sadaqat al-fitr and distinguish between its obligatory nature and the recommended time for giving it before the Eid prayer.

Core Idea
Fitr sadaqa is wajib; giving it before the Eid prayer is sunnah, not a condition of validity.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a key nuance about sadaqat al-fitr: while the charity itself is obligatory in the Hanafi school, performing it before leaving for the Eid prayer is a recommended practice (sunnah). The proof is a hadith narrated by Ibn Umar, which commands giving it before people go out to prayer. Understanding this distinction prevents the common mistake of treating the timing as obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses sadaqat al-fitr (fitr). According to the Hanafi school, giving fitr is wajib (obligatory).
Wajib means obligatory but with a slightly lower epistemological certainty than fard; nevertheless, it must be fulfilled.
2
Locate the timing recommendation
The text states that performing it before going out to the musalla (Eid prayer) is sunnah. This is a separate ruling from the obligation itself.
The phrase 'مسنون' indicates it is recommended, not compulsory.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet commanded to give fitr before people go out to prayer. The imperative implies obligation of the fitr itself, but the phrase 'before' specifies the preferred time.
Bukhari and Muslim narrated it, so it is authentic (muttafaqun alayh).
4
Determine the legal implication of the command
The Hanafi school applies the usul principle: al-amr li al-wujub (the imperative indicates obligation) for the act of giving, but the timing is understood as guidance (irshad) or recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
If the timing were wajib, delaying would invalidate the fitr, but the school holds it remains valid.
5
State the practical consequence
If one gives fitr after the Eid prayer, the obligation is fulfilled but it is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked). The optimal time is before prayer.
This shows the distinction between the wajib act and the sunnah timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُؤدِّي فطرته ويخرج إلى المصلى [١] قوله : ويؤدي فطرته ; بالكسر : أي صدقة الفطر، وهو إن كان أداؤها واجباً لكن أداءه قبل الخروج إلى المصلى مسنون ، هو المنقول عن ابن عمر ، قال : «أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم الفطر أن نؤدِّيها قبل خروج النَّاسِ إلى الصَّلاة» ، أخرجَهُ البُخَارِيُّ ومسلم.
He gives his fitr (sadaqat al-fitr) and goes out to the musalla. [1] His statement: 'and he gives his fitr' – with a kasra on the fa: meaning sadaqat al-fitr. Although performing it is obligatory, performing it before going out to the musalla is sunnah. This is transmitted from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ commanded us on the day of Fitr to give it before the people go out to prayer.' Bukhari and Muslim narrated it.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that one should give fitr sadaqa and go out to the musalla. The commentator explains that 'fitr' here means sadaqat al-fitr, the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan. While the giving itself is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, performing it before leaving for the Eid prayer is sunnah (recommended). The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar in which the Prophet directly ordered that it be given before people go out to prayer. This hadith is authentic (muttifaqun alayh). Thus, the optimal practice is to give the fitr early to allow the needy to benefit before the Eid prayer.

Key Terms
فطرته (fitrathi): Sadaqat al-fitr, the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving sadaqat al-fitr before going to the Eid prayer?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is fard.
D) It is mustahabb.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sadaqat al-fitr is wajib, but delivering it before the Eid prayer is a recommended sunnah, not a condition of validity.

Going Out to the Musalla for Eid Prayer is Sunnah Mu'akkada
Explanation of the ruling and proof for going to the musalla for Eid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on going to the musalla for Eid prayer, identify its basis in the Prophet's practice, and explain the consequence of praying in the mosque without an excuse.

Core Idea
Going to the musalla for Eid is an emphatic sunnah; praying in the mosque is valid but loses the sunnah.

This lesson clarifies the legal status of going to an open prayer ground for Eid. While the act of leaving for prayer is generally wajib, the specific act of going to the desert musalla is an emphatic sunnah. Understanding this distinction helps avoid missing a confirmed practice of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is going to the musalla for Eid prayer. The ruling is sunnah mu'akkada (emphatic sunnah).
2
Understand the nuance
Leaving the house for prayer is generally wajib (as a means), but the specific exit to the musalla is sunnah. The principle: what completes a wajib is wajib, but here it is not wajib for this specific act.
3
Examine the proof
The Prophet consistently went to the musalla and only once prayed in the mosque due to rain. This establishes the recommended nature.
4
Note the consequence
If one prays in the mosque without excuse, the prayer is valid but the sunnah is lost. The imam is encouraged to go to the musalla and appoint a deputy for the weak.
5
Acknowledge the ikhtilaf
Some contemporary scholars consider it mustahabb, but the majority (mufta bihi) is sunnah mu'akkada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ويخرج إلى المصلّى ; بصيغة المجهول، هو موضع في الصحراء يُصلّى فيه صلاة العيدين ، ويقال له : الجبانة، ومطلق الخروج من بيته إلى الصلاة، وإن كان واجباً بناء على أن ما يتم به الواجب واجب، لكن الخروج إلى الجبانة سُنَّةٌ مؤكدة، وإن وسعهم المسجد الجامع فإن صلوا فيه في مساجد المصر من غير عذر جازت صلاتهم وتركوا السنة، هذا هو الصحيح، كما في «الظهيرية». وفي «الخلاصة» و«الخانية»: السُّنَّةُ أن يخرج الإمامُ إلى الجَبَّانَةِ ويستخلف غيرَهُ ليصلي في المصر بالضعفاء بناءً على أنَّ صلاة العيدين في موضعين جائزة بالاتفاق. انتهى والأصل فيه أنَّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يخرج إلى المصلى ولم يصل صلاة العيد في مسجده مع شرفه إلا مرة بعذر المطر، كما بسطه ابن القيم في «زاد المعاد)، والقسطلاني في مواهب اللدنية»، وغيرهما. والأحاديث في هذا الباب المخرَّجة في كتب السنن وغيرها ، وقد وقع النزاع بين العلماء في عصرنا أنَّ الخروج إلى المصلى هل هو سنة مؤكدةً أم مستحبة ؟ فأفتى أكثرهم بأنه سنةٌ مؤكدة وهذا هو القولُ المنصف الموافق لكتب الأصول والفروع المطابق لما عليه الجمهور. وعن نافع : إن ابن عمر » كان يلبس في العيدين أحسن ثيابه» في «سنن البيهقي الكبير»
His statement: 'and he goes out to the musalla' – in the passive voice. It is a place in the desert where the Eid prayer is performed, also called al-jabbana. The mere exiting of his house to the prayer, although it is wajib based on the principle that what completes an obligatory act is itself obligatory, but exiting to the jabbana is an emphatic sunnah. If they fit in the congregational mosque, and they pray in the mosques of the city without an excuse, their prayer is valid but they have abandoned the sunnah. This is the correct view, as in al-Zuhayriyya. And in al-Khulasa and al-Khaniyya: It is sunnah that the imam goes out to the jabbana and appoints someone else to pray in the city with the weak, based on the consensus that performing Eid prayer in two places is permissible. End. The basis for that is that the Prophet ﷺ used to go out to the musalla and never performed Eid prayer in his mosque despite its virtue, except once due to rain, as elaborated by Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad, al-Qastallani in al-Mawahib al-Laduniyya, and others. The ahadith on this topic are recorded in the sunan and other works. A dispute occurred among scholars in our time about whether going to the musalla is an emphatic sunnah or merely mustahabb. Most of them gave the verdict that it is an emphatic sunnah, and this is the fair opinion, agreeing with the books of usul and furu', and consistent with the majority. And from Nafi': 'Ibn Umar used to wear his best clothes on the two Eids' – in Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on going to an open musalla (prayer ground) for Eid prayer. The commentator clarifies that while leaving the house for prayer is generally wajib in a sense, the specific act of going to the jabbana (a desert area) is an emphatic sunnah (sunnah mu'akkada). It is not wajib; if one prays in the city mosque without an excuse, the prayer is valid but the sunnah is missed. The text cites multiple authoritative Hanafi sources (al-Zuhayriyya, al-Khulasa, al-Khaniyya) that the preferred practice is for the imam to go to the jabbana and appoint a deputy to pray with the weak in the city. The proof is from the consistent practice of the Prophet, who only prayed in his mosque once due to rain. A contemporary dispute is mentioned: some said it is mustahabb, but the majority of later scholars affirmed it as sunnah mu'akkada, which is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
المصلّى (al-musalla): A designated place in the open desert where Eid prayer is performed.
الجبانة (al-jabbana): A synonym for musalla, an open area outside the city for Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
Going to the musalla for Eid is an emphatic sunnah; praying in the mosque is valid but loses the sunnah.

Takbir on the Way to Eid: Jahar vs Sirr
Clarification of the dispute regarding takbir on the way to Eid prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir in Eid al-Fitr, distinguish between the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The Hanafi dispute on Eid takbir is about jahr vs sirr, not permissibility – all three imams agree it is permissible.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a common misunderstanding about the Hanafi position on takbir during Eid al-Fitr. The matn states that one does not raise the voice, but the commentary reveals a nuanced intra-madhhab disagreement. We will unpack the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, examine their proofs, and see how later scholars resolved the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine what exactly is disputed: the act of saying takbir, or the manner (jahr/sirr)? The text tells us that some understood the disagreement as about whether to say takbir at all, but the correct view is that it is only about raising the voice.
The matn itself says 'non-committal' by saying 'he is not raising his voice' (غير مكبر جهراً), implying the takbir itself is not negated.
2
State the positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: In Fitr, either no takbir (or quietly). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Takbir in both Eids, and aloud in Adha. The later refinement: the core difference is jahr vs sirr; all agree on permissibility.
The text mentions two groups: those who say لا يكبر في الفطر and those who say الخلاف في الجهر.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They use qiyas (analogy) with Eid al-Adha, where jahr is mustahabb by consensus. Since both are Eids, the same ruling should apply to Fitr.
This is a clear qiyas jali argument.
4
Examine Imam's proof
Imam relies on the Quranic principle that dhikr should be concealed (Quran 7:205). The jahr in Adha is a specific exception that cannot be extended by analogy.
The verse is used as a general principle (asl).
5
Determine the tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars (as per al-Fath, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Bada'i') chose the view that the ikhtilaf is about jahr, and that takbir itself is permissible. The mufta bihi is to say it quietly in Fitr; raising the voice is not recommended.
This resolution avoids the extreme positions (mustahabb/wajib) dismissed in the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير مكبر جهراً في طريقه) ، نفي التكبير بالجهر حتى لو كبر من غير جهرٍ كان حسناً. وقيل : إنه مستحبة، وهو قول باطل لا وجه له، وأفرط بعضهم فقال : إنه واجب، وهو قول مردودٌ لا عبرة به، وللتفصيلُ موضع آخر. [1]قوله : غير مكبر... الخ ؛ اختلفوا فيه : فمن الفقهاء من قال : لا يكبرُ في عيد الفطر في أثناء الطريق ، ويكبر في الأضحى عنده ، وعندهما: يكبر فيهما. (1)w (۲) ومنهم من قال : إن الخلاف في الجهر ،وعدمه، ولا خلاف في جوازه وعدم کراهته ، وهذا هو الأصح ، كما في «الفتح»، و«غاية البيان»، و«البدائع»، وغيرها، فإنَّ ذكر الله له لا يمنع عنه بكلِّ حال ما لم يمنعه مانع خارجي. وجه قولهما: الاعتبار بعيد الأضحى، فإنَّ الجهر بالتكبير في الطريق إلى أن يبلغ المصلى، أو إلى أن يفرغ من الصَّلاةِ مستحب فيه اتفاقاً. وله أنَّ الأصل في الذكرِ الإخفاء، كما يدلُّ عليه قوله : ﴿ وَاذْكُر رَّبِّكَ فِي نفسك ) ... الخ، وقد وردَ الشَّرعُ بالجهر في عيد الأضحى، فيقتصر ذلـك علـى مورده [٢]قوله : كان حسناً ؛ كيف لا ، وقد أخرجَ الدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ: «أَنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يكبر في الفطر من حين يخرج من بيته حتى يأتي المصلى).
(He is not raising his voice in takbir on his way) – negation of takbir with jahr (loudness). Even if he says takbir without jahr, it is good. And it was said that it is mustahabb, but this is a false statement with no basis. And some went to extremes saying it is wajib, but this is a rejected statement not to be considered. For detail there is another place. [1] His statement: 'not raising his voice...' – there is ikhtilaf about it: Some jurists said: He does not say takbir on the way during Eid al-Fitr, but he says takbir during al-Adha according to him (Imam), and according to them both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he says takbir in both. (1) And some said: The ikhtilaf is about jahr itself, no difference in its permissibility and lack of karahah. This is the most correct, as in al-Fath, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Bada'i', etc. Indeed, the remembrance of Allah is not prevented in any case as long as there is no external hindrance. The proof of their (Sahibayn) view: qiyas (analogy) with Eid al-Adha, for jahr in takbir on the way until reaching the musalla or until finishing prayer is mustahabb there by agreement. And his (Imam's) proof: the basis for dhikr is concealment, as indicated by His saying: 'And remember your Lord within yourself' [al-A'raf 205]; and the Shari'a has prescribed jahr in Eid al-Adha, so that is restricted to its specific context. [2] His statement: 'it is good' – how not, when al-Daraqutni narrated that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to say takbir on Fitr from the time he left his house until he reached the musalla.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') on the way to Eid prayer. The matn states that one does not raise the voice in takbir. The commentator first notes that even if one does it quietly, it is good. Then he dismisses extreme views that it is mustahabb or wajib. The core discussion is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Some scholars report that the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is about the very act of takbir: Imam says no takbir during Fitr, while Sahibayn say yes. However, the more correct view (as per al-Fath, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Bada'i') is that the ikhtilaf is only about raising the voice (jahr vs sirr), and there is consensus that the takbir itself is permissible without karahah. The proof for Sahibayn is analogy with Adha, where jahr is mustahabb by consensus. Imam's proof is the general principle that dhikr should be quiet, based on the Quranic verse, and that the exception of jahr in Adha is limited to that context. The commentator then supports this by citing a hadith from al-Daraqutni that the Prophet used to say takbir on Fitr from his house, implying the practice is established. Thus, the preferred ruling is that in Fitr, one may say takbir quietly; jahr is not recommended, unlike in Adha where jahr is mustahabb.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Raising the voice; in this context, saying takbir aloud.
إخفاء (ikhfa'): Concealment; saying dhikr quietly or inaudibly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on saying takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr?
A) It is wajib to say it aloud.
B) It is prohibited to say it.
C) It is permissible to say it quietly; raising the voice is not recommended.
D) It is mustahabb to say it loudly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr is permissible; the difference of opinion is only about raising the voice, and the preferred view is to say it quietly.

Takbir on the Way to Eid: Audible or Silent?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jahr vs ikhfa in takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on takbir audibility on Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, and explain how the principle of ikhfa in dhikr resolves the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school agrees takbir on Eid is permissible; the disagreement is only about audibility, not legality.

The Eid takbir is a beloved Sunnah, but how should it be performed on the way to the prayer? This passage from a commentary on al-Wiqayah reveals an important intra-Hanafi difference: while Imam Abu Hanifa prefers silent recitation on Eid al-Fitr, his two companions allow audibility. Understanding this nuanced ikhtilaf sharpens our appreciation of how principles like the original rule of ikhfa and exceptions by qiyas interplay in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is saying takbir (Allahu Akbar) while walking to the Eid prayer. The dispute is whether this should be done audibly (jahr) or silently (ikhfa).
The base text negates jahr, but the commentary clarifies the ikhtilaf.
2
State the position of each Hanafi imam
Abu Hanifa: ikhfa on Fitr, jahr on Adha. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad): jahr on both. The most correct view (al-ashah) says the difference is only about audibility; permissibility is agreed.
3
Examine the proof for each side
Sahibayn use qiyas on Adha, where jahr is recommended by consensus. Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that the original rule in dhikr is ikhfa (Quran 7:205), and jahr is restricted to Adha by text.
Dalil naqli: Quran verse and athar from al-Daraqutni support takbir on Fitr but do not specify jahr.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and the nature of the disagreement
The mufta bihi is that both jahr and ikhfa are permissible; jahr is not disliked. The dispute is purely about audibility, as confirmed by al-Fath, al-Bada'i, etc.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير مكبر جهراً في طريقه) ، نفى التكبير بالجهر حتى لو كبر من غير جهرٍ كان حسنا وقيل : إنه مستحبة، وهو قول باطل لا وجه له، وأفرط بعضهم فقال : إنه واجب، وهو قول مردودٌ لا عبرة به، وللتفصيلُ موضع آخر. [1]قوله : غير مكبر... الخ ؛ اختلفوا فيه : فمن الفقهاء من قال : لا يكبرُ في عيد الفطر في أثناء الطريق ، ويكبر في الأضحى عنده ، وعندهما: يكبر فيهما. (1)w (۲) ومنهم من قال : إن الخلاف في الجهر ،وعدمه، ولا خلاف في جوازه وعدم کراهته ، وهذا هو الأصح ، كما في «الفتح»، و«غاية البيان»، و«البدائع»، وغيرها، فإنَّ ذكر الله له لا يمنع عنه بكلِّ حال ما لم يمنعه مانع خارجي. وجه قولهما: الاعتبار بعيد الأضحى، فإنَّ الجهر بالتكبير في الطريق إلى أن يبلغ المصلى، أو إلى أن يفرغ من الصَّلاةِ مستحب فيه اتفاقاً. وله أنَّ الأصل في الذكرِ الإخفاء، كما يدلُّ عليه قوله : ﴿ وَاذْكُر رَّبِّكَ فِي نفسك ﴾ ... الخ، وقد وردَ الشَّرعُ بالجهر في عيد الأضحى، فيقتصر ذلـك علـى مورده [٢]قوله : كان حسناً ؛ كيف لا ، وقد أخرجَ الدَّارَ قُطْنِيُّ: «أَنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يكبر في الفطر من حين يخرج من بيته حتى يأتي المصلى).
Not saying takbir audibly on his way) He negated saying takbir with jahr (audibility) to the point that if one says takbir without audibility, it is good. And it was said: it is recommended, but that is a false statement with no basis. And some went to extremes saying it is obligatory, but that is a rejected statement not to be considered. The detail is for another place. [1] His saying: not saying takbir... etc.; they differed concerning it: among the jurists, some said: he does not say takbir on the day of Fitr on the way, and he says takbir on Adha according to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to them (the two companions) he says takbir on both. (1) And some said: the difference is regarding audibility or its absence, and there is no difference concerning permissibility and lack of disapproval, and this is the most correct, as in al-Fath, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Bada'i', etc., for the remembrance of Allah is not prevented from him in any situation unless an external preventer prevents it. The proof of the two companions is analogy to the day of Adha, for raising the voice with takbir on the way to the prayer place or until finishing the prayer is recommended by consensus. And for him (Abu Hanifa), the principle in dhikr is concealment, as indicated by His saying: 'And remember your Lord within yourself' ... etc., and the Shari'ah has permitted jahr on the day of Adha, so it is restricted to its specific occasion. [2] His saying: it is good; how could it not be, and al-Daraqutni has narrated: 'The Messenger of Allah used to say takbir on Fitr from when he left his house until he came to the prayer place.'
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the takbir on the way to Eid prayer. The base text (matn) states 'not saying takbir audibly on his way' which negates jahr. However, the commentator (sharh) clarifies the disagreement. Some jurists, including Abu Hanifa, hold that one does not say takbir audibly on Fitr but does on Adha, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that one says takbir on both. The most correct position, as stated in major works, is that the difference is only about jahr (audibility), not permissibility. Hence, saying takbir silently is permissible and not disliked. The hadith from al-Daraqutni supports saying takbir on Fitr, but it does not specify jahr. The proof of Sahibayn is qiyas on Adha, while Abu Hanifa's proof is that the original principle in dhikr is ikhfa (concealment), and the Shari'ah only allowed jahr for Adha, so it is restricted to that occasion.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' on the way to Eid prayer as a form of remembrance.
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation or declaration of takbir.
إخفاء (ikhfa): Concealment, i.e., saying takbir in a low voice not audible to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the nature of the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr?
A) Abu Hanifa forbids takbir while Sahibayn allow it
B) The difference is only about audibility (jahr vs. ikhfa)
C) Abu Hanifa considers it wajib while Sahibayn consider it sunnah
D) The difference is about whether takbir is said before or after the prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school unanimously permits takbir on Eid; the only difference is whether it should be audible or silent, with the preferred practice being silent on Fitr.

No Voluntary Prayers Before Eid Prayer
Ruling on voluntary prayers before and after Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers before and after Eid prayer, and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet did not pray nafl before or after Eid, so the majority of Hanafis deem it makruh tanzihi to do so in the musalla.

This lesson examines the specific ruling on voluntary prayers (nafl) in connection with Eid prayer. The Hanafi school considers it makruh tanzihi to pray nafl before Eid, based on the Prophet's consistent practice. We will also explore the nuance after Eid: prayer is prohibited in the musalla but recommended at home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing voluntary prayers (nafl) before Eid prayer. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked) according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray Eid and not pray any nafl before or after. This is narrated by the leading scholars (al-A'immah al-Sunnah) and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's continuous abandonment of voluntary prayers before Eid, despite his eagerness for prayer, indicates that it is not recommended. The Hanafi principle: if the Prophet persistently leaves an act, it suggests dislike (karahah).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Hafiz Ibn Hajar and others argued that the hadith only shows there is no regular Sunnah (sunnah ratiba) before Eid, not that it is makruh. So the ruling could be simply that there is no emphasis.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The majority hold the view of karahah, and this is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school. After Eid, one should not pray nafl in the musalla, but it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs at home.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتنفل قبل صلاة العيد، وشُرط لها شروط الجمعة وجوباً، وأداء، إلا الخطبة [١]قوله : ولا يتنفل ؛ أي لا يصلي النوافل، واحترز به عن أداء الفوائت. وفي الإطلاق إشارة إلى استواء الحكم في المصلّي وغيره. والأصل فيه أنه كان يصلي العيد ولا يُصلّي قبلها ولا بعدها، أخرجه الأئمة السنة وغيرهم، وأخذ منه الجمهورُ أنَّ التنفّلَ قبلها مكروه، فإنه لم يفعله مع حرصه على الصلاة، ولو كان جائزاً لفعلهُ ولو مرّة ، لكن ناقش فيه الحافظ ابنُ حَجَرٍ وغيرُهُ بأنَّ الحديث لا يدلُّ على الكراهة ، بل على أنه ليس للعيدِ سنة راتبة لا قبلها ولا بعدها. [٢] قوله : قبل صلاة العيد ؛ وأمّا بعدها فلا يتنفّلُ في المصلى، ولا بأس به بعد رجوعه إلى البيت، بل هو حسن أخذاً ما رواه ابن ماجة : «إنَّ النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا رجع إلى منزله صلى ركعتين»(۲).
And he does not perform voluntary prayers before Eid prayer, and conditions for it are the conditions of Jumu'ah in terms of obligation and performance, except the Khutbah. [1] His saying: 'and he does not perform voluntary prayers' means he does not pray nawafil, and it excludes making up missed prayers. The absolute wording indicates the ruling applies equally to the one praying and others. The basis for it is that he would pray the Eid prayer and not pray before it or after it, as narrated by the leading scholars and others. The majority deduced from this that performing voluntary prayers before it is makruh (disliked), for he did not do it despite his eagerness for prayer, and if it had been permissible he would have done it at least once. But al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar and others disputed this, saying the hadith does not indicate dislike, but rather that there is no regular Sunnah before or after it. [2] His saying: 'before Eid prayer'; as for after it, he does not perform voluntary prayers in the prayer place, but there is no harm in doing so after returning home, rather it is good, based on what Ibn Majah narrated: 'When the Prophet returned to his home, he would pray two rak'ahs.'
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on voluntary prayers (nafl) before and after Eid prayer. The base matn states that one does not pray nafl before Eid prayer. The commentator explains that this refers to nawafil, not missed obligatory prayers. The basis is that the Prophet did not pray any nafl before or after Eid prayer, leading the majority of scholars to consider it makruh. However, Hafiz Ibn Hajar contested that the hadith only indicates there is no regular Sunnah (sunnah ratiba) associated with Eid, not that it is disliked. After Eid prayer, one should not pray nafl in the musalla (prayer place), but after returning home, it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs as per the hadith of Ibn Majah.

Key Terms
تنفل (tanafful): Voluntary prayers (nawafil) performed extra to obligatory prayers.
مصلى (musalla): The designated prayer place for Eid prayer, often an open area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing voluntary prayers (nafl) after Eid prayer in the musalla?
A) It is mustahabb (recommended)
B) It is makruh (disliked)
C) It is haram
D) It is wajib

Key Takeaway
It is makruh tanzihi to pray nafl before Eid in the musalla; after returning home, it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs.
